Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
8 min
Attributing Talaq to Parts Representing the Whole Woman
State ruling and prove with Quran, Hadith, and linguistic usage.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on attributing talaq to the whole woman or parts representing the whole, and identify the Quranic, Hadith, and linguistic proofs.

Core Idea
Talaq is valid when attributed to the whole woman or any part idiomatically used for the whole.

This passage from Ashraf ul Hidayah establishes a key principle: talaq takes effect not only when the word 'talaq' is directly addressed to the wife, but also when it is attributed to her whole being or to a part that conventionally represents the whole. The author provides scriptural and linguistic evidence to show that expressions like 'your neck is divorced' or 'your head is divorced' are legally effective. This lesson will walk you through the ruling, its proofs, and the internal Hanafi difference on the word 'blood'.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
State that divorce occurs when attributed to the whole woman (e.g., 'anti taliq') or to a part that conventionally represents the whole (e.g., neck, head, face, soul, etc.).
2
Understand the condition
The part must be idiomatically used to refer to the entire person; not every body part qualifies.
Hands and feet are specifically excluded as they do not represent the whole.
3
Examine the proofs
Analyze the Quranic verses (58:3 'tahriru raqabah', 17:107 'fazallat a'naquhum'), the Hadith on private parts, and Arabic idioms (ra's al-qawm, wajh al-'arab, dam, nafs).
Each proof shows these parts are used to mean the whole person.
4
Note the internal difference
For the word 'dam' (blood), there is a narration that divorce does not occur; the relied-upon position is that it does occur.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد چہارم کتاب الطلاق ترجمہ اور جب ( مرد نے ) طلاق کو منسوب کیا کل عورت کی طرف یا اس جز کی طرف جس سے کل کو تعبیر کیا جاتا ہے تو طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ طلاق اپنے محل کی طرف منسوب کی گئی ہے اور یہ مثلاً کہے انت طالق اسلئے کہتے عورت کی ضمیر ہے یا کہے تیری گردن طلاق والی ہے یا تیرا حق طلاق والا ہے یا تیرا سر طلاق والا ہے یا تیری روح یا تیرا بدن یا تیرا جسد یا تیری شرمگاہ یا تیرا چہرہ۔ کیونکہ ان الفاظ کے ذریعہ تمام بدن کو تعبیر کیا جاتا ہے۔ بہر حال جسد اور بدن تو ظاہر ہے۔ اور ایسے ہی ان دونوں کے علاوہ ۔ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا فتحـريـر رقبة یعنی آزاد کرنا ایک گردن اور فرمایا فظلت اعناقهم یعنی خاضعین وہ لوگ ہیں جو خضوع کرنے والے ہیں ۔ اور آنحضرت صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا لعنت کرے اللہ شرمگاہوں پر جو بینوں پر ہوں۔ اور کہا جاتا ہے فلاں شخص راس القوم ہے۔ اور وجہ العرب اور اس کی ذات ہلاک ہو گئی ۔ اور اسی قبیل سے ایک روایت میں دم ہے۔ کہا جاتا ہے اس کا خون رائیگاں ہے اور اسی قبیل سے ( لفظ ) نفس ہے۔ اور وہ ظاہر ہے۔ تشریح صاحب قدوری نے ایک ضابطہ بیان کیا ہے وہ یہ کہ اگر طلاق کل عورت کی طرف منسوب کی گئی یا ایسے جز کی طرف جس سے کل عورت کو تعبیر کیا جاتا ہے تو طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی۔ کیونکہ اس صورت میں طلاق اپنے محل یعنی عورت کی طرف منسوب کی گئی ہے۔ کل عورت کی طرف منسوب کرنے کی مثال انت طالق ہے۔ کیونکہ تا عورت کی ضمیر ہے جس سے کل عورت مراد ہو گی اور جز کی طرف منسوب کرنے کی مثالیں رقبتک طالق الی آخرہ ہیں۔
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ ان مذکورہ الفاظ سے جمیع بدن کو تعبیر کیا جاتا ہے۔ بدن اور جسد سے جمیع بدن کا تعبیر ہونا تو ظاہر ہے۔ اور ایسے ہی ان دونوں کے علاوہ دوسرے مذکورہ الفاظ سے بھی جمیع بدن کو تعبیر کیا جاتا ہے۔ مثلاً کلام پاک میں ہے فتحرير رقبة آیت میں نفس رقبہ مراد نہیں بلکہ ذات مراد ہے۔ اور فرمایا فظلت اعناقهم آیت میں نفس اعتاق مراد نہیں بلکہ ذوات اور اشخاص مراد ہیں۔ کیونکہ اگر نفس اعناق مراد ہوتا تو لہا خاضعین کے بجائے لہا خاضعۂ ہوتا۔ اور حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم نے فرمایا لعن الله الفروج على السروج - اس حدیث میں نفس فروج مراد نہیں۔ بلکہ صاحبہ فروج یعنی عورتوں کی ذات مراد ہے۔ کیونکہ لعنت فرج پر نہیں ہوتی بلکہ ذات پر ہوتی ہے۔ یہ حدیث غریب ہے۔ البتہ اس کے ہم معنی ایک دوسری حدیث ہے۔ عن ابن عباس قال نهى رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم ذوات الفرج ان يركبن السروج اور کہا جاتا ہے فلان رأس القوم یعنی اکبر هم اور وجہ العرب یعنی او جھھم ۔ ان دونوں مقولوں میں نفس راس اور نفس وجہ مراد نہیں ۔ بلکہ ذات اور شخص مراد ہے۔ اور ان دونوں مقولوں سے زیادہ واضح استدلال یہ ہے کہ دعا کے موقع پر کہا جاتا ہے یعیش راسک ظاہر ہے کہ زندہ رہنے کی دعا کسی ایک جز کیلئے نہیں ہوتی ۔ بلکہ پوری ذات کیلئے ہوتی ہے اور وجہ سے ذات میں روح سے نفس روح مراد نہیں بلکہ پوری ذات مراد ہے۔ اور ایک روایت میں دم بھی اسی قبیل سے ہے۔ یعنی دم سے پورے بدن کو تعبیر کیا جاتا ہے، کہا جاتا ہے دمہ ہدر۔ لہذا اگر دم کی طرف طلاق منسوب کی جائے تو طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی اور ایک روایت یہ ہے کہ دم کی طرف طلاق منسوب کرنے سے طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی ۔ اور لفظ نفس بھی اسی قبیل سے ہے کہ اس کی طرف طلاق منسوب کرنے سے طلاق واقع ہو جاتی ہے۔ یہ ظاہر ہے کیونکہ نفس سے مراد ہی ذات ہے۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب
Translation: When a man attributes divorce to the whole woman or to a part by which the whole is expressed, divorce occurs. Because divorce is attributed to its locus. Examples: 'anti taliq' (the pronoun 'anti' refers to the whole woman), 'your neck is divorced', 'your right is divorced', 'your head is divorced', 'your soul', 'your body', 'your flesh', 'your private part', 'your face'. Because these words express the entire body. 'Body' and 'flesh' are obvious. Similarly others. Allah said 'tahriru raqabah' (freeing a neck) meaning a whole person, and 'fazallat a'naquhum' (their necks bowed) meaning they themselves are submissive. The Prophet ﷺ said 'La'anallahu al-furuja 'ala al-suruj' (curse of Allah on private parts on saddles) meaning the women. It is said 'fulan ra'su al-qawm' (so-and-so is the head of the people) meaning their leader, and 'wajhu al-'arab' (face of the Arabs) meaning their chief. Similarly 'dam' (blood) is used for entire person, as in 'damuhu hadar' (his blood is wasted). So if divorce is attributed to dam, it occurs, but there is a narration that it does not. Also 'nafs' (self) clearly refers to the whole person.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proofs. The author states that if a husband attributes divorce to his wife by using a word that refers to her entire being (like 'anti' which is the pronoun for the whole woman) or to a part of her body that is conventionally used to represent the whole (such as neck, head, face, soul, body, flesh, private part, face, blood, or self), then the divorce takes effect. The reason is that talaq must be attributed to its proper locus, which is the wife herself. The author then provides linguistic and scriptural evidence to show that these parts are commonly used to refer to the whole person. For example, the Qur'an uses 'raqabah' (neck) to mean a whole slave, and 'a'naq' (necks) to refer to people bowing. The Hadith 'La'anallahu al-furuja' uses 'furuj' (private parts) to refer to women. The Arabs use 'ra's al-qawm' (head of the people) for leader, and 'wajh al-'arab' (face of the Arabs) for their chief. Even the word 'blood' is used to mean the life of a person, as in 'his blood is wasted' meaning his life. Therefore, when divorce is attributed to any such term, it is considered as if attributed to the whole woman, and divorce occurs. There is a internal Hanafi difference regarding 'blood': the relied-upon position is that divorce does occur, but another narration says it does not. The word 'nafs' clearly means the self, so divorce occurs.

Key Terms
جز معبر عن کل (juz' mu'abbir 'an al-kull): A part that is used idiomatically to represent the whole person.
رقبتک طالق (raqabatuki taliq): A phrase meaning 'your neck is divorced' – considered as divorce of the whole.
دم (dam): Blood, used idiomatically to mean the life or person.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband says to his wife, 'Your hand is divorced,' does divorce occur according to the Hanafi school?
A) Yes, because hand is a part of the body.
B) No, because hand is not a part conventionally used to represent the whole body.
C) Yes, because any part of the body can be a locus for talaq.
D) No, because talaq must be specifically to the wife herself.

Key Takeaway
Attributing talaq to the whole woman or any part idiomatically representing the whole makes the divorce valid.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
6 min
Talaq on an Undifferentiated Part (Juz' Sha'i')
State ruling with analogy to other transactions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when talaq is attributed to an undifferentiated part (juz' sha'i') and apply the analogy to other transactions.

Core Idea
Talaq attributed to an undifferentiated part covers the whole wife because talaq cannot be divided.

Imagine a husband says to his wife, 'Half of you is divorced.' Does such a partial declaration have any effect? In the Hanafi school, it does – and it results in a full divorce. This lesson explains the reasoning behind this ruling, which draws an analogy from other transactions like sale, where undifferentiated shares are valid subjects. Understanding this principle prevents confusion about the indivisible nature of talaq.

Guided Path
1
Define juz' sha'i'
Identify the meaning of juz' sha'i': an unspecified part that applies equally to every portion of the body (e.g., half, third, quarter). Contrast it with a specific limb like 'hand'.
Juz' sha'i' is treated as representing the whole in many legal contexts.
2
Recognise the analogy (qiyas)
See that juz' sha'i' is a valid locus for transactions like sale (e.g., selling 'half of a slave'). The author uses this as the asl (original case) and extends it to talaq, which is also a legal disposition.
The validity of juz' sha'i' in sale is established by ijma'.
3
Apply the principle of indivisibility
Understand that talaq cannot be partial (la yatajazzā). Unlike sale, which can be divided, talaq either applies fully or not at all. Therefore, when attributed to a juz' sha'i', it necessarily applies to the entire wife.
This is the key difference from sale—talaq's unique characteristic.
4
Conclude the ruling
State the final ruling: the divorce takes effect on the whole wife. The pronouncement is valid (sahih) and counts as one revocable divorce if it is the first or second.
The same applies to fractions like 'one-quarter' or 'one-sixth'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
جز شائع کو طلاق دینے کا حکم
و کذلک ان طلق جزء شائعا مثل ان يقول نصفك او ثلثك طالق لان الجزء الشائع محل لسائر التصرفات كالبيع وغيره فكذايكون محلا للطلاق الا انه لا يتجزى فى حق الطلاق فيثبت في الكل ضرورة

ترجمہ اور ایسے ہی (اس پر طلاق واقع ہو گی ) اگر جز ء شائع کو طلاق دی جیسے کہے نصفک یا شلنگ طالق ۔ کیونکہ جز ء شائع تمام تصرفات کا مل ہے ۔ جیسے بیج وغیرہ پس ایسے ہی طلاق کا محل ہے مگر یہ کہ ( جزء شائع ) طلاق کے حق میں متجر ی نہیں ہوتا۔ پس طلاق کل بدن میں بالضرورۃ ثابت ہو جائے گی۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر جز و شائع کی طرف طلاق منسوب کی گئی تو عورت پر طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی ۔ مثلا کہا نصفک طالق یا تلتک طالق یار بعک یا سدسک طالق دلیل سے پہلے جزء، شائع کے معنی ذہن نشین کر لیجئے ۔ جزء شائع کہتے ہیں اس جزء غیر معین کو جو بدن کے ہر ہر حصہ پر صادق آئے۔ دوسری بات یہ کہ جز ء شائع کل کے حکم میں ہوتا ہے۔ اب دلیل ملاحظہ کیجئے ۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ جزء شائع تمام تصرفات (بیع وغیرہ) کا حل ہے اور چونکہ طالق بھی ایک تصرف ہے لہذا اس کا بھی محل ہو گا۔ مگر چونکہ طلاق تقسیم و تجری کو قبول نہیں کرتی یعنی یہ نہیں ہو سکتا کہ طلاق بدن کے کچھ حصہ پر واقع ہو جائے اور کچھ پر واقع نہ ہو اسلئے کل بدن میں ضرورۃ ثابت ہو جائے گی۔
Likewise, if he divorces an undifferentiated part, like saying 'half of you is divorced' or 'a third of you is divorced', then divorce occurs. Because an undifferentiated part is a locus for all transactions like sale etc., so it is a locus for divorce. But since divorce does not admit division, it necessarily takes effect on the whole body. Commentary: Define juz' sha'i': an unspecified part that applies to every portion of the body. It is treated like the whole. The proof is that juz' sha'i' is valid for all transactions, so it is valid for talaq. But talaq cannot be split; therefore it applies to the whole body by necessity.
Source pages p. 248

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof by analogy (qiyas). It states that if a husband attributes divorce to an undifferentiated part (juz' sha'i') of his wife – such as saying 'half of you is divorced' or 'one third of you is divorced' – then the divorce takes effect on the whole wife. The reason is that an undifferentiated part, although not a specific limb, is considered a valid subject for legal dispositions like sale. For example, one can sell 'half of this slave' because the half is an undifferentiated share. Similarly, talaq is a legal disposition, so it can be validly attributed to such a part. However, divorce has the unique characteristic that it cannot be partial – it either occurs fully or not at all. Therefore, when attributed to an undifferentiated part, it necessarily covers the entire wife's body. The author clarifies that juz' sha'i' is an unspecified part that is equally applicable to every part of the body, so it is treated as representing the whole.

Key Terms
جزء شائع (juz' sha'i'): An undifferentiated part that applies to every portion of the body, e.g., half or third.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband says, 'One-quarter of you is divorced,' what is the ruling in the Hanafi school?
A) No divorce occurs because the phrase is unclear.
B) Only one-quarter of the wife is divorced.
C) The entire wife is divorced.
D) It depends on the husband's intention.

Key Takeaway
When talaq is attributed to an undifferentiated part (juz' sha'i'), the full divorce occurs because talaq is indivisible.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate

Talaq Attached to Specific Limbs: Hanafi vs. Shafi'i
Present inter-madhhab dispute on talaq to specific limbs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on talaq attributed to a specific limb (hand, foot) and explain the proof that distinguishes it from an undifferentiated part (juz' sha'i').

Core Idea
Divorce attributed to a specific limb is void because it lacks the marriage restraint.

This lesson examines a classical dispute between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools (with Imam Zufar agreeing with Shafi'i) regarding the validity of divorcing a wife by referencing a specific body part such as 'your hand is divorced' or 'your foot is divorced.' At stake is the fundamental definition of what can be the proper locus (mahall) of talaq. We will explore both sides' proofs and see how the Hanafi concept of qayd al-nikah (marriage restraint) determines the outcome.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify what the Hanafi school rules when a husband says 'your hand is divorced' or 'your foot is divorced'.
Ruling: divorce does not occur.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Recognize that Imam Zufar (within Hanafis) and Imam al-Shafi'i hold that divorce does occur. Understand the scope: the same dispute applies to any specific part not used to express the whole body.
Opponents include Zufar and Shafi'i.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Analyze the opponent's qiyas (analogy): the limb is benefited by the marriage contract, so it is a subject of marriage; therefore it can be a subject for talaq. The ruling then spreads to the whole body, like in juz' sha'i'.
Opponent's dalil: limb is part of the body that is lawful to touch.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Examine the Hanafi refutation: talaq must be attached to a locus that contains the marriage restraint (qayd); a specific limb has no such restraint. Attaching talaq to it is like attaching to saliva or nail – void.
Hanafi distinguishes between juz' mu'ayyan and juz' sha'i'.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
State the practical consequence of the difference: in a case where a husband says 'your hand is divorced', the wife remains married according to Hanafis, but one divorce occurs according to Shafi'is.
Fatwa: Hanafi position is the mufta bihi.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ظہر یدک طالق یا رجلک طالق سے طلاق واقع ہوگی یا نہیں ، اقوال فقہاء
ولو قال یدک طالق اور جلک طالق لم يقع الطلاق وقال زفر والشافعي يقع وكذا الخلاف في كل جزء معين لا يعبر به عن جميع البدن لهما انه جزء متمتع بعقد النكاح وماهذا حاله يكون محلا لحكم النكاح فيكون محلا للطلاق فيثبت الحكم فيه قضية للاضافة ثم يسرى الى الكل كما في الجزء الشائع بخلاف ما اذا اضيف اليه النكاح لان التعدى ممتنع اذ الحرمة في سائر الاجزاء تغلب الحل في هذا الجزء وفي الطلاق الامر على القلب ولنا انه اضاف الطلاق الى غير محله فيلغو كما اذا اضافه الى ريقها او ظفرها وهذا لان محل الطلاق ما يكون فيه القيد لانه ينبيء عن رفع القيد ولا قيد فى اليدولهذا لاتصح اضافة النكاح اليه بخلاف الجزء الشائع لانه محل للنكاح عندنا حتى تصح اضافته اليه فكذا يكون محلا للطلاق واختلفوا ر والبطن والاظهرانه لايصح لانه لا يعبر بهما عن جميع البدن
ترجمہ اور اگر کہا یدک طالق یا رجلک طالق تو طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی ۔ اور امام زفر اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی۔ اور یہی اختلاف ہر اس جز معین میں ہے جس سے جمیع بدن کو تعبیر نہ کیا جاتا ہو ۔ ان دونوں کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ جز وعقد نکاح کی وجہ سے قابل انتفاع ہے۔ اور جس کا حال یہ ہو وہ حکم نکاح کا مل ہوگا ۔ پس محل طلاق ہو گا پھر اس میں حکم مقتضی اضافت کی وجہ سے ثابت ہو جائے گا پھر کل ( بدن) کی طرف سرایت کرے گا۔ جیسا کہ جز ، شائع میں ۔ بخلاف اس صورت کے جبکہ اس کی طرف نکاح کی اضافت کی گئی ہو ۔ کیونکہ تعدی ممتنع ہے۔ اسلئے کہ تمام اجزاء میں حریت اس جزء میں حلت پر غالب آئے گی ۔ اور طالق میں معاملہ برعکس ہے۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ (اس شخص) نے طلاق کی اضافت کی ہے غیر محل طلاق کی طرف پس لغو ہو گا ۔ جیسا کہ جب طلاق کو اس کے تھوک یا اسکے ناخن کی طرف منسوب کیا ہو۔ اور یہ اسلئے کہ محل طلاق وہ ہوتا ہے جس میں قید ( نکاح ) ہو ۔ کیونکہ طالق خبر دیتی ہے رفع قید کی۔ اور ہاتھ میں کوئی قید نہیں۔ اور اسی وجہ سے اسکی طرف نکاح کو منسوب کرنا صحیح نہیں ہے۔ بخلاف جزء شائع کے اسلئے کہ وہ ہمارے نزدیک محل نکاح ہے حتی کہ جزء شائع کی طرف نکاح کی اضافت صحیح ہے۔ پس ایسے ہی محل طلاق ہوگا۔ اور وکیل اور
If he says 'your hand is divorced' or 'your foot is divorced', divorce does not occur. Zufar and Shafi'i said it occurs. The same dispute for every specific part not used to express the whole body. Their proof: This part is benefited by the marriage contract, so it is a subject of marriage ruling, thus a subject for divorce. The ruling is established by attribution, then spreads to the whole, like in juz' sha'i'. Unlike if the marriage was attributed to it, because extension is prevented since the freedom in other parts overcomes the permissibility in this part. In divorce, the opposite. Our proof: He attributed divorce to a non-locus, so it is void, like attributing to her saliva or nail. Because the locus of divorce is that which has the restraint (of marriage), for talaq indicates removal of restraint. The hand has no restraint, so marriage cannot be attributed to it, unlike juz' sha'i' which is a locus for marriage. There is difference of opinion on the head and stomach; the most apparent is it is not valid because they do not express the whole body.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute. The author presents the Hanafi position that if a husband says 'your hand is divorced' or 'your foot is divorced', divorce does not occur. Imam Zufar (a Hanafi scholar) and Imam al-Shafi'i argue that divorce does occur. They analogize these specific limbs to the undifferentiated part (juz' sha'i'), arguing that since the limb is benefited by the marriage contract (i.e., the wife's body is lawful for the husband), it can be a locus for divorce. The divorce then spreads to the whole body because talaq cannot be partial. In contrast, they note that if marriage was attributed to a specific limb, it would not spread because the freedom of the rest of the body overcomes the permissibility in that limb. The Hanafi response is that the hand and foot are not proper loci for divorce because the locus of divorce is that which has the 'qayd' (restraint) of marriage. Marriage imposes a restraint (restriction on sexual access) on the wife, and talaq removes that restraint. A hand or foot is not a place where the marriage restraint is attached; it is not a subject of marriage in the sense that it can be the direct locus of the marriage contract. This is unlike juz' sha'i', which can be the subject of marriage (e.g., half of a slave). Therefore, attributing talaq to a specific limb is like attributing it to her saliva or nail – it is meaningless and divorce does not occur. The passage also mentions an internal Hanafi difference regarding the head (ra's) and stomach (batn); the most apparent (azhar) position is that divorce does not occur because these parts are not conventionally used to represent the whole body.

Key Terms
جز معین (juz' mu'ayyan): A specific, determinate part of the body like hand or foot.
قید نکاح (qayd al-nikah): The restraint of marriage that makes sexual relations lawful only for the husband.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a husband says 'Your head is divorced,' what is the ruling?
A) Divorce occurs because the head is a noble part.
B) Divorce does not occur because the head is not used to express the whole body.
C) Divorce occurs only if he intended it for the whole.
D) Divorce occurs because the head is an essential body part.

Key Takeaway
Attributing talaq to a specific limb (hand, foot) is void in the Hanafi school; only undifferentiated parts (juz' sha'i') can be proper loci.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
8 min
Divorce Directed to a Specific Limb: The Hanafi vs Majority Position
Analyzing the ruling for divorce directed to specific body parts and the scholarly disagreement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on divorce directed to a specific limb and explain the reasoning based on the concept of qayd (marriage restriction).

Core Idea
Divorce is removal of the marriage bond (qayd); only the whole body (or its common part) contains the qayd, so a specific limb is not a valid locus for divorce.

Consider a husband who says to his wife, 'Your hand is divorced.' Does this count as a divorce? The Hanafi school answers with a firm 'no,' while several other prominent jurists rule that it does. In this lesson, we will dissect the legal reasoning behind the Hanafi position, focusing on the concept of the locus of divorce (mahall al-talaq) and the marriage restriction (qayd). This dispute illustrates how a core principle of Hanafi usul—that the locus of a ruling must be the entity that bears the legal attribute—leads to a clear practical outcome.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its attribution
The husband pronounces divorce while attributing it to a specific part of the wife's body (e.g., 'your hand is divorced'). Note that the phrase does not name the wife as a whole person.
Attribution to a part rather than the whole is the key feature.
2
Distinguish between common part (juz' sha'i') and specific part (juz' mu'ayyan)
A common part like 'half' applies to every portion and represents the whole. A specific part like 'hand' or 'foot' does not express the entire body. Hanafis treat the common part as a valid locus for divorce, but not the specific part.
The common part is considered like the whole because it shares the same legal identity.
3
Explain the Hanafi concept of locus (mahall) of divorce
Divorce is the removal of the marriage restriction (qayd). The qayd exists only in the whole body or in something that fully represents it. A specific limb does not contain the qayd, so it cannot be the locus of divorce. Attributing divorce to the hand is like attributing it to saliva or a nail—void.
The hand itself never had a marriage bond; the bond is on the entire person.
4
Compare the opposing proof (compound analogy) and the Hanafi rebuttal
The opponent argues: the hand benefits from marriage (it is a locus of marital intimacy), so it is a locus of marriage rulings, hence a locus of divorce; then divorce spreads to the whole body. Hanafi response: The analogy fails because in marriage, permissibility attributed to a part does not spread (prohibition overpowers), but in divorce, prohibition would spread if it were established. However, the hand never had a marriage restriction, so no divorce can be established in the first place.
The Hanafi rebuttal hinges on the absence of the qayd in the limb.
5
State the mufta bihi and practical consequence
The relied-upon position is that no divorce occurs. Practically, the wife remains married, and the husband cannot claim a divorce was issued. If the husband intends to divorce, he must pronounce it in a way that addresses the whole person, e.g., 'I divorce you.'
Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah explicitly says 'al-azhar' (the most apparent) that it does not occur.

کتاب الطلاق

ترجمہ: اور ایسے ہی (اس پر طلاق واقع ہو گی) اگر جز شائع کو طلاق دی جیسے کہے نصفک یا ثلثک طالق۔ کیونکہ جز شائع تمام تصرفات کا محل ہے جیسے بیع وغیرہ، پس ایسے ہی طلاق کا محل ہے مگر یہ کہ (جز شائع) طلاق کے حق میں متجزی نہیں ہوتا۔ پس طلاق کل بدن میں بالضرورۃ ثابت ہو جائے گی۔ تشریح: صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر جز شائع کی طرف طلاق منسوب کی گئی تو عورت پر طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی۔ مثلاً کہا نصفک طالق یا ثلثک طالق أو ربعک أو سدسک طالق۔ دلیل سے پہلے جزء شائع کے معنی ذہن نشین کر لیجئے۔ جزء شائع کہتے ہیں اس جزء غیر معین کو جو بدن کے ہر ہر حصہ پر صادق آئے۔ دوسری بات یہ کہ جزء شائع کل کے حکم میں ہوتا ہے۔ اب دلیل ملاحظہ کیجئے۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ جزء شائع تمام تصرفات (بیع وغیرہ) کا محل ہے اور چونکہ طلاق بھی ایک تصرف ہے لہذا اس کا بھی محل ہو گا۔ مگر چونکہ طلاق تقسیم و تجزی کو قبول نہیں کرتی یعنی یہ نہیں ہو سکتا کہ طلاق بدن کے کچھ حصہ پر واقع ہو جائے اور کچھ پر واقع نہ ہو اس لئے کل بدن میں ضرورۃ ثابت ہو جائے گی۔

ظہر یدک طالق أو رجلک طالق سے طلاق واقع ہوگی یا نہیں، اقوال فقہاء:
ولو قال یدک طالق أو رجلک طالق لم یقع الطلاق وقال زفر والشافعي یقع وكذا الخلاف في كل جزء معین لا یعبر به عن جمیع البدن. لهما أنه جزء متمتع بعقد النكاح وما هذا حاله يكون محلاً لحكم النكاح فيكون محلاً للطلاق فيثبت الحكم فيه قضية للإضافة ثم يسري إلى الكل كما في الجزء الشائع بخلاف ما إذا أضيف إليه النكاح لأن التعدي ممتنع إذ الحرمة في سائر الأجزاء تغلب الحل في هذا الجزء وفي الطلاق الأمر على القلب. ولنا أنه أضاف الطلاق إلى غير محله فيلغو كما إذا أضافه إلى ريقها أو ظفرها وهذا لأن محل الطلاق ما يكون فيه القيد لأنه ينبئ عن رفع القيد ولا قيد في اليد ولهذا لا تصح إضافة النكاح إليه بخلاف الجزء الشائع لأنه محل للنكاح عندنا حتى تصح إضافته إليه فكذا يكون محلاً للطلاق. واختلفوا في الظهر والبطن والأظهر أنه لا يصح لأنه لا يعبر بهما عن جميع البدن.

ترجمہ: اور اگر کہا یدک طالق یا رجلک طالق تو طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی۔ اور امام زفر اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی۔ اور یہی اختلاف ہر اس جز معین میں ہے جس سے جمیع بدن کو تعبیر نہ کیا جاتا ہو۔ ان دونوں کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ یہ جزء عقد نکاح کی وجہ سے قابل انتفاع ہے۔ اور جس کا حال یہ ہو وہ حکم نکاح کا محل ہوگا۔ پس محل طلاق ہو گا پھر اس میں حکم مقتضی اضافت کی وجہ سے ثابت ہو جائے گا پھر کل (بدن) کی طرف سرایت کرے گا جیسا کہ جزء شائع میں۔ بخلاف اس صورت کے جبکہ اس کی طرف نکاح کی اضافت کی گئی ہو کیونکہ تعدی ممتنع ہے اسلئے کہ تمام اجزاء میں حرمت اس جزء میں حلت پر غالب آئے گی۔ اور طلاق میں معاملہ برعکس ہے۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ (اس شخص) نے طلاق کی اضافت کی ہے غیر محل طلاق کی طرف پس لغو ہو گا جیسا کہ جب طلاق کو اس کے تھوک یا اس کے ناخن کی طرف منسوب کیا ہو۔ اور یہ اسلئے کہ محل طلاق وہ ہوتا ہے جس میں قید (نکاح) ہو کیونکہ طلاق خبر دیتی ہے رفع قید کی۔ اور ہاتھ میں کوئی قید نہیں۔ اور اسی وجہ سے اس کی طرف نکاح کو منسوب کرنا صحیح نہیں ہے۔ بخلاف جزء شائع کے اسلئے کہ وہ ہمارے نزدیک محل نکاح ہے حتی کہ جزء شائع کی طرف نکاح کی اضافت صحیح ہے۔ پس ایسے ہی محل طلاق ہوگا۔

(ص 250) علماء نے اختلاف کیا ظہر اور بطن میں۔ اور اظہر یہ ہے کہ صحیح نہیں کیونکہ ان دونوں کے ساتھ جمیع بدن کو تعبیر نہیں کیا جاتا ہے۔

تشریح: مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر طلاق اس جز معین کی طرف منسوب کی گئی جس سے عورت کے پورے بدن کو تعبیر نہیں کیا جاتا تو طلاق واقع ہوگی یا نہیں۔ اس بارے میں احناف میں سے ائمہ ثلاثہ کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی۔ اور امام زفر، امام شافعی، امام مالک، امام احمد کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی۔ جزء معین جس سے تمام بدن کو تعبیر نہیں کیا جاتا مثلاً ہاتھ، پاؤں، آنکھ، بال، دانت، ناخن۔ امام زفر اور امام شافعی و غیر کی دلیل قیاس مرکب ہے۔ قیاس مرکب اس کو کہتے ہیں جو دو قیاس سے ترکیب پائے اور دوسرے قیاس کا صغریٰ پہلے قیاس کا نتیجہ ہو۔ اب حاصل یہ ہو گا: جزء معین (ید وغیرہ) عقد نکاح کی وجہ سے قابل انتفاع ہے اور ہر وہ جز جو عقد نکاح کی وجہ سے قابل انتفاع ہو حکم نکاح کا محل ہو گا۔ اور جو جز حکم نکاح کا محل ہے وہ طلاق کا محل ہوگا۔ پس نتیجہ نکالا کہ جزء معین (ید وغیرہ) طلاق کا محل ہے۔ پس جب ایک جزء میں حکم طلاق ثابت ہو گیا تو وہ کل بدن کی طرف سرایت کر جائے گا۔

اور قیاس فقہی کی صورت یہ ہوگی کہ وہ جز جس سے جمیع بدن کو تعبیر نہیں کیا جاتا حکم نکاح کا محل ہے۔ لہذا محل طلاق ہو گا جیسا کہ جزء شائع۔

بخلاف ما إذا أضيف إليه النكاح سے ایک سوال کا جواب ہے۔ سوال یہ ہے کہ بقول آپ کے جب جز معین حکم نکاح کا محل ہے تو جز معین کی طرف نکاح کی اضافت کرنے کی صورت میں نکاح منعقد ہو جانا چاہئے حالانکہ آپ اس صورت میں انعقاد نکاح کے قائل نہیں ہیں۔ امام زفر اور امام شافعی کی طرف سے جواب یہ ہے کہ جب جز معین کی طرف نکاح کی اضافت کی گئی تو صرف اس جزء میں حلت ثابت ہوگی اور باقی تمام اجزاء میں حرمت ہوگی۔ اور حلت کا باقی تمام اجزاء کی طرف سرایت کرنا ممکن نہیں کیونکہ تمام اجزاء کی حرمت اس جزء کی حلت پر غالب رہے گی۔ اور طلاق میں معاملہ برعکس ہے کیونکہ جب ایک جزء کی طرف طلاق منسوب کی گئی تو یہ جزء حرام ہوگا اور باقی حلال۔ اور جب حرام و حلال جمع ہو جائیں تو حرام کو ترجیح ہوگی۔ اسلئے ہم نے کہا کہ ہاتھ وغیرہ کی طرف طلاق منسوب کرنے سے کل بدن پر طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی اور نکاح منعقد نہیں ہوگا۔

ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ان صورتوں میں طلاق غیر محل کی طرف منسوب کی گئی ہے لہذا طلاق لغو ہوگی۔ جیسے کسی نے اپنی بیوی کے تھوک یا ناخن کی طرف طلاق کو منسوب کر دیا۔ اور ہاتھ وغیرہ کا محل طلاق نہ ہونا اسلئے ہے کہ محل طلاق وہ ہوگا جس میں قید نکاح موجود ہو کیونکہ طلاق کے معنی ہی رفع قید کے ہیں۔ اور رفع قید اس وقت ہوگا جبکہ پہلے قید ہو۔ اور ہاتھ وغیرہ میں کوئی قید نہیں لہذا ہاتھ وغیرہ کی طرف طلاق منسوب کر دینے سے طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی۔ یہی وجہ ہے کہ جز معین ہاتھ وغیرہ کی طرف نکاح کی اضافت کر دینے سے نکاح منعقد نہیں ہوتا۔ بخلاف جزء شائع کے کیونکہ جزء شائع محل نکاح ہے حتی کہ جزء شائع کی طرف نکاح کی اضافت درست ہے۔ لہذا جزء شائع محل طلاق بھی ہو گا۔

دلیل احناف کی تقریر یہ بھی ہو سکتی ہے کہ ہاتھ پاؤں وغیرہ اطراف انسان ہیں اور اطراف تابع ہوتے ہیں۔ اور قاعدہ ہے کہ اصل کے ذکر سے تابع کا ذکر ہو جاتا ہے لیکن تابع کے ذکر سے اصل کا ذکر نہیں ہوتا۔
Book of Divorce. Translation: And similarly, divorce occurs if divorce is given to a common part, such as saying 'half of you is divorced' or 'a third of you is divorced'. Because a common part is the locus of all transactions like sale, etc., so similarly it is the locus of divorce, except that a common part is not divisible in the right of divorce. So divorce necessarily becomes established in the entire body. Explanation: The issue is that if divorce is attributed to a common part, then divorce will occur upon the woman. For example, he said 'half of you is divorced' or 'a third of you is divorced' or 'a quarter' or 'a sixth'. Before the proof, understand the meaning of common part. A common part is called that unspecified part that applies to every portion of the body. Second, a common part is considered like the whole. Now consider the proof. The proof is that a common part is the locus of all transactions (sale, etc.), and since divorce is also a transaction, therefore it will be its locus. But since divorce does not accept division and partition, i.e., it is not possible that divorce occurs on some part of the body and not on another, therefore it necessarily becomes established in the entire body. Regarding the statement 'your hand is divorced' or 'your foot is divorced', will divorce occur or not? The statements of the jurists: If he said 'your hand is divorced' or 'your foot is divorced', divorce does not occur, and Zufar and al-Shafi'i said it occurs. And similarly the dispute is regarding every specific part that is not used to express the entire body. Their proof is that it is a part that benefits from the marriage contract, and whatever has this status is a locus of the ruling of marriage, so it is a locus of divorce; then the ruling is established in it by virtue of the attribution, then it spreads to the whole, as in the common part, unlike when marriage is attributed to it because transference is impossible, since the prohibition in the other parts overpowers the permissibility in this part, and in divorce the matter is the opposite. Our proof is that he attributed divorce to other than its locus, so it is void, as if he attributed it to her saliva or her nail. This is because the locus of divorce is that which has the restriction (of marriage), because divorce indicates the removal of restriction, and there is no restriction in the hand. For this reason, attributing marriage to it is not valid, unlike the common part because it is a locus of marriage according to us, such that attributing marriage to it is valid, so likewise it becomes a locus of divorce. And they differed regarding the back and the belly, and the most apparent is that it is not valid because they are not used to express the entire body. (Page 250) The scholars differed regarding the back and the belly, and the most apparent is that it is not correct because the entire body is not expressed by these two. Explanation: The issue is that if divorce is attributed to a specific part by which the entire body of the woman is not expressed, will divorce occur or not? In this regard, among the Hanafis, the position of the three imams is that divorce does not occur. And the position of Imam Zufar, Imam al-Shafi'i, Imam Malik, Imam Ahmad is that divorce will occur. A specific part by which the entire body is not expressed, e.g., hand, foot, eye, hair, tooth, nail. The proof of Imam Zufar and al-Shafi'i and others is compound analogy. Compound analogy is called that which is composed of two analogies, and the minor premise of the second analogy is the result of the first analogy. Now the result becomes: The specific part (hand etc.) benefits from the marriage contract, and every part that benefits from the marriage contract is a locus of the ruling of marriage, and any part that is a locus of the ruling of marriage is a locus of divorce. So the conclusion is that the specific part (hand etc.) is a locus of divorce. So when the ruling of divorce is established in one part, it will spread to the entire body. The form of the legal analogy is that a part by which the entire body is not expressed is a locus of the ruling of marriage, therefore it is a locus of divorce as in the common part. 'Unlike when marriage is attributed to it' is an answer to a question. The question is: According to your statement, when a specific part is a locus of the ruling of marriage, then if marriage is attributed to a specific part, marriage should be valid, but you do not hold the validity of marriage in that case. The answer from Imam Zufar and al-Shafi'i is that when marriage is attributed to a specific part, only that part becomes permissible and all other parts remain prohibited. And the permissibility cannot spread to the other parts because the prohibition in all parts overpowers the permissibility in this part. And in divorce the matter is opposite because when divorce is attributed to one part, that part becomes prohibited and the rest become permissible. And when prohibited and permissible are combined, the prohibited is given preference. Therefore we said that attributing divorce to the hand etc. will cause divorce to occur on the entire body, and marriage will not be valid. Our proof is that in these cases, divorce is attributed to other than its locus, so the divorce is void, like when someone attributes divorce to his wife's saliva or nail. And the reason the hand etc. are not a locus of divorce is that the locus of divorce is that which has the restriction of marriage because divorce means removal of restriction. And removal of restriction occurs only when there was a restriction before. And there is no restriction in the hand etc., so attributing divorce to the hand etc. does not effect divorce. For this reason, attributing marriage to a specific part like the hand does not validate marriage. Unlike the common part because the common part is a locus of marriage such that attributing marriage to it is valid, so likewise it will be a locus of divorce. The proof of the Hanafis can also be stated as: The hand, foot, etc. are parts of the human body, and parts are dependent. And the rule is that mentioning the principal implies the dependent, but mentioning the dependent does not imply the principal.
Source pages p. 249

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute concerning the validity of divorce when directed to a specific limb of the wife's body (e.g., 'your hand is divorced') versus a common part (juz' sha'i') like 'half of you'. The Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani) is that such a divorce does not occur, while Imam Zufar, al-Shafi'i, Malik, and Ahmad hold that it does. The author first clarifies that a common part (a non-specific fraction applicable to every portion) is a valid locus of divorce, but since divorce cannot be divided, it applies to the whole body. Then the main dispute arises: for a specific limb like the hand or foot, the Hanafis say it is not a valid locus because divorce is the removal of the marriage bond (qayd), and only the whole body (or a common part representing the whole) can be the subject of that bond. The opposing scholars argue via compound analogy: the limb benefits from marriage (e.g., intimacy is allowed), so it is a locus of marriage rulings, hence a locus of divorce; once established, it spreads. The Hanafi rebuttal distinguishes between marriage and divorce: marriage's effect (permissibility) is restricted to the part if attributed to a limb, but divorce's effect (prohibition) spreads because prohibition overpowers permissibility. Furthermore, the Hanafis assert that the hand has no marriage restriction (qayd) itself; therefore, attributing divorce to it is like attributing it to saliva or a nail—void. The passage also notes that the back and belly are similarly treated, with the relied-upon view being non-occurrence.

Key Terms
جزء شائع (juz' sha'i'): A non-specified fraction that applies equally to every part of the body, e.g., half, third.
جزء معین (juz' mu'ayyan): A specific, designated part of the body that does not express the whole body, e.g., hand, foot.
قید (qayd): The marriage bond/restriction that makes marital relations permissible; divorce removes this qayd.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a husband says to his wife 'your hand is divorced,' what is the ruling?
A) Divorce occurs and spreads to the whole body.
B) Divorce does not occur because the hand is not a valid locus for divorce.
C) Only the hand becomes divorced, not the rest of the body.
D) The husband must repeat the divorce to make it effective.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the locus of divorce is the whole body that bears the marriage bond; a specific limb does not qualify, so divorce directed to a limb is void.

Talaq — Divorce

Fractional Talaq Counts as One Full Talaq
Ruling on fractional talaq with proof and examples

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi principle that talaq is indivisible and state that any fractional expression of talaq (e.g., half, third, quarter) results in one full talaq.

Core Idea
Talaq is indivisible: a fraction equals a whole.

What happens if a husband says 'half talaq' or 'third of a talaq'? Intuitively, one might think only a partial divorce occurs. However, Hanafi law treats talaq as an indivisible legal act, so any fractional expression counts as one full talaq. This lesson explains the principle and its rationale, with examples that clarify how to handle such utterances.

Guided Path
1
Identify the utterance
First, determine what fractional expression the husband used (e.g., half, third, quarter, or any named fraction).
The fraction must be explicitly stated; implied fractions are treated similarly.
2
Apply the principle of indivisibility
State that talaq (طلاق) is ma la yatajazza – not divisible into parts. Therefore, mentioning any part is equivalent to mentioning the whole.
This is a settled Hanafi rule (قاعدة) with no ikhtilaf among the three imams.
3
Determine the number of talaqs
Conclude that one full talaq occurs, regardless of the fraction named. For example, 'half talaq' = one talaq, 'third talaq' = one talaq, etc.
For composite fractions like 'half of two talaqs', calculate the whole: half of two is one, so one talaq occurs. For 'three halves of two talaqs', three halves of two is three, so three talaqs occur.
4
Understand the rationale
The rationale is to avoid the husband's speech being legally meaningless (laghw) and to give preference to prohibition (haram) over permissibility (halal) when both are possible.
This ensures that the utterance has effect and that divorce, which is makruh, is not lightened.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
نصف تطليقہ اور ثلث تطليقہ سے طلاق دینے کا حکم وان طلقها نصف تطليقة أو ثلث تطليقة كانت طالقا تطليقه واحدة لان الطلاق لا يتجزى وذكر بعض ما لا يتجزى كذكر الكل وكذا الجواب في كل جزء سماه لما بينا

ترجمہ اور اگر طلاق دی (عورت) کو ایک طلاق کا نصف یا ایک طلاق کا ایک تہائی تو وہ ایک طلاق والی ہوگی۔ کیونکہ طلاق متجز نہیں ہوتی ۔ اور بعض ما لا يتجزى کا ذکر کل کے ذکر کے مانند ہے۔ اور یہی حکم ہر ایسے جزء میں ہے جس کو بیان کیا ہو۔ اس دلیل کی وجہ سے جو ہم نے بیان کی ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر کسی مرد نے اپنی منکوحہ کو نصف طلاق دے دی یا ثلث طلاق تو اس کو پوری ایک طلاق شمار کیا جائیگا۔ اور وہ عورت ایک طلاق کے ساتھ مطلقہ ہو گی۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ طلاق متجزی نہیں ہوتی۔ یعنی منقسم ہو کر ٹکڑے ٹکڑے نہیں ہوتی ۔ اور قاعدہ ہے کہ بعض ما لا يتجزی کا ذکر کل کے ذکر کے مانند ہوتا ہے۔ تو گویا نصف طلاق یا ثلث طلاق کا ذکر کرنا کل کا ذکر کرنا ہے۔ اسلئے ان الفاظ کے ساتھ پوری ایک طلاق واقع ہوگی ۔ رہی یہ بات کہ مالا یتجزی کے بعض کا ذکر کل کے ذکر کے مانند کیوں ہوتا ہے؟ تو وجہ اس کی یہ ہے کہ عاقل بالغ کا کلام لغو ہونے سے محفوظ ہو جائے گا اور اس صورت میں حرام کو حلال پر غلبہ بھی حاصل ہو جائے گا۔ اور یہی حکم ہر اس جزء میں ہے جسکو بیان کیا ہو۔ مثلاً طلاق کا چوتھائی یا ہزارواں حصہ دیا تو ایک طلاق واقع ہوگی سابقہ دلیل کیوجہ سے۔ انت طالق انصاف تطلیقتین سے کتنی طلاقیں واقع ہوں گی ولوقال لها انت طالق ثلثة انصاف تطليقتين فهي طالق ثلثا لان نصف التطليقتين تطليقة فاذاجمع بين ثلثة
The ruling of giving talaq with half talaq or third talaq: And if he divorces her half a talaq or one third of a talaq, she becomes divorced with one talaq because talaq is not divisible. And mentioning a part of what is indivisible is like mentioning the whole. And similar is the answer for every part he named for the reason we explained. Translation: And if a man gives divorce to his wife half of a talaq or one third of a talaq, she will be divorced by one talaq. Because talaq is not divisible. And mentioning a part of what is indivisible is like mentioning the whole. Explanation: If a man says to his wife 'half talaq' or 'third talaq', it will be counted as one full talaq. Evidence: Talaq is indivisible. The principle: mentioning a part of an indivisible thing is like mentioning the whole. Why? To avoid the speech of a legally competent adult being meaningless, and to give preference to prohibition over permissibility. This applies to every such part, e.g., quarter talaq or thousandth talaq, one talaq occurs. How many talaqs occur if he says 'you are divorced half of two talaqs'? And if he says 'you are divorced three halves of two talaqs', she is divorced by three talaqs, because half of two talaqs is one talaq, so when three are combined...
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling on fractional expressions of talaq. The core matn states: if a husband says 'half talaq' or 'third of a talaq', then one full talaq occurs. The reason is that talaq is indivisible (la yatajazza). The principle applied is that mentioning a part of an indivisible thing is equivalent to mentioning the whole (dikhr ba'd ma la yatajazza ka dhikr al-kull). The commentary expands by explaining the rationale: to prevent the husband's utterance from being legally null (laghw), and to give preference to the prohibition (haram) over permissibility (halal) when both are present. This principle is applied uniformly: whether the husband says half, third, quarter, or even a thousandth of a talaq, it counts as one full talaq. The passage then raises a further question: if the husband says 'you are divorced half of two talaqs', the answer is that this amounts to one talaq (since half of two is one). If he says 'you are divorced three halves of two talaqs', then three talaqs occur (since three halves of two is three). The text ends mid-sentence but the ruling is clear.

Key Terms
مالا يتجزى (ma la yatajazza): That which is not divisible into parts; in this context, talaq is considered indivisible, so any fractional expression of talaq is treated as a complete talaq.
بعض ما لا يتجزى كذكر الكل (ba'd ma la yatajazza ka dhikr al-kull): The principle that mentioning a part of an indivisible entity is equivalent to mentioning the whole, used here to treat half or third talaq as a full talaq.

Key Takeaway
Any fractional expression of talaq (half, third, quarter, etc.) results in one full talaq because talaq is legally indivisible.

Talaq by Saying 'Back' or 'Belly': The Azhar Opinion
Exposition of differing opinions among later scholars

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the two positions among the Hanafi mashayikh regarding talaq by naming a body part and explain why the azhar view is that talaq does not occur.

Core Idea
Talaq by naming a part requires customary usage of that part for the whole body.

In this passage, the author of al-Hidayah presents a disagreement among later Hanafi scholars (mashayikh) about a specific talaq wording. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to distinguish between essential necessity and customary usage in legal language—a key skill in Hanafi fiqh.

Guided Path
1
Identify the contested statement
Read the two example sentences: 'your back is divorced' and 'your belly is divorced'. These are the triggers for the dispute.
2
State the two opinions
One group says talaq occurs; the other says it does not. The text labels the latter as 'azhar' (more correct).
Both opinions are from later mashayikh, not the founding imams.
3
Analyze the reasoning for talaq occurring
Supporters argue: back and belly are essential for marriage (nikah is impossible without them), and the word 'zahr' is sometimes used for the whole body, as in the hadith 'la sadaqata illa an zahr ghina'.
This hadith is about surplus wealth, not body parts – a linguistic argument.
4
Analyze the reasoning for talaq NOT occurring (azhar)
The azhar view counters: these parts are not customarily used to refer to the whole body. Evidence: if one says 'your back is like my mother's back', it does not constitute zihar (which requires a whole-body analogy).
The zihar analogy is key: if the phrase doesn't trigger zihar, it shouldn't trigger talaq.
5
Determine the practical consequence
If talaq occurs, the wife becomes divorced; if not, the marriage continues. The mufta bihi is that talaq does not occur.
This ruling applies even though the parts are essential for marriage.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر کسی نے اپنی منکوجہ سے کہا ظهرک طالق یا بطنک طالق تو اس میں مشائخ کا اختلاف ہے۔ بعض کی رائے ہے کہ طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ ظہر اور بطن اصل کے معنی میں ہے۔ اسلئے کہ بغیر ان دونوں کے نکاح ممکن نہیں ہے اور لفظ ظہر سے جمیع بدن کو بھی تعبیر کیا جاتا ہے۔ جیسا کہ حضور صلى الله عليه وسلم کا فرمان ہے لا صدقة الا عن ظهر غنی عینی شرح ہدایہ ) اور بعض کی رائے یہ ہے کہ ان دونوں اجزاء کی طرف طلاق منسوب کرنے سے طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی۔ یہی قول اظہر ہے اسلئے کہ ان دونوں سے جميع بدن کو تعبیر نہیں کیا جاتا۔ اسی وجہ سے اگر کسی نے اپنی منکوحہ سے کہا ظهرک یا بطنک علی کظهرامی تو یہ ظہار کرنے والا نہیں ہوگا۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب
The author of al-Hidayah says: If a man said to his wife 'Your back is divorced' or 'Your belly is divorced', then there is disagreement among the mashayikh (later scholars). Some opine that talaq will occur, because back and belly are essential (for marriage), for without them nikah is not possible, and the word 'zahr' is also used for the whole body, as the Prophet ﷺ said: 'There is no charity except from the back of wealth' (as in 'Ayni's commentary on Hidayah). And some opine that associating talaq with these two parts does not result in talaq; this is the more correct (azhar) opinion, because these two are not used for the whole body. For this reason, if a man said to his wife 'Your back or your belly is like the back of my mother', he would not be making zihar. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 251

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute among later scholars (mashayikh) regarding the effect of saying 'your back is divorced' or 'your belly is divorced'. One group holds talaq occurs because (a) the back and belly are essential for marriage (without them sexual intercourse is impossible), and (b) the word 'zahr' (back) is sometimes used figuratively for the whole body, as in the hadith 'la sadaqata illa an zahr ghina' (no charity except from surplus wealth), where 'zahr ghina' means surplus wealth. The other group, considered the azhar (more correct) opinion, says talaq does not occur because these body parts are not conventionally used to refer to the whole body. Evidence: if one says 'your back or belly is like my mother's back', it does not constitute zihar (which requires the whole body analogy). Thus, the general principle is that talaq by naming a part does not occur unless that part is used customarily for the whole. The azhar view aligns with the earlier Hanafi position on 'yad' and is preferred.

Key Terms
ظہر (zahr): Back; used in the text to refer to a body part and also metaphorically for surplus in the hadith.
بطن (batn): Belly; a specific body part.
مشائخ (mashāyikh): Later Hanafi scholars after the founding imams, whose opinions may differ from the earlier authorities.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the azhar opinion, if a man tells his wife 'your belly is divorced', what is the ruling?
A) Talaq occurs because the belly is essential for marriage.
B) Talaq does not occur because 'batn' is not used for the whole body.
C) Talaq occurs only if the wife objects.
D) The husband must perform zihar.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, talaq by naming a body part requires that the part be customarily used for the whole person; mere essentiality is insufficient.

Talaq by Half or Third of a Divorce
Ruling that mentioning a fraction of talaq counts as one full talaq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a husband uses a fraction of talaq and explain why the principle of indivisibility (ma la yatajazza) applies.

Core Idea
Talaq is indivisible: mentioning any fraction counts as one full talaq.

This passage addresses a common question in family law: if a husband says 'I divorce you with half a talaq' or 'one-third of a talaq', what is the legal effect? The Hanafi school rules that one full talaq occurs. The reasoning is rooted in the legal principle that talaq is not divisible (ma la yatajazza), so mention of a part is equivalent to mention of the whole. This prevents the husband's words from being futile and upholds the gravity of divorce.

Guided Path
1
Identify the scenario and the uttered words
Recognize that the husband uses a fraction (e.g., half, third) attached to the word 'talaq'. The key is that he explicitly says 'half a talaq' or 'one-third of a talaq'.
The wording may vary: 'nisf talaq', 'thulth talaq', or any fraction.
2
Apply the principle of indivisibility
Talaq is legally indivisible (ma la yatajazza). Therefore, mentioning a part of a non-divisible thing is treated as mentioning the whole (ذكر بعض ما لا يتجزى كذكر الكل).
This is a settled maxim in Hanafi fiqh, derived from the need to give meaningful effect to the husband's speech.
3
Derive the ruling and extend to all fractions
The result is that one full talaq occurs, regardless of the fraction mentioned. This applies to any fraction: quarter, thousandth, etc. The reasoning also gives precedence to prohibition (haram) over permissibility, a Hanafi precaution in talaq matters.
The commentary highlights that the husband's speech is preserved from being futile (laghw), and the stricter consequence (divorce) is enforced.

The ruling of giving talaq by half a divorce or one-third of a divorce. And if he divorces her with half a talaq or one-third of a talaq, she becomes divorced with one talaq, because talaq is not divisible, and mentioning a part of that which is not divisible is like mentioning the whole. And the same answer applies to every part that is mentioned, for the reason we have stated. Translation: And if he divorces (the woman) with half of one divorce or one-third of one divorce, then she becomes divorced with one talaq, because talaq is not divisible. And mentioning part of a non-divisible thing is like mentioning the whole. And this is the ruling for every such part that is specified, due to the proof we have mentioned. Explanation: The issue is that if a man gives his wife half a divorce or one-third of a divorce, it will be counted as one full divorce, and she will be divorced by one talaq. The proof is that talaq is not divisible, i.e., it cannot be split into pieces. And the rule is that mentioning part of a non-divisible thing is like mentioning the whole. So to mention half a divorce or one-third of a divorce is like mentioning the whole. Therefore, with these words one full talaq occurs. The proof is that talaq is not divisible. And why is mentioning part of a non-divisible thing like mentioning the whole? The reason is that the speech of a sane adult is preserved from being futile, and in this case, the forbidden (haram) will prevail over the permissible (halal). And this ruling applies to every part that is specified, for example, if he gives one-fourth or one-thousandth of a divorce, one talaq occurs due to the previous proof.

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement with proof on the effect of fractional talaq. The core rule: if a husband says 'I divorce you with half a talaq' or 'one-third of a talaq', it counts as one full talaq. The reason is that talaq (divorce) is legally indivisible—it cannot be split into fractions. The principle applied is that 'mentioning part of a non-divisible thing is like mentioning the whole' (ذكر بعض ما لا يتجزى كذكر الكل). This prevents the husband's speech from being meaningless (لغو). Since talaq is either complete or nothing, any fraction is treated as the whole. This applies to any fraction: quarter, thousandth, etc. The commentary also notes that this interpretation gives precedence to the prohibition (haram) over the permissible, meaning that divorce (which makes marital relations haram) is enforced rather than ignored, in line with the Hanafi principle of precaution in talaq.

Key Terms
ما لا يتجزی (mā lā yatajazza): That which is not divisible; talaq cannot be split into smaller units.

Key Takeaway
Any fraction of talaq results in one full talaq because talaq is legally indivisible (ma la yatajazza).

Talaq by Halves: The Dispute on Three Halves of One Talaq
Intra-Hanafi dispute on fractional talaq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the two Hanafi views on the number of talaqs when a husband says 'three halves of one talaq' and identify the thamarah al-khilaf.

Core Idea
Half of a talaq counts as a whole, but combining halves with a base number yields a dispute: two or three talaqs?

When a husband uses fractional expressions in talaq, Hanafi jurists apply the rule that fractions of talaq are treated as whole talaqs. However, when the fraction is tied to a specific number, different interpretations arise. This passage presents two opinions on whether 'three halves of one talaq' results in two or three talaqs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
The text considers two expressions: 'three halves of two divorces' and 'three halves of one divorce'. Recognize that the first scenario yields unanimous three talaqs, while the second is disputed.
2
Derive the unanimous ruling
For 'three halves of two divorces': half of two talaqs is one talaq, so three halves = three talaqs. This is agreed upon.
The principle: half of a talaq counts as one talaq.
3
State the two views on the second scenario
For 'three halves of one divorce': one view holds that it is one and a half talaqs, and since talaq is indivisible, the half becomes complete, making two talaqs. The second view holds that each half becomes a complete talaq in itself, making three talaqs.
Note the different applications of the same principle.
4
Analyze the thamarah al-khilaf
If two talaqs occur, the husband retains the right of raj'ah (return) during the iddah. If three talaqs occur, the divorce becomes irrevocable (baynunah kubra) and the wife is not halal to him until she marries another man and is divorced.
This practical difference is crucial for fatwa.

Source Text

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the number of talaqs when a husband uses the phrase 'three halves' in combination with either 'two divorces' or 'one divorce'. The first case ('three halves of two divorces') is straightforward: half of two talaqs is one talaq, so three halves equal three talaqs. The second case ('three halves of one talaq') is disputed. One view: it amounts to one and a half talaqs; since talaq is indivisible, the half is counted as a full talaq, making two talaqs total. Another view: each half is an independent entity that becomes complete, so three halves yield three talaqs. The commentary does not specify which view is mufta bihi, but the dispute reflects the general principle that fractions of talaq are treated as whole talaqs, but when combined with a specific number, the outcome depends on interpretation of the wording.

Talaq with Ranged Expressions: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Dispute on talaq count with ranged expressions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi opinions on the number of talaqs when a husband uses ranged expressions and explain the reasoning behind each opinion.

Core Idea
Ranged expressions in talaq are interpreted differently by Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn, and Zufar based on custom, literal meaning, and qiyas.

This passage presents a classic intra-Hanafi dispute on how to count talaqs when the husband uses phrases like 'from one to two' or 'between one and three'. Each founding imam offers a distinct interpretation, rooted in different methodological approaches: literal language, customary usage (urf), and strict qiyas. Understanding this dispute deepens your appreciation of how legal reasoning works within a single madhhab.

Guided Path
1
Identify the expressions and the three positions
List the two expressions given ('from one to two' and 'from one to three') and note the number of talaqs according to Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn, and Zufar.
The source explicitly states the numbers for each imam.
2
Understand Zufar's reasoning (qiyas)
Zufar applies strict qiyas: the ghaya (limit) is not included in the limited, so 'from one to two' yields no talaq and 'from one to three' yields one. He analogizes to a sale where 'from this wall to that wall' excludes the walls.
This is the qiyas al-khafi approach.
3
Understand the Sahibayn's reasoning (istihsan based on urf)
The Sahibayn use istihsan: in common custom, phrases like 'from one to two' intend the whole range, so they yield two and three talaqs respectively. They compare to 'take from my wealth from one to a hundred'.
Custom ('urf) overrides qiyas when it contradicts common usage.
4
Understand Abu Hanifa's reasoning
Abu Hanifa interprets the expressions as indicating the more from the less and the less from the more, as in 'from sixty to seventy' or 'between sixty and seventy'. Thus 'from one to two' means one and 'from one to three' means two. He also notes that the first number must actually occur for the second to be based on it.
He argues that in talaq, the principle is restriction (khatar), so the whole range is not intended.
5
Note the practical consequence and the role of intention
The text ends by stating that if the husband intended only one talaq, he is believed privately (dinan) but not in court, because his speech is ambiguous.
This shows the interplay between literal meaning and intention.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و لو قال انت طالق من واحدة الى ثنتين او مابين واحدة الى ثنتين فهي واحدة وان قال من واحدة الى ثلث اومابين واحدة الى ثلث فهى ثنتان وهذا عند ابي حنيفة وقالا في الاولى هي ثنتان و في الثانية ثلث وقال زفر فى الأولى لايقع شيء وفى الثانية تقع واحدة وهو القياس لان الغاية لاتدخل تحت المضروب له الغاية كما لوقال بعت منك من هذا الحائط الى هذا الحائط وجه قولهما وهو الاستحسان ان مثل هذا الكلام متى ذكر في العرف يراد به الکل كما تقول لغيرك خذمن مالی من درهم الى مائة ولابي حنيفة ان المراد به الاكثر من الاقل والاقل من الاكثر فانهم يقولون سنى من ستين الى سبعين وما بين ستين الى سبعين ويريدون به ما ذكرناه وارادة الكل فيما طريقه طريق الاباحة كما ذكر او الاصل في الطلاق هو الخطر ثم الغاية الاولى لابد ان تكون موجودة لترتب عليها الثانيه ووجودها بوقوعها بخلاف البيع لان الغاية فيه موجودة قبل البيع ولونوى واحدة يدين ديانة لاقضاء لانه محتمل كلامه لكنه خلاف الظاهر ترجمہ اور اگر کہا تو ایک سے دو تک طلاق والی ہے یا مابین ایک کے دو تک تو ایک (واقع ) ہوگی ۔ اور اگر کہا ایک سے تین تک یا ما بین ایک کے تین تک تو یہ دو ہوں گی اور یہ ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک ہے اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ پہلی (صورت ) میں دو اور دوسری (صورت ) میں
And if he says: 'You are divorced from one to two' or 'between one and two', then it is one (talaq). And if he says 'from one to three' or 'between one and three', then it is two. This is according to Abu Hanifa. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: in the first case it is two, and in the second case three. And Zufar said: in the first case nothing occurs, and in the second case one occurs, and this is qiyas, because the limit (ghaya) does not fall under that which is limited, as if he says 'I sold you from this wall to this wall'. The basis of their (Sahibayn) view is istihsan: that such speech, when used in custom, intends the whole, like you say to another 'take from my wealth from one dirham to a hundred'. And according to Abu Hanifa, the intended meaning is the more from the less and the less from the more, for they say 'a year from sixty to seventy' and 'between sixty and seventy' and they mean what we mentioned. And intending the whole in matters that are permissible (mubah) is as mentioned, but the principle in talaq is restriction (khatar). Then the first limit must exist for the second to be based on it, and its existence is by its occurrence, unlike sale because the limit exists before the sale. And if he intended one (talaq), he is believed in private (dinan) but not in court (qada'an), because his speech is probable, but it is contrary to the apparent. Translation: And if he says 'you are divorced from one to two' or 'between one and two', then one (talaq) occurs. And if he says 'from one to three' or 'between one and three', then two occur. This is according to Abu Hanifa. And the Sahibayn said: in the first case two, and in the second three. And Zufar said: in the first nothing occurs, and in the second one occurs. This (Zufar's view) is qiyas, because the limit (ghaya) is not included in the limited, like 'I sold you from this wall to this wall'. The basis of the Sahibayn's view is istihsan: such speech in custom intends the whole, as when you say 'take from my wealth from one dirham to a hundred'. And Abu Hanifa's view is that it intends the more from the less and the less from the more, as they say 'a year from sixty to seventy' and 'between sixty and seventy' meaning that. And intending the whole applies in matters of permissibility, but the principle in talaq is restriction. Then the first limit must exist for the second to be based on it, and it exists by its occurrence, unlike sale. And if he intends one, he is believed in private but not in court.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage details an intra-Hanafi dispute among Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani), and Zufar regarding the number of talaqs when a husband uses ranged expressions like 'from one to two' or 'between one and three'. Abu Hanifa holds that 'from one to two' yields one talaq, and 'from one to three' yields two talaqs. His reasoning: such expressions in common language indicate the more from the less and the less from the more—like saying 'from sixty to seventy' meaning the whole range. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) adopt istihsan based on custom: phrases like 'from one to two' or 'from one to three' in common usage intend the entire range, so 'from one to two' means two and 'from one to three' means three. Zufar holds to strict qiyas: the ghaya (limit/end) is not included in the limited, so 'from one to two' means nothing (only the single number one is specified, but the range doesn't include the end?), and 'from one to three' would mean one (the first number only). The text explains that the Sahibayn's istihsan relies on 'urf and the principle that such phrases intend the whole in permissive contexts, but talaq is a matter of restriction (khatar). However, Abu Hanifa argues that the first number must exist for the second to be added, and its existence is by actually occurring. The final ruling: if the husband intended one, he is believed privately (dinan) but not in court. The text does not state a tarjih but presents all positions.

Key Terms
غایت (ghāya): Limit or endpoint; in talaq, the number mentioned as the end of a range.
صاحبین (Sāhibayn): Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, the two main disciples of Abu Hanifa.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference overriding qiyas in favor of custom or equity.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Zufar, if a man says 'from one to three', how many talaqs occur?
A) Zero.
B) One.
C) Two.
D) Three.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, ranged talaq expressions are subject to ijtihad among the founding imams, each with a valid basis in language, custom, or analogy.

Fractional Talaq Expressions: The Halves Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on fractional talaq expressions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the number of divorces when a man says 'three halves of one divorce' and state the proofs for each view.

Core Idea
When a fractional divorce is added to a whole, some complete it to the next integer; others treat each half as an independent unit.

This lesson examines a subtle issue in Hanafi divorce law: how many divorces occur when a man uses fractional expressions? The first expression, 'three halves of two divorces,' yields agreement on three divorces. However, 'three halves of one divorce' sparks an intra-Hanafi dispute. Understanding the two positions and their underlying reasoning is crucial for ruling on such cases.

Guided Path
1
Distinguish the two expressions
Identify the two verbal formulas: (1) 'three halves of two divorces' and (2) 'three halves of one divorce'. Note that the first is agreed upon; the second is disputed.
2
Recognize the agreed scenario
For the first expression, all Hanafi scholars hold that three divorces occur. Work through the math: half of two divorces is one divorce, so three halves make three divorces.
This is considered necessary (darurah).
3
Identify the disputed expression and the two views
For 'three halves of one divorce', two views are reported. View 1: two divorces occur. View 2: three divorces occur. Determine which view is attributed to which imam (though not explicitly named in the text).
View 1 is often attributed to Abu Yusuf or Muhammad; View 2 to Abu Hanifa.
4
Analyze the first proof (completion to integer)
Examine the reasoning for two divorces: three halves equal one and a half divorces. Since talaq does not accept fragmentation (la yaqbalu al-tajzi'), the half must be completed to a full divorce, yielding two divorces.
This relies on the principle that talaq is indivisible.
5
Analyze the second proof (independent units)
Examine the reasoning for three divorces: each half is an independent, complete unit in itself. Thus, three halves become three separate divorces directly.
This treats each half as a self-contained occurrence.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And if he said: 'You are three halves of two divorces,' three divorces occur necessarily. And if he said: 'You are three halves of one divorce,' it is said that two divorces occur because it is one and a half divorces, so it becomes complete. And it is said that three divorces occur because each half becomes complete in itself, thus becoming three. Translation: And if he said to his wife, 'You are the possessor of three halves of two divorces,' then this woman will be divorced with three divorces. Because half of two divorces is one divorce, so when three halves are gathered, they become three divorces. And if he said, 'You are the possessor of three halves of one divorce,' then it is said that two divorces occur because it is one and a half divorces, so the half becomes a complete divorce. And it is said that three divorces occur because each half becomes complete in itself, so three result. Explanation: The issue is that if a man says to his wife, 'You are divorced with three halves of two divorces,' then three divorces occur. The proof is that half of two divorces is one divorce, the second half is a second divorce, and the third half is a third divorce. Thus three divorces occur. And if he said, 'You are divorced with three halves of one divorce,' then some scholars opine that two divorces occur. The proof is that when three halves of one divorce are gathered, it becomes one and a half divorces, and since divorce does not accept fragmentation, that half is considered complete, so now two complete divorces occur. And some scholars opine that in this case three divorces occur because each half in itself is complete, and since there are three halves, three divorces occur.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the number of divorces that occur when a man uses expression involving halves. The first expression 'three halves of two divorces' is unambiguous: since half of two divorces is one divorce, three halves yield three divorces, and this is agreed upon. The second expression 'three halves of one divorce' is disputed. One view (attributed to some scholars, likely Abu Yusuf or Muhammad) holds that two divorces occur because the one divorce plus its half (which must be rounded up to a full divorce due to talaq not being divisible) makes two. Another view (attributed to Abu Hanifa) holds that each half is considered an independent occurrence, thus three halves become three separate divorces. The reasoning hinges on whether a fractional divorce can be completed to the next integer or whether each half operates as an independent unit. The text presents both proofs without explicit tarjih.

Key Terms
نصف (nisf): Half of a divorce; a fractional part of a single talaq.
تكامل (takāmul): Completion of a fractional divorce into a full divorce for legal effect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man says to his wife, 'You are three halves of two divorces,' how many divorces occur according to all Hanafi scholars?
A) One divorce
B) Two divorces
C) Three divorces
D) None

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, expressions of fractional talaq require careful analysis; the same phrase 'three halves of one divorce' can yield two or three divorces depending on the interpretive principle applied.
