Three Hanafi Views on 'From X to Y' in Divorce
Three-way Hanafi ikhtilaf on ghayah in divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions regarding divorce counts in 'from X to Y' expressions and explain the reasoning (dalil) behind each.

Core Idea
In divorce, 'from one to three' splits Hanafi imams: Abu Hanifa counts 2, Sahibayn count 3, Zufar counts 1.

When a husband says 'you are divorced from one to three,' how many divorces take effect? The answer varies even within the Hanafi school. This passage presents a three-way dispute among Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and Zufar, each relying on different methods: qiyas on sale, istihsan based on custom, and a nuanced view of the first endpoint. Understanding this dispute reveals how Hanafi scholars weigh analogy, custom, and the unique nature of divorce.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi positions
Identify the three positions: Abu Hanifa, Sahibayn, Zufar. For each, note the number of divorces in 'from one to two' and 'from one to three'.
Abu Hanifa: 1 and 2; Sahibayn: 2 and 3; Zufar: 0 and 1.
2
Identify the opponents' proofs
Zufar's proof: qiyas on sale where boundaries are excluded. Sahibayn's proof: istihsan based on custom where such phrases intend the whole set.
The source cites 'take from my wealth from one dirham to a hundred' as an example.
3
Analyze Abu Hanifa's response
Abu Hanifa distinguishes divorce from sale: in divorce the first endpoint must occur (be actualized) for the second to attach, whereas in sale the boundary exists before the contract. Custom in age statements shows intention of range, not inclusion of both extremes.
He also notes that the original principle in divorce is restriction (hazard?), so the first number is included only after it occurs.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: e.g., a husband says 'from one to three' – according to Abu Hanifa two divorces occur (revocable), Sahibayn three (irrevocable), Zufar one (revocable).
5
Assess the tarjih
The text does not explicitly choose, but presents Abu Hanifa first and in detail, indicating it may be the relied-upon view. Later Hanafi works often adopt Abu Hanifa's view.
Students should note that this is an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و لو قال انت طالق من واحدة الى ثنتين او مابين واحدة الى ثنتين فهي واحدة وان قال من واحدة الى ثلث اومابين واحدة الى ثلث فهى ثنتان وهذا عند ابي حنيفة وقالا في الاولى هي ثنتان و في الثانية ثلث وقال زفر فى الأولى لايقع شيء وفى الثانية تقع واحدة وهو القياس لان الغاية لاتدخل تحت المضروب له الغاية كما لوقال بعت منك من هذا الحائط الى هذا الحائط وجه قولهما وهو الاستحسان ان مثل هذا الكلام متى ذكر في العرف يراد به الکل كما تقول لغيرك خذمن مالی من درهم الى مائة ولابي حنيفة ان المراد به الاكثر من الاقل والاقل من الاكثر فانهم يقولون سنى من ستين الى سبعين وما بين ستين الى سبعين ويريدون به ما ذكرناه وارادة الكل فيما طريقه طريق الاباحة كما ذكر او الاصل في الطلاق هو الخطر ثم الغاية الاولى لابد ان تكون موجودة لترتب عليها الثانيه ووجودها بوقوعها بخلاف البيع لان الغاية فيه موجودة قبل البيع ولونوى واحدة يدين ديانة لاقضاء لانه محتمل كلامه لكنه خلاف الظاهر
And if he said: 'You are divorced from one to two' or 'between one and two,' then it is one (divorce). And if he said: 'from one to three' or 'between one and three,' then it is two. This is according to Abu Hanifa. And they (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said: in the first case it is two, and in the second case it is three. And Zufar said: in the first case nothing occurs, and in the second case one occurs, and this is qiyas because the endpoint does not enter under that for which the endpoint is set, just as if he said: 'I sold you from this wall to this wall.' The justification of their (Sahibayn's) saying, which is istihsan, is that such speech when mentioned in custom intends the whole, just as you say to another: 'Take from my wealth from one dirham to a hundred.' And for Abu Hanifa, the intended meaning is the greater from the lesser and the lesser from the greater, because they say: 'My age is from sixty to seventy' and 'between sixty and seventy' and they intend what we mentioned. And intending the whole is in matters that are permissible, as mentioned. And the original principle in divorce is restriction (or prohibition). Then the first endpoint must exist so that the second can be attached to it, and its existence is by its occurrence, unlike sale because the endpoint in it exists before the sale. And if he intended one, it is accepted in his internal belief but not in judgment because it is possible in his speech, but it is contrary to the apparent meaning.
Source pages p. 252

Commentary
This passage discusses a three-way ikhtilaf on the number of divorces when a phrase of the type 'from X to Y' is used. Abu Hanifa holds that only the starting number is counted and the ending number is excluded, so 'from one to two' gives one divorce (the 'one'), and 'from one to three' gives two divorces (the 'one' and the 'two', excluding 'three'). Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the entire range inclusive is intended, so 'from one to two' gives both one and two = two divorces, and 'from one to three' gives one, two, and three = three divorces. Zufar holds that in such expressions the endpoints are excluded entirely (like in sale of a boundary), so 'from one to two' yields no divorce (since one and two are endpoints, none falls within?), and 'from one to three' yields only the middle, i.e., two (= one divorce? Actually Zufar says in the second case one divorce occurs, meaning the number two alone). The text explains: Zufar's is qiyas upon the rule that the end (ghayah) is not included in that for which it is set, analogy with selling a wall boundary. Sahibayn's is istihsan based on common usage where such expressions intend the full set, e.g., 'take from my wealth from one dirham to a hundred' means the whole hundred. Abu Hanifa's proof is based on the common saying of ages: 'my age is from sixty to seventy' meaning the range, but the greater is intended from the lesser and the lesser from the greater; also, in divorce the original ruling is restriction (prohibition), so the first end must occur first to attach the second, and its occurrence is by actually falling (as a divorce), unlike sale where the boundary exists prior. The text ends noting that if he intended only one divorce, his intention is accepted religiously but not judicially because his speech is capable of that meaning but it is against the apparent (zahir), so the court takes the apparent meaning.

Key Terms
غاية (ghāyah): Endpoint; the limit stated in a phrase like 'from X to Y'.
قياس (qiyās): Analogical reasoning; here applied to divorce by analogy with sale.
استحسان (istiḥsān): Juristic preference; Sahibayn prefer custom over strict analogy.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a man says to his wife 'You are divorced from one to three,' how many divorces occur?
A) One
B) Two
C) Three
D) None

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the interpretation of 'from X to Y' in divorce depends on whether the endpoint is included; Abu Hanifa's view (excluding the last number) is often the relied-upon position.

Dispute on Divorce with Two Limits: Min Wahida Ila Thintayn
Explaining intra-Hanafi dispute on whether limits are included

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on divorce limits and apply Abu Hanifa's rule to determine the number of divorces.

Core Idea
In divorce, limits are interpreted restrictively; consecutive numbers intend the smaller, non-consecutive the larger.

When a husband says 'You are divorced from one to two' or 'from one to three', how many divorces occur? The answer is not straightforward, as the Hanafi masters differed. This lesson unpacks the reasoning of Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn, and Imam Zufar, and explains why Abu Hanifa's view is relied upon. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to interpret conditional and limited expressions in divorce.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario and positions
Identify the two cases: 'from one to two' and 'from one to three'. List the outcomes according to Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn, and Zufar.
2
Identify the four possibilities
The husband's speech has two limits (starting and ending). There are four logical possibilities: both included, both excluded, only starting included, only ending included. Map each imam to one possibility.
Abu Hanifa: starting included; Sahibayn: both included; Zufar: both excluded.
3
Understand each imam's dalil
Analyze the proofs: Zufar's qiyas on sale of land between two walls; Sahibayn's appeal to custom (urf) in permissive contexts; Abu Hanifa's distinction based on whether there is a number between the limits.
Abu Hanifa uses the rule 'al-akthar min al-aqall' or 'al-aqall min al-akthar' depending on the presence of an intermediate number.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response to opposing proofs
Study how the author of Hidayah refutes: to Sahibayn – custom applies to permissive contexts like gift, not restrictive divorce; to Zufar – in sale the limit pre-exists, in divorce it does not.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Conclude that Abu Hanifa's position is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) because it is most consistent with the original prohibition (hazr) in divorce.
Tarjih by Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

عدد ذكر كيے جائيں تو اس كی دو صورتيں ہيں: اگر درميان ميں كوئی عدد ہے تو اس سے مراد الأكثر من الأقل ہوگا، يعنی اقل عدد سے اوپر والا عدد مراد ہوگا۔ مثلاً من واحدة الى ثلث ميں غايتين كے درميان ايك كا عدد ہے، اور اس مثال ميں اقل عدد واحدہ ہے، اور اس سے اكثر يعنی اس سے اوپر ثنتين (دو) ہے تو يہ ہوا الأكثر من الأقل، لہذا اس صورت ميں دو طلاقيں واقع ہو جائيں گی۔ اور اگر درميان ميں كوئی عدد نہيں تو مراد الأقل من الأكثر ہوگا، يعنی اكثر سے كم مراد ہوگا۔ مثلاً من واحدة الى ثنتين ميں دونوں غايتوں كے درميان كوئی عدد نہيں تو اس صورت ميں الأقل من الأكثر مراد ہوگا، اور اكثر ثنتين كا عدد ہے اور اس سے كم ايك ہے، لہذا ايك كا عدد مراد ہوگا۔ صاحب ہدايہ فرما تے ہيں كہ لوگ اپنی عمر بتلاتے وقت كہتے ہيں "سنى من ستين الى سبعين" يا "ما بين ستين الى سبعين" اور اس سے مراد ان دونوں كے درميان كا عدد ہوتا ہے۔ اور ارادۃ الكل سے صاحبين كی دليل كا جواب ہے۔ حاصل جواب يہ كہ دو غايتيں ذكر كی جائيں تو كل كا ارادہ اباحت كے موقع پر كيا جاتا ہے، جيسے مثال مذكورہ "خذ من مالی من درهم الى مائة" ميں۔ اس ليے كہ اس مثال ميں سو درہم مخاطب كے ليے مباح كيا گيا ہے، جس قدر چاہے لے لے۔ اور طلاق ميں اصل ممانعت ہے۔ لہذا مسئلہ طلاق كو اس پر قياس كرنا قياس مع الفارق ہے۔ ثم الغاية الأولى سے امام زفر كی دليل كا جواب ہے۔ جواب كا حاصل يہ ہے كہ چونكہ غايت ثانيہ غايت اولی پر مرتب ہوتی ہے، اس ليے غايت اولی كا موجود رہنا ضروری ہے اور غايت اولی كا وجود اس كے وقوع سے ہوگا۔ اس ليے ہم كہتے ہيں كہ غايت اولی داخل ہوگی۔ امام زفر نے "بعت منك من هذا الحائط الى هذا الحائط" پر قياس كيا تھا، سو ہم كہتے ہيں كہ يہ قياس فاسد ہے، كيونكہ غايت مقيس عليہ ميں اس كو غايت بنانے سے پہلے موجود ہے، لہذا اس كو داخل كرنے كی كوئی ضرورت نہيں ہے۔ اور مختلف فيہ مسئلہ ميں غايت پہلے سے موجود نہيں، حالانكہ اس كا موجود ہونا ضروری ہے تا كہ اس پر غايت ثانيہ مرتب ہو سكے، اور اس كا وجود اس كے وقوع سے ہوگا، اس ليے غايت اولی داخل ہوگی۔ اور اگر من واحدة الى ثلاث ميں ايك طلاق كی نيت كی ہے تو ديانةً تصديق كی جائے گی نہ كہ قضاءً، كيونكہ ايك طلاق تو اس كے كلام كا محتمل ہے ليكن خلاف ظاہر ہے۔
There is a dispute between Abu Hanifa, the Sahibayn, and Imam Zufar: when a husband says 'You are divorced from one to two' or 'between one and two', how many divorces occur? According to Abu Hanifa, in the first case (from one to two) one divorce occurs, and in the second case (from one to three) two divorces occur. According to the Sahibayn, in the first case two and in the second case three divorces occur. Imam Zufar said: in the first case no divorce occurs, in the second case one divorce occurs. The source of the disagreement is that the husband's speech contains two limits (a starting limit and an ending limit). So either both limits are included in the thing limited, or both are excluded, or the starting limit is included and the ending limit is not, or the ending limit is included and the starting limit is not. The first view is held by the Sahibayn, the second by Imam Zufar, the third by Imam Abu Hanifa, and no one holds the fourth. The proof of Imam Zufar is that the limit of a thing is not included in what it limits, i.e., the limit is not included in the thing limited, because if it were included, it would not remain a limit. For example, if someone says 'I sold to you from this wall to that wall', both walls are not included in the sale. It is narrated that Imam Abu Hanifa argued with Imam Zufar about this: he asked Zufar how old he was, and Zufar replied 'between sixty and seventy'. Abu Hanifa said that this is 9 years. Zufar was stunned. The point was that if both limits are excluded, the starting limit is 60 and the ending limit is 70, leaving 9. The proof of the Sahibayn is that in common usage, such speech intends the whole. For example, if someone says 'Take from my wealth from one dirham to one hundred', he has the right to take all one hundred, not just 98. This shows both limits are included. The proof of Abu Hanifa is that when two numbers are mentioned as limits, two cases arise: if there is a number between them, the intended meaning is 'the greater from the lesser' (al-akthar min al-aqall), i.e., the number above the lesser; e.g., from one to three has one between, the lesser is one, greater is two, so two divorces occur. If there is no number between them, the intended meaning is 'the lesser from the greater' (al-aqall min al-akthar); e.g., from one to two has no number between, the greater is two, lesser is one, so one divorce occurs. The author of Hidayah says that when people state their age, they say 'my age from sixty to seventy' and mean the number between them. The answer to the Sahibayn's proof of intending the whole is that intending the whole occurs in a context of permission, like 'Take from my wealth from one to one hundred', where the amount is permissible. But in divorce, the original rule is prohibition (prevention). Therefore analogizing divorce to that is an invalid analogy. The answer to Imam Zufar's proof is that the second limit depends on the first limit, so the first limit must exist, and its existence is through its occurrence. Therefore the first limit is included. Zufar's analogy to 'I sold from this wall to that wall' is invalid because in that case the limit (wall) exists before being made a limit, so inclusion is unnecessary. But in the present case, the first limit does not pre-exist, and its existence is necessary for the second limit to be built upon it, so it must be included. If the husband intended one divorce in the case of 'from one to three', it is accepted diyanatan (as a matter of conscience) but not qada'an (in court), because it is possible but contrary to the apparent meaning.
Source pages p. 253

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute on how to interpret a divorce statement that specifies a range with two limits (e.g., 'from one to two' or 'between one and three'). The key question is whether the starting and ending numbers are included in the number of divorces that occur. The three positions are: (1) Abu Hanifa: for 'from one to two', one divorce occurs (since there is no number between them, the lesser from the greater is intended); for 'from one to three', two divorces occur (since there is a number between them, the greater from the lesser is intended). (2) Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): both limits are included, so 'from one to two' gives two, 'from one to three' gives three. (3) Zufar: both limits are excluded, so 'from one to two' gives none, 'from one to three' gives one. The dispute is rooted in the treatment of 'ghaya' (limit) in Arabic speech. Zufar argues by analogy to sale of a plot between two walls, where the walls are not sold. Abu Hanifa argues from common usage of age statements, and also that in divorce, due to the original prohibition (prevention of divorce), the range is interpreted most restrictively. The Sahibayn rely on general custom where such phrases imply the whole range. The author then answers both opposing proofs: the Sahibayn's proof from permissive contexts does not apply to divorce (which is prohibited), and Zufar's analogy fails because in the sale case the limit pre-exists, whereas in divorce the first limit does not exist until the utterance. The passage also notes that if the husband intended a different number than the apparent meaning, it is accepted diyanatan but not in court. This is a classic hanafi example of istihsan overriding qiyas.

Key Terms
غاية (ghāyah): The limit or boundary mentioned in a divorcing phrase, e.g., the starting number (ghāyah ibtidā') and the ending number (ghāyah intihā').
مغيا (mughtā): The thing limited, i.e., the range of numbers between the two limits.
الأكثر من الأقل (al-akthar min al-aqall): The greater from the lesser: when two limits are mentioned with a number between them, the intention is to take the number greater than the smaller limit.
الأقل من الأكثر (al-aqall min al-akthar): The lesser from the greater: when two limits are mentioned without a number between them, the intention is to take the number smaller than the larger limit.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Imam Abu Hanifa, how many divorces occur if a husband says 'You are divorced from one to three' (anta taliq min wahida ila thalath)?
A) One divorce
B) Two divorces
C) Three divorces
D) No divorce

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when a divorce statement uses two limits, the number of divorces is determined by whether there is an intermediate number: if there is, take the number above the smaller limit; if not, take the number below the larger limit, always favouring the minimum in line with the restrictive nature of divorce.

The Ruling on 'Anta Taliq Wahidatan Fi Thintayn' – One Divorce in Two
Ruling on divorce phrase with 'fi' meaning multiplication

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling for the divorce phrase 'anta taliq wahidatan fi thintayn' and explain the rational proof that multiplication of parts does not increase the number of divorces.

Core Idea
Multiplication of divorce parts does not multiply the divorces themselves.

When a husband uses ambiguous language in divorce, the default is to interpret it in the least burdensome way. This lesson examines the phrase 'you are divorced one in two' and why the Hanafi school holds that only one divorce occurs, even if multiplication is intended.

Guided Path
1
Identify the phrase and its possible meanings
Recognize the phrase 'anta taliq wahidatan fi thintayn' and consider possible intentions: multiplication (one times two) or addition (one and two).
The word 'fi' can mean 'in' or mathematically 'times'.
2
State the Hanafi majority position
According to Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn, only one divorce occurs, whether the husband intends multiplication or has no intention.
The ruling is based on the principle that multiplication operates on parts, not on the divorce itself.
3
Recognize the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Zufar and Hasan ibn Ziyad argue that two divorces occur, relying on the custom of calculation where 'one in two' equals two.
This is a legitimate ikhtilaf within the Hanafi school.
4
Analyze the Hanafi rational proof
The Hanafi proof is that multiplication (ḍarb) applies to the parts (ajzā') of the single divorce, not to the number of divorces. Multiplying parts does not create multiple divorces.
This is a linguistic and rational argument.
5
Apply the exception for addition intention
If the husband intends 'one and two' (addition), then three divorces occur because the phrase can bear that meaning.
The exception shows that intention matters when the language can support it.

Source Text

ولوقال انت طالق واحدة فى ثنتين و نوى الضرب والحساب اولم تكن له نية فهي واحدة وقال زفر تقع ثنتان لعرف الحساب وهو قول حسن بن زيادولنا ان عمل الضرب في تكثير الاجزاء لافي زيادة المضروب وتكثير اجزاء التطليقة لا يوجب تعددها فان نوى واحدة وثنتين فهى ثلث لانه يحتمله فان حرف
And if he says 'You are divorced one in two' and intends multiplication and calculation, or if he has no intention, then it is one. Zufar said: two occur, because of the custom of calculation. This is the saying of Hasan ibn Ziyad. Our proof is that the operation of multiplication is for multiplying parts, not for increasing the thing multiplied, and the multiplication of parts of a divorce does not necessitate its multiplicity. If he intends one and two, then it is three, because it is possible. The word 'fa' (then)...
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage addresses a specific phrasing: 'anta taliq wahidatan fi thintayn' (You are divorced one in two). The word 'fi' can mean 'in' or mathematically 'times'. According to the majority (including Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn), only one divorce occurs, even if the husband intends multiplication, because multiplication acts on the parts of the single divorce, not to produce multiple divorces. Imam Zufar and Hasan ibn Ziyad argue that two divorces occur, relying on the custom of calculation where 'one in two' equals two. The Hanafi position is that the phrase without context of calculation only means one divorce, and even with intention of multiplication, it does not multiply the number of divorces, only the parts or the severity. However, if the husband intends to combine 'one and two' (i.e., one plus two), then three divorces would occur, because the language can possibly bear that meaning. This illustrates the principle that the default in divorce is restriction, and ambiguous expressions are interpreted in the least burdensome way, unless a clear intention of a larger number is expressed.

Key Terms
ضرب (ḍarb): Multiplication or calculation; here it refers to arithmetic multiplication of the number of divorces.
اجزاء التطليقة (ajzā' al-taṭlīqah): Parts or components of a single divorce; multiplying these does not create multiple divorces.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a husband says 'You are divorced one in two' (anta taliq wahidatan fi thintayn) without any intention, how many divorces occur according to the Hanafi school?
A) One divorce
B) Two divorces
C) Three divorces
D) No divorce

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the phrase 'anta taliq wahidatan fi thintayn' results in one divorce regardless of multiplication intention, unless the husband intends addition ('one and two') which yields three.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Divorce via Numerical Formulae: One in Two vs. Two in Two
Detailed commentary on divorce formulae with numbers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on divorce formulae using 'fi' with numbers and evaluate the opposing view of Imam Zufar.

Core Idea
When a husband says 'one in two', multiplication operates on parts, not the divorce count—so one divorce stands.

This lesson unpacks a nuanced intra-Hanafi dispute regarding divorce formulae that include numbers and the preposition 'fi'. The core question: does saying 'you are divorced one in two' yield one divorce, two divorces, or something else? We will explore the Hanafi position, the opposing view of Imam Zufar and Hasan ibn Ziyad, and the rational proofs behind each stance.

Guided Path
1
Identify the formulae and the dispute
Recognize the two key formulae: 'wahidatan fi thintain' and 'thintain fi thintain'. The dispute centers on whether the preposition 'fi' implies multiplication, and if so, how many divorces result.
Imam Abu Hanifa says one divorce for the first, two for the second. Imam Zufar says two and three respectively.
2
Analyze the Hanafi proof: multiplication applies to parts
Understand the distinction: multiplication (darab) on physical objects multiplies the object itself; on non-physical entities like talaq, it multiplies only the parts (ajza). A single divorce with multiple parts remains one divorce.
Example: 'You are divorced one and a half and a third' still equals one divorce.
3
Examine Zufar's argument from custom and qiyas
Zufar relies on the custom of accountants (ahl al-hisab) who interpret such phrases as multiplication. He also uses qiyas to the sale of a wall (ba'tu min ha'it ila ha'it) where the first limit is included.
Zufar's qiyas: the first limit (one) must be included, leading to two divorces.
4
Understand the Hanafi response: qiyas is fasid
The Hanafi rebuttal: the qiyas is invalid because in the sale, the wall pre-exists; in divorce, the number one does not pre-exist—it is created by the utterance. Moreover, the custom of accountants is not decisive in divorce matters.
The response also notes that 'fi' can mean 'ma'a' (with) as in Quran 89:29, altering the meaning.
5
Apply to variants: different intentions and the second formula
If the husband intends 'one and two' (wahidatan wa thintain), three divorces occur. If he intends 'one with two' (ma'a), also three. If 'fi' is intended as a container (zarf), only one. For 'thintain fi thintain', the Hanafi view is two divorces; Zufar says three (two multiplied by two, capped at three).
The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's position.

Source Text

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد چہارم

اختیار ہے۔ اس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ دونوں غایتیں منیاء میں داخل ہیں۔
کتاب الطلاق
ابو حنیفہ کے قول کی وجہ یہ ہے کہ اگر غایتیں دو عدد ذکر کیئے جائیں تو اس کی دو صورتیں نہیں اسلئے کہ ان دونوں کے درمیان کوئی عدد ہو گا یا نہیں ۔ اگر درمیان میں کوئی عدد ہے تو اس سے مراد الا کثر من الاقل ہوگا۔ یعنی اقل عدد سے اوپر والا عد دمراد ہوگا۔ مثلا من واحدۃ الی ثلث میں غایتین کے درمیان ایک کا عدد ہے۔ اور اس مثال میں اقل عدد واحدۃ الی ثلث میں غایتین کے درمیان ایک کا عدد ہے۔ اور اس مثال میں اقل عدد واحدۃ ہے۔ اور اس سے اکثر یعنی اس سے او پر ثنتین (دو) ہے تو یہ نشین الاکثر من الاقل ہوا۔ لہذا اس صورت میں دو طلاقیں واقع ہو جائیں گی۔ اور اگر درمیان میں کوئی عدی نہیں تو مراد الاقل من الاکثر ہو گا۔ یعنی اکثر سے کم مراد ہوگا۔ مثلا من واحدة الیٰ ثنتین میں دونوں غائیتوں کے درمیان کوئی عدد نہیں تو اس صورت میں الاقل من الاکثر مراد ہوگا۔ اور اکثر ششمین کا عدد ہے اور اس سے کم ایک ہے۔ لہذا ایک کا عدد مراد ہوگا۔
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ لوگ اپنی عمر بتلاتے وقت کہتے ہیں سنی من سنتين الى سبعين يامـا بين ستين الى سبعين اور اس سے مراد ان دونوں کے درمیان کا عدد ہوتا ہے۔
وارادۃ الکل سے صاحبین کی دلیل کا جواب ہے . حاصل جواب یہ کہ دو غایتیں ذکر کی جائیں تو کل کا ارادہ اباحت کے موقع پر کیا جاتا ہے۔ جیسے مثلا مذکور خذ من مالی من درهم الى مائة میں۔ اسلئے کہ اس مثال میں سو درہم مخاطب کیلئے مباح کیا گیا ہے۔ جس قدر چاہے لے لے اور طلاق میں اصل ممانعت ہے۔ لہذا مسئلہ طلاق کو اس پر قیاس کرنا قیاس مع الفارق ہے۔
ثم الغاية الاولیٰ سے امام زفر کی دلیل کا جواب ہے۔ جواب کا حاصل رہے چونکہ غایت ثانیہ غایت اولی پر مرتب ہوتی ہے۔ اسلئے غایت اولی کا موجود رہنا ضروری ہے اور غایت اولی کا وجود اس کے وقوع سے ہوگا۔ اسلئے ہم کہتے ہیں کہ غایت اولی داخل ہوگی ۔ امام زفر نے بعت منك من هذا الحائط الى هذا الحائط پر قیاس کیا تھا۔ سو ہم کہتے ہیں کہ یہ قیاس فاسد ہے۔ کیونکہ غایت مقیس علیہ میں اس کو غایت بنانے سے پہلے موجود ہے۔ لہذا اس کو داخل کرنے کی کوئی ضروت نہیں ہے۔ اور مختلف فیہ مسئلہ میں غایت پہلے سے موجود نہیں ۔ حالانکہ اس کا موجود ہونا ضروری ہے تا کہ اس پر غایت ثانیہ مرتب ہو سکے۔ اور اس کا وجود اس کے وقوع سے ہوگا ۔ اس لئے غایت اولی داخل ہوگی۔ اور اگر من واحدۃ الی ثلاث میں ایک طلاق کی نیت کی ہے تو دیانہ تصدیق کی جائے گی نہ کہ قضاء ۔ کیونکہ ایک طلاق تو اس کے کلام کا متحمل تو ہے لیکن خلاف ظاہر ہے۔ اور یہ پہلے گزر چکا کہ جواحتمال خلاف ظاہر ہوتا ہے اس کا دیا نہ تو اعتبار ہوتا ہے مگر قضاء نہیں۔ واللہ اعلم انت واحدة في ثنتین کے الفاظ سے طلاق دی خواہ ضرب و حساب کی نیت
ہو یا نہیں کتنی طلاقیں واقع ہوں گی
ولوقال انت طالق واحدة فى ثنتين و نوى الضرب والحساب اولم تكن له نية فهي واحدة وقال زفر تقع ثنتان لعرف الحساب وهو قول حسن بن زيادولنا ان عمل الضرب في تكثير الاجزاء لافي زيادة المضروب وتكثير اجزاء التطليقة لا يوجب تعددها فان نوى واحدة وثنتين فهى ثلث لانه يحتمله فان حرف

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد چہارم
کتاب الطلاق الواو للجمع والظرف يجمع الى المظروف و لو كانت غير مدخول بهايقع واحدة كما في قوله واحدة و ثنتين و ان نوع واحدة مع ثنتين يقع الثلث لان كلمة فى تاتى بمعنى مع كمافي قوله تعالى فادخلی فی عبادى اى مع عبادى ولونوى الظرف يقع واحدة لان الطلاق لا صلح ظرفا فيلغو ذكر الثاني ولوقال اثنتين في اثنتين ونوى الضرب والحساب فهى ثنتان وعندزفر ثلث لان قضيته ان يكون اربعا لكن لا مزيد للطلاق وعندنا الاعتبار للمذكور الاول على ما بيناه
على
الثلث
ترجمہ اور اگر کہا انت طالق واحدة فى ثنتین اور ضرب و حساب کی نیت کی ۔ یا اسکی کوئی نیت نہیں ہے تو یہ ایک ہے اور امام زفر نے فرمایا کہ دو واقع ہوں گی حساب کرنے والوں کے عرف کی وجہ سے اور یہ قول حسن بن زیاد کا ہے۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ضرب کا عمل تکثیر اجزاء میں ہوتا ہے نہ کہ زیادتی مضروب ہیں۔ اور ایک طلاق کے اجزاء کی تکثیر تعدد طلاق کا موجب نہیں ہے۔ پس اگر نیت کی ایک اور دو کی تو یہ تین ( طلاق ) ہوں گی ۔ اسلئے کہ لفظ اس کا احتمال رکھتا ہے کیونکہ حرف واو جمع کیلئے ہے۔ اور ظرف مظروف کو جامع ہے۔ اور اگر ( وہ عورت ) غیر مدخول بہا ہے تو ایک ( طلاق واقع ہوگی۔ جیسا کہ اس کے قول واحدة و ثنتین میں ۔ اور اگر نیت کی ایک کی دو کے ساتھ تو تین ( طلاق ) واقع ہوں گی ۔ کیونکہ کلمہ فی مع کے معنی میں آتا ہے۔ جیسے باری تعالیٰ کا قول فادخلي في عبادي يعني مع عبادی ۔ اور اگر ظرف کی نیت کی تو ایک واقع ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ طلاق ظرف بنے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتی ہے۔ پس ثانی کا ذکر لغو ہوگا۔ اور اگر کہا دو میں اور ضرب و حساب کی نیت کی تو یہ دو ہیں۔ اور امام زفر کے نزدیک تین ہیں۔ کیونکہ ضرب کا تقاضا تو یہ تھا کہ چار ہوتیں ۔ لیکن طلاق تین سے زائد نہیں۔ اور ہمارے نزدیک اعتبار مذکور اول کا ہے اسی دلیل پر جو ہم نے بیان کیا ہے۔
تشریح لِعُرُفِ الْحُسَابِ میں ، حساب جمع کا صیغہ ہے۔ اور ضرب کہتے ہیں اجد العد دین کو دوگنا کرنا عدد آخر کی مقدار کے مطابق ۔
مثلاً آپ نے اربعة في الخمسة کہا تو میں ہوں گے۔ کیونکہ اربعہ کو پانچ مرتبہ دو گنا کیا گیا یا پانچ کو چار مرتبہ دوگنا کیا ہے۔ صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ مرد نے اپنی منکوحہ سے انت طالق واحدة في ثنتین کہا اور ضرب و حساب کی نیت کی یا کوئی نسبت نہیں کی ہے تو اس صورت میں ایک طلاق واقع ہو گی۔ اور امام زفر نے فرمایا کہ دو واقع ہوں گی۔ اور یہ حسن بن زیاد کا قول ہے۔ امام زفر کی دلیل حساب لگانے والوں کا عرف ہے۔ کیونکہ اس قسم کے کلام سے بالعموم ضرب ہی کا ارادہ کیا جاتا ہے۔ اور ایک کو دو میں ضرب دینے سے دو
طلاق ہوں گی ۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اشیاء کی دو قسمیں ہیں۔ ایک وہ جس کیلئے طول عرض اور عمیق تینوں ہوں ۔ جیسے اجسام اور دوسری وہ جس کیلئے یہ تینوں چیزیں ہوں۔ جیسے غیر محسوسات ۔ پس قسم اول میں ضرب دینے سے مشروب میں تکثیر ہوتی ہے اور قسم ثانی میں ضرب دینے سے اجزاء میں تکثیر ہوتی ہے نہ کہ مضروب میں۔ اور طلاق قسم ثانی سے ہے۔ لہذا انت طالق واحد فی ٹنتین کا مطلب ہوگا ایک طلاق دو جزوں والی۔ اور طلاق کے اجزاء کی تکثیر تعد وطلاق کا موجب نہیں ہے۔ پس اگر ایک طلاق کے متعدد اجزا ء کر کے طلاق دی جائے تو ایک ہی واقع ہوگی ۔ جیسے کسی نے کہا انت طالق طلقة و نصفها و ثلثها وربعها وسدسها و ثمنھا ۔اس صورت میں ایک ہی واقع ہو گی نہ کہ متعدد۔
اگر واحــدة في ثنتين سے واحدۃ و ثنتین کی نیت کی تو تین طلاقیں واقع ہو جائیں گی ۔ کیونکہ کلام اس کا احتمال رکھتا ہے۔
Ashraf al-Hidaya Urdu commentary on Hidayah, Volume 4. Page 253: [Previous discussion on two limits (ghayatayn)]. The Book of Divorce. The reason for Abu Hanifa's statement: If two limits are mentioned as numbers, there are two possibilities: either there is a number between them or not. If there is a number between them, then the intended meaning is the greater of the lesser (al-akthar min al-aqall), i.e., the number above the lesser. For example, from one to three, there is the number one between the two limits. In this example the lesser number is one, and the greater than it is two, so it is the greater of the lesser. Thus in this case two divorces occur. And if there is no number between them, then the intended meaning is the lesser of the greater (al-aqall min al-akthar), i.e., the number less than the greater. For example, from one to two, there is no number between the two limits, so in that case the lesser of the greater is intended. The greater number is two, and what is less than it is one. Hence one number is intended. The author of Hidayah says: People when stating their ages say 'I am from two to seventy years' or 'between sixty and seventy', and they intend the number between them. The response to the proof of the two companions (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding intending the whole (aradat al-kull) is: The answer is that when two limits are mentioned, intending the whole occurs in a context of permission (ibaha). For example, the mentioned example 'Take from my wealth from one dirham to one hundred.' In this example one hundred dirhams is made permissible for the addressee; he may take as much as he wishes. But in divorce the original principle is prohibition. Therefore analogizing the issue of divorce to this is a qiyas ma'a al-fariq (analogy with a difference). Then the response to the proof of Imam Zufar regarding the first limit (thumma al-ghayat al-ula): The gist of the answer is that since the second limit is dependent on the first limit, the existence of the first limit is necessary, and the existence of the first limit is through its occurrence. Therefore we say that the first limit is included. Imam Zufar analogized to 'I have sold to you from this wall to this wall.' So we say this analogy is invalid because in the analogized case, the limit exists before it is made a limit. Hence there is no need to include it. In the disputed case, the limit does not pre-exist, although its existence is necessary so that the second limit can be based on it, and its existence is through its occurrence. Hence the first limit is included. And if in 'from one to three' the intention is one divorce, then it will be accepted de dicto (diyanatan) but not de jure (qada'an), because one divorce is possible from his words but it is contrary to the apparent meaning. And it has passed earlier that a possibility contrary to the apparent meaning is considered de dicto but not de jure. And Allah knows best. [Regarding the phrase] 'You are divorced one in two', whether the intention is multiplication and calculation or not, how many divorces occur? And if he says 'You are divorced one in two' and intends multiplication and calculation, or he has no intention, then it is one. And Zufar said: Two occur due to the custom of accountants, and this is the statement of Hasan ibn Ziyad. Our proof is that the operation of multiplication is for multiplying parts (ajza), not for increasing the thing multiplied. Multiplying the parts of one divorce does not necessitate its multiplicity. For if he intends one and two, then it is three because it is possible: the letter waw is for conjunction, and the container (zarf) collects the contained. And if she is not consummated, then one occurs as in his statement 'one and two'. And if he intends one with two, then three occurs because the word 'fi' comes in the meaning of 'with' as in the Almighty's statement 'Enter into My servants' (fadkhuli fi 'ibadi), meaning 'with My servants'. And if he intends the container (zarf), then one occurs because divorce is not fit to be a container, so the mention of the second becomes void. And if he says 'two in two' and intends multiplication and calculation, then it is two. And according to Zufar it is three because its requirement would be four, but divorce does not exceed the limit. According to us, the consideration is for the first mentioned, as we have explained upon the third. Translation: And if he said 'You are divorced one in two' and intended multiplication and calculation, or he has no intention, then it is one. And Imam Zufar said: Two occur due to the custom of those who calculate, and this is the statement of Hasan ibn Ziyad. Our proof is that the operation of multiplication occurs in multiplying parts, not in increasing the things multiplied. Multiplying the parts of one divorce does not necessitate multiplicity of divorce. So if he intends one and two, then it is three divorces because the word can bear it: the letter waw is for conjunction, and the container collects the contained. And if the woman is non-consummated, then one divorce occurs as in his statement 'one and two'. And if he intends one with two, then three occur because the word 'fi' comes in the meaning of 'with', as in the Almighty's statement 'Enter into My servants' meaning 'with My servants'. And if he intends the container, then one occurs because divorce is not fit to be a container, so the mention of the second becomes void. And if he said 'two in two' and intended multiplication and calculation, then it is two. And according to Zufar it is three because the requirement of multiplication would be four, but divorce does not exceed three. And according to us, the consideration is given to the first mentioned, as we have explained. Clarification: In 'upon the custom of calculation', 'hisab' is the form of collection. And 'darab' (multiplication) means doubling two numbers according to the quantity of the other number. For example, if you say 'four in five', it becomes twenty because four is doubled five times or five is doubled four times. The scenario: A man said to his wife 'You are divorced one in two' and intended multiplication and calculation, or he had no intention, then in this case one divorce occurs. Imam Zufar said that two occur, and this is the statement of Hasan ibn Ziyad. Imam Zufar's proof is the custom of calculators because such speech generally intends multiplication. Multiplying one by two yields two divorces. Our proof is that things are of two types: one which has length, width, and depth, like bodies; and another which does not have these three things, like insensibles. In the first type, multiplication produces increase in the thing multiplied; in the second type, multiplication produces increase in parts, not in the thing multiplied. Divorce is of the second type. Therefore, 'You are divorced one in two' means one divorce with two parts. Moreover, multiplying the parts of divorce does not necessitate multiplicity of divorce. So if one divorces by making multiple parts of one divorce, only one occurs. For example, if someone says 'You are divorced one and a half and a third and a quarter and a sixth and an eighth', in this case only one occurs, not multiple. If from 'one in two' he intends 'one and two', then three divorces occur because the speech can bear it.
Source pages p. 254

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the interpretation of divorce formulae that include the word 'fi' (in) with numbers, particularly focusing on the number of divorces that occur. The author of Ashraf al-Hidayah is expanding upon the text of al-Hidayah, providing proofs and responses to opposing views.

The passage opens by discussing the general principle when two limits (ghayatayn) are mentioned—for example, 'from one to three' or 'from one to two'. If there is a number between the limits, the intention is the greater of the lesser; if there is no number between, the intention is the lesser of the greater. This part serves as background to the more specific dispute.

The core dispute is about a husband saying to his wife 'Ante Taliqun wahidatan fi thintain' (You are divorced one in two). The question is: how many divorces occur? According to Imam Abu Hanifa, it is one divorce, whether the husband intended multiplication (darab wa hisab) or had no intention. Imam Zufar (and Hasan ibn Ziyad) hold that it is two divorces, relying on the custom of accountants (ahl al-hisab) who would interpret such a phrase as multiplication: one multiplied by two equals two.

The Hanafi response is based on a distinction: multiplication operates differently on physical objects versus non-physical entities. For physical objects like bodies, multiplication increases the object itself. For non-physical entities like divorce, multiplication only multiplies the parts (ajza) of the singular divorce, not the divorce itself. Thus, one divorce with two parts is still one divorce. The author gives an example: if one says 'You are divorced one and a half and a third and a quarter...', it remains one divorce, not multiple.

The passage also addresses scenarios where the husband intends 'one and two' (wahidatan wa thintain). In that case, because the letter waw is for conjunction, it becomes three divorces if the woman is consummated. If she is non-consummated, it remains one divorce because the waw combines two numbers but for a non-consummated woman only one divorce can occur.

Additionally, if the husband intends 'one with two' (wahidatan ma'a thintain), using 'fi' in the sense of 'ma'a' (with), it also becomes three divorces, citing the Quranic verse 'fadkhuli fi 'ibadi' meaning 'with My servants'. If he intends the word 'fi' as a container (zarf), then only one divorce occurs because divorce cannot be a container, so the second number is void.

The passage further discusses the case of 'thintain fi thintain' (two in two). According to Abu Hanifa, two divorces occur if multiplication is intended. Imam Zufar says three, because two times two is four, but divorce is limited to three. The Hanafi view is that consideration is given to the first mentioned number (two), not the multiplication.

Thus, the passage is a detailed expansion of the Hidayah text, providing the Hanafi position, the opposing view of Zufar and Hasan ibn Ziyad, and the rational proofs based on the nature of multiplication and linguistic interpretation.

Key Terms
ضرب (darab): Multiplication; in this context, it means the arithmetic operation of multiplying two numbers, e.g., one multiplied by two.
حساب (hisab): Calculation; the custom of accountants (ahl al-hisab) who interpret phrases like 'one in two' as multiplication.
في (fi): A preposition that can mean 'in', 'into', 'with' (ma'a), or indicate multiplication depending on context. The text argues it can mean 'ma'a' as in Quran 89:29.
غاية (ghayah (pl. ghavat)): Limit or boundary; the first and last numbers in a phrase like 'from one to three'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man says to his wife 'Ante Taliqun wahidatan fi thintain' (You are divorced one in two) with no intention, how many divorces occur according to the Hanafi school?
A) One divorce
B) Two divorces
C) Three divorces
D) No divorce

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules one divorce for 'one in two' because multiplication in divorce affects only parts, not the count, and the custom of accountants is not decisive.

Talaq — Divorce
advanced
15 min
Ruling on Saying 'Anti Taliq Wahidatan Fi Ithnatayn' and Its Variants
Intra-Hanafi dispute on divorce numbers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the number of divorces resulting from different intentions when using the phrase 'anti taliq wahidatan fi ithnatayn' and its variants, and explain the Hanafi majority position against Imam Zufar's view.

Core Idea
The first number in divorce counts; multiplication only affects components, not the count.

The classical Hanafi jurists deeply analyzed the language of divorce to ensure precise legal outcomes. This passage examines a complex expression involving numbers and the word 'fi' (in). Depending on the husband's intention, a single phrase can yield one, two, or three divorces. Understanding how the Hanafi school navigates these nuances is essential for anyone involved in issuing fatwas on divorce.

Guided Path
1
Identify the expression and scenarios
The passage deals with the phrase 'anti taliq wahidatan fi ithnatayn' and its variants. Identify the different scenarios based on intention: no intention, multiplication, 'and', 'with', container, and the case of 'ithnatayn fi ithnatayn'.
Pay attention to the grammatical role of 'fi'.
2
Understand the Hanafi majority ruling for each intention
For each scenario, state the number of divorces according to the majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad). Note that for a consummated wife, 'and' or 'with' intention gives three; container intention gives one; multiplication intention gives one. For non-consummated, always one.
The first mentioned number controls except when 'fi' substitutes for 'waw'.
3
Recognize Imam Zufar's opposing view and his proof
Imam Zufar holds that with multiplication intention, two divorces occur for 'wahidatan fi ithnatayn' and three for 'ithnatayn fi ithnatayn'. His proof is the custom of mathematicians (urf al-hisab) where 'one in two' conventionally means two.
Hasan ibn Ziyad agrees with Zufar.
4
Analyze the Hanafi rebuttal using the analogy of physical vs non-physical multiplication
The Hanafi response distinguishes between physical objects (bodies) and non-physical legal constructs like divorce. In physical multiplication, the substance increases; in non-physical, only components increase. Thus, one divorce with multiple components remains one divorce.
The example of 'taliq talqatan wa nisfaha' illustrates this.
5
Apply the ruling to practice
Given a real-life scenario, determine the number of divorces according to the mufta bihi (majority) position. Consider whether the wife is consummated and the intention of the husband.
The practical consequence is whether reconciliation is possible.

الواو للجمع والظرف يجمع الى المظروف و لو كانت غير مدخول بهايقع واحدة كما في قوله واحدة و ثنتين و ان نوع واحدة مع ثنتين يقع الثلث لان كلمة فى تاتى بمعنى مع كمافي قوله تعالى فادخلی فی عبادى اى مع عبادى ولونوى الظرف يقع واحدة لان الطلاق لا صلح ظرفا فيلغو ذكر الثاني ولوقال اثنتين في اثنتين ونوى الضرب والحساب فهى ثنتان وعندزفر ثلث لان قضيته ان يكون اربعا لكن لا مزيد للطلاق وعندنا الاعتبار للمذكور الاول على ما بيناه

ترجمہ اور اگر کہا انت طالق واحدة فى ثنتین اور ضرب و حساب کی نیت کی ۔ یا اسکی کوئی نیت نہیں ہے تو یہ ایک ہے اور امام زفر نے فرمایا کہ دو واقع ہوں گی حساب کرنے والوں کے عرف کی وجہ سے اور یہ قول حسن بن زیاد کا ہے۔ اور ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ ضرب کا عمل تکثیر اجزاء میں ہوتا ہے نہ کہ زیادتی مضروب ہیں۔ اور ایک طلاق کے اجزاء کی تکثیر تعدد طلاق کا موجب نہیں ہے۔ پس اگر نیت کی ایک اور دو کی تو یہ تین ( طلاق ) ہوں گی ۔ اسلئے کہ لفظ اس کا احتمال رکھتا ہے کیونکہ حرف واو جمع کیلئے ہے۔ اور ظرف مظروف کو جامع ہے۔ اور اگر ( وہ عورت ) غیر مدخول بہا ہے تو ایک ( طلاق واقع ہوگی۔ جیسا کہ اس کے قول واحدة و ثنتین میں ۔ اور اگر نیت کی ایک کی دو کے ساتھ تو تین ( طلاق ) واقع ہوں گی ۔ کیونکہ کلمہ فی مع کے معنی میں آتا ہے۔ جیسے باری تعالیٰ کا قول فادخلي في عبادي يعني مع عبادی ۔ اور اگر ظرف کی نیت کی تو ایک واقع ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ طلاق ظرف بنے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتی ہے۔ پس ثانی کا ذکر لغو ہوگا۔ اور اگر کہا دو میں اور ضرب و حساب کی نیت کی تو یہ دو ہیں۔ اور امام زفر کے نزدیک تین ہیں۔ کیونکہ ضرب کا تقاضا تو یہ تھا کہ چار ہوتیں ۔ لیکن طلاق تین سے زائد نہیں۔ اور ہمارے نزدیک اعتبار مذکور اول کا ہے اسی دلیل پر جو ہم نے بیان کیا ہے۔

تشریح لِعُرُفِ الْحُسَابِ میں ، حساب جمع کا صیغہ ہے۔ اور ضرب کہتے ہیں اجد العد دین کو دوگنا کرنا عدد آخر کی مقدار کے مطابق ۔
مثلاً آپ نے اربعة في الخمسة کہا تو میں ہوں گے۔ کیونکہ اربعہ کو پانچ مرتبہ دو گنا کیا گیا یا پانچ کو چار مرتبہ دوگنا کیا ہے۔ صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ مرد نے اپنی منکوحہ سے انت طالق واحدة في ثنتین کہا اور ضرب و حساب کی نیت کی یا کوئی نسبت نہیں کی ہے تو اس صورت میں ایک طلاق واقع ہو گی۔ اور امام زفر نے فرمایا کہ دو واقع ہوں گی۔ اور یہ حسن بن زیاد کا قول ہے۔ امام زفر کی دلیل حساب لگانے والوں کا عرف ہے۔ کیونکہ اس قسم کے کلام سے بالعموم ضرب ہی کا ارادہ کیا جاتا ہے۔ اور ایک کو دو میں ضرب دینے سے دو طلاق ہوں گی ۔ ہماری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اشیاء کی دو قسمیں ہیں۔ ایک وہ جس کیلئے طول عرض اور عمیق تینوں ہوں ۔ جیسے اجسام اور دوسری وہ جس کیلئے یہ تینوں چیزیں ہوں۔ جیسے غیر محسوسات ۔ پس قسم اول میں ضرب دینے سے مشروب میں تکثیر ہوتی ہے اور قسم ثانی میں ضرب دینے سے اجزاء میں تکثیر ہوتی ہے نہ کہ مضروب میں۔ اور طلاق قسم ثانی سے ہے۔ لہذا انت طالق واحد فی ٹنتین کا مطلب ہوگا ایک طلاق دو جزوں والی۔ اور طلاق کے اجزاء کی تکثیر تعد وطلاق کا موجب نہیں ہے۔ پس اگر ایک طلاق کے متعدد اجزا ء کر کے طلاق دی جائے تو ایک ہی واقع ہوگی ۔ جیسے کسی نے کہا انت طالق طلقة و نصفها و ثلثها وربعها وسدسها و ثمنھا ۔اس صورت میں ایک ہی واقع ہو گی نہ کہ متعدد۔

اگر واحــدة في ثنتين سے واحدۃ و ثنتین کی نیت کی تو تین طلاقیں واقع ہو جائیں گی ۔ کیونکہ کلام اس کا احتمال رکھتا ہے۔

تشریح کیونکہ جس طرح و او جمعیت کیلئے آتا ہے۔ اسی طرح ظرف بھی مظروف کیلئے جامع ہے۔ بیس و او اور فی میں ایک گونہ اتصال پویا آگیا ۔ اس وجہ سے فی بول کر و او مراد لینے میں کوئی حرج نہیں۔ یہ حکم مدخول بہا عورت کا ہے۔ ورنہ اگر غیر مدخول بہا ہو تو صرف ایک واقع ہو کہ بصراحت واحدۃ اور تختین کہنے کی صورت میں ایک طلاق واقع ہوتی ہے۔

اور اگر واحدة في ثنتین سے مع ثنتین کی نسبت کی ہے تو تین طلاقیں واقع ہو جائیں گی ۔ کیونکہ لفظ فی جمع کے معنی میں مستعمل ہے۔ جیسے فادخلي في عباديين مع عبادی

اور اگر واحدة في ثنتین سے ظرف کی نیت کی ہے تو صرف ایک طلاق واقع ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ طلاق غیہ کیلئے ظرف بننے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتی ہے۔ لہذا الفظ ثانی یعنی فی ثنتین کا ذکر لغو ہوگا۔ اور واحدۃ سے ایک طلاق واقع ہوگی ۔

اور اگر کہا اثنتین فی اثنتین اور ضرب و حساب کی نیت کی ہے تو دو واقع ہوں گی اور امام زفر کے نزدیک نان و نا ہوں گی ۔ امام زق کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ضرب کا تقاضا تو یہ تھا کہ چار طلاق واقع ہوتیں۔ لیکن چونکہ تین سے زائد طلاق نہیں اسلئے تین واقع ہو جائیں گی۔ او ہمارے نزدیک سابقہ دلیل کی وجہ سے مذکور اول معتبر ہے۔
The waw for conjunction and the container combines with the contained. And if she is not consummated, one occurs, as in his saying: one and two. And if he intends one with two, three occur, because the word 'fi' comes in the meaning of 'with', as in Allah's saying: 'Enter among My servants', i.e., with My servants. And if he intends container, one occurs, because divorce cannot serve as a container, so the second mention becomes void. And if he says 'two in two' and intends multiplication and calculation, then it is two. According to Zufar, three, because its requirement would be four, but there is no increase in divorce beyond three. According to us, the consideration is for the first mentioned, as we have explained. Translation: And if he said 'anti taliq wahidatan fi ithnatayn' and intended multiplication and calculation, or had no intention, then it is one. Imam Zufar said two occur due to the custom of calculators, and this is the saying of Hasan ibn Ziyad. Our proof is that the operation of multiplication increases components, not the multiplicand. And increasing the components of one divorce does not cause multiplicity of divorce. So if he intended one and two, then three (divorces) occur because the word is capable of that, since the letter waw is for conjunction and the container encompasses the contained. And if (the woman) is non-consummated, then one occurs, as in his saying 'one and two'. And if he intended one with two, then three (divorces) occur, because the word 'fi' is used in the meaning of 'with', as in Allah's saying 'Enter among My servants' meaning 'with My servants'. And if he intended container, then one occurs, since divorce is not fit to be a container, so the second mention becomes void. And if he said 'two in two' and intended multiplication and calculation, then it is two, and according to Imam Zufar three, because multiplication would require four, but divorce does not exceed three. And according to us, consideration is for the first mentioned, based on the proof we have explained. Elaboration: In 'urf al-hisab', 'hisab' is the plural form. Multiplication means doubling the two numbers according to the quantity of the other number. For example, if you say 'four in five', then twenty, because four is doubled five times or five is doubled four times. The case is that a man said to his wife 'anti taliq wahidatan fi ithnatayn' and intended multiplication and calculation, or had no intention, then in this case one divorce occurs. Imam Zufar said two occur, and this is the saying of Hasan ibn Ziyad. Imam Zufar's proof is the custom of calculators, because from this type of speech generally multiplication is intended, and multiplying one by two gives two divorces. Our proof is that things are of two types: one for which length, width, and depth all exist, like bodies; and the other for which these three things do not exist, like insensibles. In the first type, multiplication increases the substance, and in the second type, multiplication increases components, not the multiplicand. Divorce is of the second type. So 'anti taliq wahidatan fi ithnatayn' means one divorce with two parts. And increasing the components of divorce does not cause multiplicity of divorce. So if one divorce is given with multiple components, only one occurs. For example, if someone says 'anti taliq talqatan wa nisfaha wa thulthaha wa rub'aha wa sudusaha wa thumnaha', in this case only one occurs, not multiple. If from 'wahidatan fi ithnatayn' he intends 'one and two', then three divorces occur, because the speech is capable of that. Elaboration: Since just as waw is for conjunction, similarly the container encompasses the contained. Between waw and 'fi' a connection is found, so by saying 'fi' intending waw is not objectionable. This ruling is for the consummated woman. If she is non-consummated, only one occurs, as in saying explicitly 'one and two'. And if from 'wahidatan fi ithnatayn' he intends 'with two', then three divorces occur, because 'fi' is used in the meaning of conjunction, as in 'Enter among My servants: with My servants'. And if from 'wahidatan fi ithnatayn' he intends container, then only one divorce occurs, because divorce is not capable of being a container, so the second word becomes void. And if he says 'two in two' and intended multiplication and calculation, then two occur, and according to Imam Zufar three. Imam Zufar's proof is that multiplication requires four, but since divorce does not exceed three, three occur. According to us, based on the previous proof, the first mentioned is authoritative.
Source pages p. 255

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about the effect of the expression 'anti taliq wahidatan fi ithnatayn' (you are divorced one in two). The core issue is whether the word 'fi' (in) when used with numbers and the intention of multiplication (darb) results in multiple divorces. The Hanafi majority (Imam Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad al-Shaybani) hold that only one divorce occurs, because multiplication in the context of divorce (which is a legal construct, not a physical object) affects the components of one divorce, not the count. Imam Zufar disagrees, arguing based on the custom of mathematicians (urf al-hisab) that saying 'one in two' with intention of multiplication should yield two divorces. The text also discusses variations: if the husband intends 'one and two' (wahidah wa ithnatayn) it becomes three divorces if the wife is consummated, because the word 'fi' can substitute for 'waw' (and) in this construction. If he intends 'with two', it also becomes three divorced based on the Quranic usage of 'fi' meaning 'with'. If he intends a container (zarf) meaning 'one divorce contained within the period of two', it remains one divorce because divorce cannot be a container. For a non-consummated wife, only one divorce occurs regardless. The text also covers the case of saying 'two in two' (ithnatayn fi ithnatayn) with multiplication intention: Hanafi says two divorces, Zufar says three (because multiplication would give four but max is three). The Hanafi reasoning is that the first number mentioned controls.

Key Terms
ضرب (darb): Multiplication; here, the linguistic intention when saying a number in relation to another, meaning raising to a power or multiplying.
حساب (hisab): Calculation; the custom of mathematicians (urf al-hisab) is used by Zufar as a proof.
ظرف (zarf): Container; a grammatical term meaning a particle or construction indicating the container or time of an action.
مظروف (mazruf): Contained; that which is placed in a container.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man says to his consummated wife 'anti taliq wahidatan fi ithnatayn' with the intention of multiplication (darb), how many divorces occur according to the Hanafi majority?
A) One divorce because components are multiplied but not the count.
B) Two divorces because one multiplied by two equals two.
C) Three divorces because the maximum is three.
D) No divorce because the expression is ambiguous.

Key Takeaway
The first number controls divorce count; 'fi' with multiplication intention yields one divorce in Hanafi law.

Talaq — Divorce

Spatial Restriction in Talaq: Raj'i vs Ba'in
Dispute between Hanafi and Zufar on talaq type

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi position that a spatial restriction in a divorce pronouncement yields a revocable divorce, and contrast it with Imam Zufar's view that such a phrase implies irrevocability.

Core Idea
A spatial restriction shortens the divorce effect, making it raj'i.

When a husband says 'You are divorced from here to Syria,' a dispute arises: does mentioning a distant place extend the divorce (making it ba'in) or restrict it (making it raj'i)? This lesson unpacks the reasoning of the Hanafi majority and Imam Zufar, focusing on the concepts of tul (length) and qasr (shortening).

Guided Path
1
Identify the pronouncement
Read the exact phrase: 'anti taliq min huna ila al-sham'. Note that it includes a spatial boundary ('min huna ila al-sham').
2
Contrast the two interpretations
The Hanafi majority interprets the boundary as a limitation (qasr), while Zufar interprets it as an extension (tul). Understand how each derives the ruling.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
If the phrase were simply 'anti taliq', it would apply everywhere. Adding 'ila al-sham' restricts the effect, showing the intent to shorten, not strengthen.
4
Evaluate the practical consequence
The difference: under Hanafi, the husband can revoke the divorce during iddah. Under Zufar, he cannot—marriage ends immediately.
This is the thamarah al-khilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولوقال انت طالق من ههنا الى الشام فهى واحدة يملك الرجمع وقال زفر هی بائنة لانه وصف الطلاق بالطول قلنا لابل وصفه بالقصر لانه متى وقع وقع في الاماكن كلها

ترجمہ اور اگر کہا کہ تو طلاق والی ہے یہاں سے (ملک) شام تک تو یہ ایک ہے رجعت کا مالک ہوگا۔ اور کہا امام زفر نے کہ یہ بائنہ ہے۔ کیونکہ طلاق کو وصعف طول کے ساتھ متصف کیا ہے۔ ہم جواب دیں گے کہ نہیں بلکہ اسکو متصف کیا ہے قصر ( کوتاہ کرنے کے ) ساتھ اسلئے کہ جب واقع ہوگی تو تمام مکانوں میں واقع ہوگی ۔

تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر مرد نے اپنی منکوحہ سے انت طالق من ههنا الى الشام کہا تو ہمارے نزدیک طلاق رجعی واقع ہو گی ۔ اور امام زفر کے نزدیک طلاق بائن واقع ہوگی۔ امام زفر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ طلاق کو ونصف طول کے ساتھ متصف کیا گیا ہے۔ اور طول کا استعمال قوت کے معنی میں ہوتا ہے اور قوت کا اظہار طلاق بائن میں ہوگا نہ کہ رجعی میں۔ اسلئے طلاق بائن واقع ہو گی۔ ہماری طرف سے کہا گیا کہ ایسا نہیں جیسا کہ امام زفر نے فرمایا بلکہ ملک شام کی قید لگا کر اس شخص نے طلاق کو کوتاہ کر دیا۔ کیونکہ اگر شخص انت طالق کہتا اور الی الشام ذکر نہ کرتا تو دنیا اور آسمان ہر جگہ میں طلاق واقع ہوتی ۔ پس جب الی الشام ذکر کیا تو گویا اس نے ایک محدود مکان میں طلاق کو خاص کر دیا۔ لہذا یہ کہنا کہ طلاق کو وصف طول کے ساتھ متصف کر دیا ہے درست نہیں ۔
And if he said 'You are divorced from here to Syria', then it is one (revocable) and he has the right to take back. Zufar said it is irrevocable, because he described the divorce with length. We say: rather, he described it with shortness, because when it occurs, it occurs in all places. Translation: And if he said 'you are divorced from here to Syria', then it is one, he has the right to take back. Imam Zufar said it is irrevocable, because he described the divorce with length. We reply: no, rather he described it with shortness, because when it occurs, it occurs in all places. Elaboration: The case is that if a man says to his wife 'anti taliq min huna ila al-sham', according to us a revocable divorce occurs. According to Imam Zufar an irrevocable divorce occurs. Imam Zufar's proof is that divorce is described with length, and length is used in the meaning of strength, and strength is manifested in an irrevocable divorce not in a revocable one. It is said on our behalf: This is not as Imam Zufar said; rather, by imposing the condition of the land of Syria, the person shortened the divorce. Because if the person says 'you are divorced' and does not mention 'to Syria', the divorce would occur everywhere in the earth and sky. So when he mentions 'to Syria', it is as if he restricted the divorce to a limited place. Therefore, saying that he described the divorce with length is not correct.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute within the Hanafi school between the majority (Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn) and Imam Zufar regarding the effect of saying 'you are divorced from here to Syria'. The Hanafi position is that this results in one revocable (raj'i) divorce because the phrase actually restricts the divorce to a specific place (Syria), thereby shortening its scope. Imam Zufar argues that it is an irrevocable (ba'in) divorce because the mention of a spatial limit describes the divorce with 'length' (tul), implying strength and finality. The Hanafi response is that if the man had not mentioned Syria, the divorce would apply everywhere; mentioning Syria restricts it, so it is a shortening (qasr), not an extension. Hence, it remains raj'i.

Key Terms
رجعی (raj'i): Revocable divorce; the husband can take back the wife during the waiting period without a new marriage.
بائن (ba'in): Irrevocable divorce; the marriage is immediately ended and the husband cannot take back except with a new marriage.
طول (tul): Length; here in the sense of extension or strength, used by Zufar as proof for ba'in.
قصر (qasr): Shortening; the Hanafi claim that the phrase actually shortens the scope of the divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad), what type of divorce occurs when a man tells his wife 'anti taliq min huna ila al-sham'?
A) Ba'in (irrevocable) because the phrase implies strength.
B) Raj'i (revocable) because the phrase restricts the divorce to a certain place.
C) Three divorces because 'ila al-sham' implies all places.
D) No divorce because the phrase is ambiguous.

Key Takeaway
Spatial restrictions in talaq pronouncements indicate qasr (shortening), resulting in a revocable divorce rather than an irrevocable one.

Talaq — Divorce

Ruling on 'One in Two' and 'Two in Two' Divorce Phrases
Ruling on number of divorces when using 'fi' with numerals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the different interpretations of 'fi' in divorce phrases and apply the correct number of divorces based on the husband's intent, following the Hanafi school's ruling.

Core Idea
The meaning of 'fi' in divorce phrases determines the number of divorces: association gives three, container gives one; 'two in two' with multiplication intent gives two divorces.

The word 'fi' (في) can function as a preposition indicating a container (zarf) or a conjunction (like 'waw') meaning association. When used in talaq phrases like 'one in two' or 'two in two', the intended meaning drastically changes the number of divorces that occur. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling for consummated and non-consummated wives, and examines the intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Muhammad and Imam Zufar on the interpretation of multiplication in 'two in two'.

Guided Path
1
Determine the wife's status
First, check if the wife is consummated (madhkhul biha) or not. The ruling for 'one in two' differs: for a non-consummated wife, only one divorce occurs regardless of intent because she cannot be divorced with three unless explicitly stated.
The passage explicitly states that the ruling applies to a consummated wife; otherwise, only one divorce.
2
Interpret the husband's intent for 'one in two'
If the husband says 'one in two' and intends association (joining 'one' with 'two'), then three divorces occur because 'fi' is used in the sense of conjunction, like the Quranic verse 'Enter among My servants.' If he intends container (zarf), then the phrase is nonsensical (divorce cannot contain something), so only one divorce occurs from 'one'.
The Quranic proof is cited: فادخلي في عباديين (Enter among My servants) where 'fi' means 'among'.
3
Interpret the husband's intent for 'two in two'
If the husband says 'two in two' intending multiplication (darb), the Hanafi position is that two divorces occur. This is because the literal multiplication would give four, but the intended meaning is simply to refer to the number two, not to perform arithmetic.
Imam Zufar (within the Hanafi school) disagrees, arguing that multiplication requires four but capped at three, so three occur.
4
Apply the mufta bihi position
The relied-upon (mufta bihi) position is that for 'two in two' with multiplication intent, two divorces occur. The commentator favors this view based on the previous proof that 'fi' does not necessarily imply multiplication.
This position is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is the authoritative view for fatwa.
5
Note the practical consequence
The thamarah al-khilaf: if two divorces occur, the husband can take his wife back during the 'iddah; if three occur, she becomes irrevocably divorced and cannot remarry him without a halala.
This highlights the importance of correctly determining the husband's intent.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کیونکہ جس طرح و او جمعیت کیلئے آتا ہے۔ اسی طرح ظرف بھی مظروف کیلئے جامع ہے۔ بیس و او اور فی میں ایک گونہ اتصال پویا آگیا ۔ اس وجہ سے فی بول کر و او مراد لینے میں کوئی حرج نہیں۔ یہ حکم مدخول بہا عورت کا ہے۔ ورنہ اگر غیر مدخول بہا ہو تو صرف ایک واقع ہو کہ بصراحت واحدۃ اور تختین کہنے کی صورت میں ایک طلاق واقع ہوتی ہے۔ اور اگر واحدة في ثنتین سے مع ثنتین کی نسبت کی ہے تو تین طلاقیں واقع ہو جائیں گی ۔ کیونکہ لفظ فی جمع کے معنی میں مستعمل ہے۔ جیسے فادخلي في عباديين مع عبادی اور اگر واحدة في ثنتین سے ظرف کی نیت کی ہے تو صرف ایک طلاق واقع ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ طلاق غیہ کیلئے ظرف بننے کی صلاحیت نہیں رکھتی ہے۔ لہذا الفظ ثانی یعنی فی ثنتین کا ذکر لغو ہوگا۔ اور واحدۃ سے ایک طلاق واقع ہوگی ۔ اور اگر کہا اثنتین فی اثنتین اور ضرب و حساب کی نیت کی ہے تو دو واقع ہوں گی اور امام زفر کے نزدیک نان و نا ہوں گی ۔ امام زق کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ ضرب کا تقاضا تو یہ تھا کہ چار طلاق واقع ہوتیں۔ لیکن چونکہ تین سے زائد طلاق نہیں اسلئے تین واقع ہو جائیں گی۔ او ہمارے نزدیک سابقہ دلیل کی وجہ سے مذکور اول معتبر ہے۔
Because just as 'waw' is used for conjunction, similarly a container (zarf) encompasses its content. Between 'ba' and 'waw' and 'fi' there is a kind of connection. Therefore, saying 'fi' and intending 'waw' is not problematic. This ruling is for a woman who has been consummated. Otherwise, if she is not consummated, only one divorce occurs when explicitly saying 'one' and specifying 'two' in that manner. And if one says 'one in two' intending association with two, then three divorces occur, because the word 'fi' is used in the sense of conjunction, like 'Enter among My servants.' And if one intends 'in' (container) from 'one in two', then only one divorce occurs, because divorce does not have the capacity to be a container for something. Therefore, the second phrase 'fi two' becomes superfluous, and one divorce occurs from 'one'. And if one says 'two in two' and intends multiplication and calculation, then two occur, and according to Imam Zufar, three occur. Imam Zufar's proof is that multiplication would require four divorces, but since more than three are not possible, three occur. And according to us, due to the previous proof, the first mentioned is considered.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage explains the effect of the word 'fi' when used in divorce phrases like 'one in two' or 'two in two'. The commentator first clarifies that 'fi' can sometimes imply association ('waw') or container (zarf). For a consummated wife, if the husband says 'one in two' intending association with two, three divorces occur because 'fi' in that context means 'with, as in the Quranic verse 'Enter among My servants.' If he intends 'in' as a container, the phrase is meaningless because divorce cannot contain something, so only one divorce occurs from 'one'. For 'two in two' with intent of multiplication, the Hanafi position is that two divorces occur, while Imam Zufar argues that multiplication would give four but capped at three, so three occur. The commentator sides with the Hanafi position that only two occur, because the intended multiplication is literal and not overridden by the cap.

Key Terms
ظرف (zarf): A container or location; in this context, the word 'في' used to indicate a physical container or location for something.
ضرب (darb): Multiplication; in the phrase 'اثنتین فی اثنتین', if one intends arithmetic multiplication, it could imply 2×2=4 divorces.
مدخول بہا (madhkhul biha): A wife with whom the husband has consummated the marriage; different rulings apply to her vs. non-consummated wife.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) One divorce
B) Two divorces
C) Three divorces
D) No divorce

Key Takeaway
The number of divorces depends on the intended meaning of 'fi': association yields three, container yields one; for 'two in two' with multiplication, two divorces are effective according to the Hanafi position.

Divorce from Here to Sham: Raj'i or Ba'in?
Intra-Hanafi dispute on spatial limitation effect on divorce type

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school rules that a spatially limited divorce is revocable (raj'i) and evaluate Imam Zufar's counter-argument for irrevocability (ba'in).

Core Idea
Specifying a place limits divorce, making it revocable; strength is not in distance but in unrestricted scope.

When a husband says to his wife 'You are divorced from here to Sham,' does the mention of a distant land strengthen the divorce or restrict it? The Hanafi school and Imam Zufar offer opposite answers. This lesson unpacks the linguistic and legal reasoning behind each position and shows how the same phrase can yield radically different rulings depending on how you interpret the intent.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling given in the matn: the divorce is one revocable (raj'i) divorce, meaning the husband may take her back during the waiting period.
The base text clearly states raj'i.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
Note that Imam Zufar (within the Hanafi school) disagrees, holding that it is irrevocable (ba'in). Recognize that intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf is valid and recognized in our tradition.
Imam Zufar is a major Hanafi scholar; his views are recorded in the nawadir.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand Imam Zufar's reasoning: 'to Sham' implies length (tul), which suggests strength, and strength is a quality of irrevocable divorce (ba'in).
He interprets the spatial extent as an attribute of power.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
See how the Hanafi school rebuts: the specification actually restricts the divorce to a limited area; without the limit it would occur everywhere. Hence it is a description of restriction (qasr), not extension.
The key insight: mentioning 'Sham' confines, not expands, the effect.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Appreciate the practical difference: under the Hanafi ruling, the husband can revoke during 'iddah; under Zufar's, the wife is immediately separate and a new marriage is required.
This is the real-world consequence that makes the dispute matter.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولوقال انت طالق من ههنا الى الشام فهى واحدة يملك الرجمع وقال زفر هی بائنة لانه وصف الطلاق بالطول قلنا لابل وصفه بالقصر لانه متى وقع وقع في الاماكن كلها ترجمہ اور اگر کہا کہ تو طلاق والی ہے یہاں سے (ملک) شام تک تو یہ ایک ہے رجعت کا مالک ہوگا۔ اور کہا امام زفر نے کہ یہ بائنہ ہے۔ کیونکہ طلاق کو وصعف طول کے ساتھ متصف کیا ہے۔ ہم جواب دیں گے کہ نہیں بلکہ اسکو متصف کیا ہے قصر ( کوتاہ کرنے کے ) ساتھ اسلئے کہ جب واقع ہوگی تو تمام مکانوں میں واقع ہوگی ۔ تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر مرد نے اپنی منکوحہ سے انت طالق من ههنا الى الشام کہا تو ہمارے نزدیک طلاق رجعی واقع ہو گی ۔ اور امام زفر کے نزدیک طلاق بائن واقع ہوگی۔ امام زفر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ طلاق کو ونصف طول کے ساتھ متصف کیا گیا ہے۔ اور طول کا استعمال قوت کے معنی میں ہوتا ہے اور قوت کا اظہار طلاق بائن میں ہوگا نہ کہ رجعی میں۔ اسلئے طلاق بائن واقع ہو گی۔ ہماری طرف سے کہا گیا کہ ایسا نہیں جیسا کہ امام زفر نے فرمایا بلکہ ملک شام کی قید لگا کر اس شخص نے طلاق کو کوتاہ کر دیا۔ کیونکہ اگر شخص انت طالق کہتا اور الی الشام ذکر نہ کرتا تو دنیا اور آسمان ہر جگہ میں طلاق واقع ہوتی ۔ پس جب الی الشام ذکر کیا تو گویا اس نے ایک محدود مکان میں طلاق کو خاص کر دیا۔ لہذا یہ کہنا کہ طلاق کو وصف طول کے ساتھ متصف کر دیا ہے درست نہیں ۔
And if he said, 'You are divorced from here to Sham,' then it is one (revocable) divorce, and he may take her back. Zufar said it is an irrevocable divorce because he described the divorce with length. We said: No, rather he described it with shortness, because when it occurs, it occurs in all places. Translation: And if he said, 'You are divorced from here to Sham,' then it is one, he may take her back. Imam Zufar said it is ba'in because he described the divorce with length. We answer: No, rather he described it with shortness, because when it occurs, it occurs in all places. Explanation: The issue is that if a man says to his wife, 'You are divorced from here to Sham,' then according to us, it is a revocable divorce. According to Imam Zufar, it is an irrevocable divorce. Imam Zufar's proof is that the divorce is described with length, and length is used in the sense of strength, and strength is expressed in ba'in divorce, not revocable. So it will be ba'in. Our side said: It is not as Imam Zufar said; rather, by specifying the area to Sham, the man restricted the divorce. Because if he had said 'You are divorced' without 'to Sham,' it would occur in all places on earth and sky. So when he mentioned 'to Sham,' he confined it to a limited place. Therefore, saying that he described divorce with length is incorrect.
Source pages p. 256

Commentary
This passage discusses a dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam Zufar regarding the phrase 'You are divorced from here to Sham.' The Hanafi position holds that this is a revocable (raj'i) divorce, because by specifying a spatial limit the husband actually restricts the divorce, not strengthens it. If he had not mentioned the limit, the divorce would take effect in all places. By limiting it, he makes it seem restricted, which is a characteristic of shortcoming (qasr), not strength (tul). Imam Zufar argues that the word 'to Sham' implies a long stretch, thus describing divorce with length (tul), which indicates strength, and strength is associated with irrevocability (ba'in). The Hanafi rebuttal is that the limit actually confines the divorce to a specific area, which is a restriction, not an extension. The divorce is revocable, and the husband can take her back.

Key Terms
رجعی (raj'i): Revocable divorce; the husband has the right to take back his wife during the waiting period without a new marriage contract.
بائن (ba'in): Irrevocable divorce; the wife becomes completely separate and a new marriage with a new contract is needed to reunite.
قصر (qasr): Restriction or shortcoming; used here to describe the effect of the spatial limit on the divorce.
طول (tul): Length or extension; interpreted by Imam Zufar as indicating strength.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is ba'in because the distance shows strength.
B) It is raj'i because the restriction shows weakness.
C) No divorce occurs because it is impossible.
D) It is three divorces.

Key Takeaway
A spatially limited divorce is revocable (raj'i) because the limitation indicates restriction, not strength.
