Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
6 min
Ruling on Talaq Uttered with Reference to Yesterday (anti taliq ams)
Ruling on talaq with past time reference

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the two scenarios of 'anti taliq ams' and apply the Hanafi principle of inshā' fī al-māḍī to determine whether talaq occurs.

Core Idea
Talaq referred to a time before marriage is invalid; referred to a time within marriage takes effect immediately.

A man says to his wife, 'You are divorced yesterday.' Does a divorce occur? The answer depends on when he married her. This lesson unpacks the Hanafi ruling and the reasoning behind it, distinguishing between an enactment and a mere report, and explaining why the same words can produce different results based on the marriage timeline.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
First scenario: he says 'anti taliq ams' after marrying her today. Second scenario: he married her before yesterday (e.g., a week ago) and then says the same phrase.
The key variable is whether she was in his marriage at the time referred to.
2
Apply the principle of inshā' fī al-māḍī
If the statement is an enactment (inshā'), it takes effect in the present because we cannot change the past. If it is a report (khabar) about a past fact, it has no divorcing effect.
The default assumption is that a statement like 'anti taliq ams' is an enactment unless it can be interpreted as a truthful report.
3
Test the possibility of a report
If the statement can be interpreted as a report that she was not his wife yesterday (first scenario) or that she was already divorced by someone else, then it is treated as a report and no talaq occurs.
This is a rescue mechanism to avoid an invalid enactment.
4
Assess compatibility with ownership
If the statement attributes divorce to a time when she was not in his ownership (e.g., before marriage), it is incompatible and thus canceled (laghw). In the second scenario, she was his wife yesterday, so compatibility exists.
The objection that 'ams' itself is not incompatible is answered by noting that the implicit time is before marriage.
5
Conclude the ruling
First scenario: no talaq occurs (by consensus). Second scenario: talaq occurs immediately upon utterance.
The difference is due to the ability (or inability) to assign a truthful report meaning.

Source Text

انت طالق امس سے طلاق دی حالانکہ آج نکاح کیا طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی

ولوقال انت طالق امس وقد تزوجها اليوم لم يقع شئى لانه اسنده الى حالة معهودة منافية لمالكية الطلاق فيلغو كما اذا قال انت طالق قبل ان اخلق ولانه يمكن تصحيحه اخباراً عن عدم النكاح او عن كونها مطلقته بتطليق غيره من الازواج ولوتزوجها اول من امس وقع الساعة لانه ما اسنده الى حالة منافية ولا يمكن تصحيحه اخبار ايضا فكان انشاء والانشاء في الماضى انشاء في الحال فيقع الساعة ترجمہ اور اگر کہا تو کل گذشتہ طلاق والی ہے حال یہ کہ اس سے آج نکاح ہوا ہے تو کوئی طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ اس نے 

 طلاق کو ایسی حالت معہودہ کی طرف منسوب کیا ہے جو مالکیت طلاق کے منافی ہے۔ پس لغو ہو گا ۔ جیسا کہ جب کہا تو طلاق والی ہے قبل اسکے کہ میں پیدا کیا جاؤں اور اسلئے کہ ممکن ہے اس کو صحیح قرار دینا عدم نکاح کی خبر دیتے ہوئے یا اس بات کی کہ وہ عورت کسی دوسرے شوہر کے طلاق دینے سے مطلقہ ہے۔ اور اگر اس سے نکاح کیا کل گذشتہ سے پہلے تو اسی وقت واقع ہو جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ حالت منافیہ کی طرف طلاق کو منسوب نہیں کیا ہے۔ اور اس کو خبر بنانا بھی صحیح نہیں ہے۔ پس انشاء ہو گا اور انشاء فی الماضی انشاء فی الحال ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا اسی وقت واقع ہوگی۔

تشریح مسئلہ، اگر مرد نے انت طالق امس کہا درانحالیکہ اس عورت سے نکاح آج کیا ہے تو بالا تفاق طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی ۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس شخص نے اپنا کلام ایسی حالت معلومہ کی طرف منسوب کیا ہے جو مالکیت طلاق کے منافی ہے۔ یعنی ایسے وقت کی طرف منسوب کیا ہے جبکہ وہ عورت اس کی نکو د نہیں تھی۔ لہذا اس کا کلام لغو ہوگا۔ اور کوئی طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی ۔ جیسے کسی نے کہا انت طالق قبل ان اخلق
اس دلیل پر ایک اشکال ہے وہ یہ کہ انت طالق اس میں لفظ اس مذکور ہے۔ اور امسیت مالکیت طلاق کے منافی نہیں بلکہ مالکیت طلاق کے منافی طلاق کا قبل التزوج ہونا ہے۔ اور طلاق کا قبل التزوج ہو نا کلام میں مذکور نہیں ۔ دوسری دلیل یہ ہے کہ اس کلام کو صحیح بنانا من ہے۔ بایں طور کہ اس شخص نے انت طلاق اس کہہ کر اس بات کی خبر دی ہے کہ یہ عورت کل گذشتہ غیر منکوحہ تھی۔ اور یہ بالکل صحیح ہے۔ یا اس بات کی خبر دی ہے کہ وہ کل گذشتہ اپنے سابق شوہر کی مطلقہ تھی یہ بھی درست ہے۔ ان دونوں صورتوں میں طلاق بھی واقع نہیں ہوگی اور کلام بھی لغو ہونے سے بچ جائے گا۔
اور اگر یہ شخص اس عورت سے کل گذشتہ سے پہلے نکاح کر چکا اور اس سے انت طالق امس کہا تو اس وقت طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی۔ دلیل یہ کہ اس شخص نے طلاق ایسی حالت کی طرف منسوب نہیں کی ہے جو مالکیت طلاق کے منافی ہو۔ کیونکہ کل گذشتہ یہ عورت اس کی ملک میں تھی۔ اور اسکے کلام کو اخبار بنا کر صحیح قرار دینا بھی ممکن نہیں ۔ پس یہ کلام (انت طالق امس ) انشاء ہوگا۔ اور فقہاء کا اصول ہے کہ انشاء فی الماضی انشاء فی الحال ہوتا ہے۔ یعنی موجودہ زمانے میں رہتے ہوئے اگر کوئی حکم ماضی میں ثابت کیا جائے تو وہ حکم زمانہ حال میں ثابت ہوگا۔ کیونکہ اثبات فی الماضی پر کوئی انسان قادر نہیں ہے۔
If he says 'You are divorced yesterday' while he married her today, no divorce occurs. And if he says 'You are divorced yesterday' and he married her today, nothing occurs because he attributed it to a recognized state that is incompatible with ownership of divorce; thus it is canceled, just as if he said 'You are divorced before I was created.' And because it can be corrected as a report about the absence of marriage, or that she is divorced by another husband. And if he married her before yesterday, it occurs at that moment because he did not attribute it to an incompatible state, nor can it be corrected as a report, so it is an enactment (inshā’). And enactment in the past is enactment in the present, so it occurs at that moment.

Explanation of the issue: If a man said 'You are divorced yesterday' while he married her today, by consensus no divorce occurs. The proof is that he attributed his speech to a known state incompatible with ownership of divorce, i.e., to a time when she was not in his marriage. So his speech is canceled. Like if someone said 'You are divorced before I was created.' There is an objection on this proof: that in 'anti taliq ams', the word 'ams' (yesterday) is mentioned, and 'yesterday' is not incompatible with ownership of divorce; rather, what is incompatible is that the divorce occurred before marriage, and that is not mentioned in the speech. The second proof is that this speech can be made correct as a report: by saying 'anti taliq ams', he is reporting that she was not married yesterday, which is true, or that she was divorced by her previous husband yesterday. In both cases, no divorce occurs and the speech is saved from being cancel. And if this person married her before yesterday and said 'anti taliq ams', then divorce occurs at that moment. The proof is that he did not attribute divorce to a state incompatible with ownership of divorce, because yesterday she was in his ownership. And it is not possible to correct his speech as a report. So this speech is an enactment, and the jurists' principle is that an enactment in the past is an enactment in the present; that is, if a ruling is established in the past while in the present, that ruling is established in the present because no human can establish something in the past.
Source pages p. 260

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling on a man who says to his wife 'anti taliq ams' (you are divorced yesterday) under two scenarios: (1) he married her today, and (2) he married her before yesterday. In the first scenario, the talaq does not occur by consensus. The reason is that the statement attributes divorce to a time (yesterday) when she was not his wife, which is incompatible with the ownership of divorce. Therefore, the statement is canceled (لغو). Alternatively, the statement can be interpreted as a report (خبر) about the past: either that she was not his wife yesterday, or that she was divorced by someone else. Both interpretations are true and avoid the need for talaq. In the second scenario, if he married her before yesterday, talaq does occur immediately upon utterance. The reason is that yesterday she was in his marriage, so the time is not incompatible. Moreover, it cannot be interpreted as a report because she was his wife yesterday and not divorced by another. Thus, the statement is an enactment (انشاء) of talaq, and according to Hanafi principle, enacting something in the past tense counts as an enactment in the present (since we cannot actually change the past). The passage also addresses an objection: one might argue that 'ams' itself is not incompatible with ownership; the incompatibility is the fact that the divorce is placed before marriage. The response is that the statement implicitly refers to a time before marriage, so the ruling stands. This lesson reinforces the principle that talaq referred to a time when the wife was not in the husband's ownership is invalid, ensuring that talaq is only effective when it can actually dissolve an existing marriage.

Key Terms
انشاء فی الماضی (inshā’ fī al-māḍī): An enactment in the past tense; legally treated as an enactment in the present because the past cannot be changed.
لغو (laghw): Canceled or void; a statement that has no legal effect due to incompatibility with the intended meaning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man says 'anti taliq ams' to his wife. He married her a week ago. What is the ruling?
A) Talaq does not occur because it refers to yesterday when she was his wife.
B) Talaq does occur immediately because yesterday she was his wife.
C) Talaq does not occur because the statement is a report about her status.
D) Talaq occurs only if he intends divorce.

Key Takeaway
Talaq uttered with reference to a time before marriage is invalid; talaq uttered with reference to a time within marriage is effective immediately.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
6 min
Talaq Attributed to Time Before Marriage: No Effect
Ruling on talaq with reference to time before marriage

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling when a husband attributes talaq to a time before marriage, identify the underlying principle of incompatible state (ḥālah munāfiyah), and apply it to analogous cases.

Core Idea
Talaq attributed to a time before marriage is void because it refers to a state incompatible with divorce.

In this passage, the author examines a peculiar scenario: a husband says to his wife, 'You are divorced before I marry you.' Despite using the word 'divorce,' the Hanafi school rules that no talaq occurs. The reason is that the utterance is attributed to a time before marriage, when no marital relationship existed. The author supports this by analogy to cases where the husband lacked legal capacity (childhood or sleep). This lesson unpacks the reasoning and its application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is uttering 'anti taliq qabla an atazawwajak'. The ruling: no talaq occurs.
2
Locate the proof
The proof is based on attribution to a state incompatible with talaq (ḥālah munāfiyah).
The author uses the concept of incompatible state to nullify the effect.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The author draws an analogy to cases where the husband was a child or asleep, showing that the illa (effective cause) is lack of capacity/ownership at the attributed time.
Both child and sleep are states where talaq cannot be effective.
4
Note the ikhtilaf
This ruling is unanimous within the Hanafi school and presumably across schools.
No intra-Hanafi or cross-madhhab dispute is mentioned.
5
Evaluate the thamarah
The practical consequence is that the marriage remains intact; no divorce is recorded.
This prevents wrongful dissolution of marriage.

انت طالق قبل ان اتزوجک سے طلاق دینے کا حکم
و لو قال انت طالق قبل ان اتزوجك لم يقع شيء لانه اسنده الى حالة منافية فصار كما اذاقال طلقتك و انا صبى او نائم اويصح اخبار على ما ذكرنا ترجمہ اور اگر کہا تجھ کو طلاق ہے قبل اسکے کہ میں تجھ سے نکاح کروں تو کوئی طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی ۔ کیونکہ طلاق کو ایسی حالت کی طرف منسوب کیا ہے جو منافی طلاق ہے۔ پس ایسا ہو گیا جیسا کہ جب کہا کہ میں نے تجھ کو طلاق دی حالانکہ میں بچہ تھا۔ یا سویا ہوا تھا یا صحیح ہے خبر دینا اس تفصیل پر جو ہم نے ذکر کی ہے۔
Ruling on giving talaq with 'You are divorced before I marry you.' And if he said 'You are divorced before I marry you', nothing occurs because he attributed it to a state incompatible with divorce, so it becomes like when he said 'I divorced you while I was a child' or 'while I was asleep', or it is correct as a report according to what we mentioned. Translation: And if he said 'You are divorced before I marry you', no divorce occurs. Because he attributed divorce to a state that is incompatible with divorce. So it becomes like when he said 'I divorced you while I was a child' or 'while I was asleep', or it is correct as a report according to the details we mentioned.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage gives a concise ruling on a man who says to his wife 'anti taliq qabla an atazawwajak' (you are divorced before I marry you). Since they are already married, this statement attributes divorce to a time before marriage, which is an incompatible state (because at that time she was not his wife and he had no right to divorce). Therefore, no talaq occurs. The author compares it to analogous scenarios: saying 'I divorced you while I was a child' or 'while I was asleep' – both are invalid because the person at that time lacked legal capacity. Alternatively, the statement can be interpreted as a report (خبر) about the future: i.e., informing that before he marries her (which is absurd since he is already married), she is divorced. But that interpretation is also invalid. Thus, the statement is either canceled (لغو) or treated as a report that has no effect. This ruling is consistent with the previous lesson: any talaq referred to a time when the husband had no ownership of talaq is void. The passage is brief but reinforces the principle that talaq must be assigned to a valid marital relationship at the time of utterance.

Key Terms
حالہ منافیہ (ḥālah munāfiyah): A state incompatible with talaq, such as before marriage, during childhood, or sleep.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Talaq occurs immediately.
B) Talaq occurs only if he intended it.
C) No talaq occurs.
D) Talaq occurs after the time of marriage passes.

Key Takeaway
Talaq attributed to a time before marriage is void because it is founded on a state incompatible with divorce.

Ruling on Saying 'You Are Divorced Yesterday' (Anti Taliq Ims)
Explains two scenarios for 'anti taliq ims' and their rulings.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the two scenarios of the pronouncement 'anti taliq ims' and state the ruling in each, applying the Hanafi principles of insha, khabar, and malikiyyat al-talaq.

Core Idea
Divorce attributed to a time before marriage is void; attributed to a time of ownership takes effect immediately.

This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya examines a specific divorce pronouncement: 'You are divorced yesterday' (anti taliq ims). The ruling hinges on whether the husband had ownership of the wife at the time to which the divorce is attributed. Understanding this distinction reveals the Hanafi application of the concepts of insha (enactment) versus khabar (report), and the principle that attribution to a state of non-ownership renders the divorce void.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two scenarios
Distinguish between Scenario A (marriage occurred today) and Scenario B (marriage occurred before yesterday). In Scenario A, the wife was not his yesterday; in Scenario B, she was.
This sets up the difference in ownership.
2
Apply the condition of malikiyyat al-talaq
Divorce is only valid if attributed to a time when the husband owned the right to divorce. If attributed to a time before marriage, it is void. Determine whether at the time of attribution (yesterday) the wife was in his ownership.
This is the core legal criterion.
3
Distinguish between insha and khabar
In Scenario A, the statement can be interpreted as a report (khabar) that she was not married yesterday, preserving truthfulness. In Scenario B, no such interpretation is possible; it must be an enaction (insha). Hanafi rules allow a statement to be taken as khabar if it can be true, thus avoiding a void insha.
This prevents the divorce from being void in Scenario A.
4
Apply the principle 'insha fi al-madi insha fi al-hal'
If the statement is an enaction referring to the past, it takes effect in the present because one cannot change the past. So in Scenario B, divorce occurs immediately upon utterance.
This principle is a secondary proof.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

انسان قادر نہیں ہے۔
The book of divorce: Divorce is attributed to a time that is contrary to ownership of divorce, so it is void. For example, when he said 'You are divorced before I was created.' And because it is possible to consider it as informing of non-marriage or that the woman is divorced by another husband. And if he married her before yesterday, then it occurs immediately, because the divorce is not attributed to a contrary state, and it cannot be considered as informing; so it is an enactment, and enactment in the past is enactment in the present, so it occurs immediately. Explanation of the issue: If a man said 'You are divorced yesterday' while he married her today, then by consensus divorce does not occur. The proof is that he attributed his speech to a known state contrary to ownership of divorce, i.e., a time when she was not his wife, so his speech is void and no divorce occurs, like saying 'You are divorced before I was created.' There is an objection: the word 'yesterday' is mentioned, and 'yesterday' is not contrary to ownership; rather the contrary is divorce before marriage, which is not mentioned. The second proof is that it is possible to interpret the speech as informing that she was not married yesterday, which is correct, or that she had been divorced by a previous husband, which is also correct. In both cases, no divorce occurs and speech is not void. And if he married her before yesterday and said 'You are divorced yesterday', then divorce occurs immediately. The proof is that he did not attribute divorce to a state contrary to ownership, because yesterday she was in his ownership, and it is not possible to interpret it as informing; so it is an enactment, and the principle of jurists is that enactment in the past is enactment in the present, i.e., while in the present, if a ruling is established in the past, it takes effect in the present because no one can establish something in the past.
Source pages p. 261

Commentary
This passage from Ashraf al-Hidaya explains the ruling on a husband saying to his wife 'anti taliq ims' (you are divorced yesterday). Two scenarios determine the outcome. First: if the marriage occurred today (i.e., she was not his wife yesterday), then no divorce takes effect. The proof is that the husband attributed the divorce to a time when he had no ownership over her, making the statement void. Additionally, the statement can be interpreted as a factual report (ikhbar) that she was not his wife yesterday, preserving its truthfulness. Second: if he married her before yesterday, divorce occurs immediately upon utterance. Here, the attribution is to a time when she was his wife, so the clause cannot be interpreted as a report; it becomes an enaction (insha). According to Hanafi principles, an enaction referring to the past takes effect in the present because one cannot actually effect a change in the past. Thus, divorce is effective at the moment of speech. The passage also addresses an objection: the word 'yesterday' itself does not negate ownership; rather, the negation lies in the fact that she was not his wife at that time. This ruling is consistent across the Hanafi school without known dissent.

Key Terms
انشاء (insha): A performative utterance that creates a legal effect, such as divorce, as opposed to report (khabar).
خبر (khabar): A statement that reports a fact and can be true or false.
مالکیت طلاق (malikiyyat al-talaq): The husband's ownership of the right to divorce at the time the pronouncement is made or to which it is attributed.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
A man marries a woman today and says 'anti taliq ims' (you are divorced yesterday). What is the ruling?
A) Divorce occurs immediately.
B) No divorce occurs.
C) Divorce occurs only if she was married before yesterday.
D) The marriage is invalidated.

Key Takeaway
The validity of a divorce pronounced with a past-time reference depends on whether the husband owned the right to divorce at that time; if not, the pronouncement is void, but if so, it takes effect immediately as an enaction.

Immediate Divorce upon Silence in 'As Long as I Haven't Divorced You'
Explains that divorce occurs immediately upon silence in these suspended formulas.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on divorce formulas using 'ma lam utallik' and explain why silence triggers immediate divorce.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, 'ma lam' in divorce is temporal; silence realizes the time, making divorce immediate.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a specific suspended divorce formulation. The husband says 'You are divorced as long as I have not divorced you' and then falls silent. The ruling might seem counterintuitive: why would silence cause divorce? The key is the linguistic interpretation that 'ma' here indicates time, not condition. Let's trace the reasoning.

Guided Path
1
Identify the statement and the action
The husband says one of the three formulas: 'ma lam utallik', 'matta lam utallik', or 'matta ma lam utallik'. After uttering it, he remains silent.
Silence here means he does not actually divorce her; he simply says nothing.
2
Understand the temporal attachment
The divorce is attached to a time that is free from divorce. By remaining silent, the husband actualizes that time — he neither divorces nor revokes the statement, so the condition (a time free from divorce) is fulfilled.
3
Analyze the linguistic argument
The words 'matta' and 'matta ma' are explicit adverbs of time. The word 'ma' in this context is also interpreted temporally, as in the Quranic verse 'ma dumtu hayyan' (as long as I live).
The proof is Quran 19:31, showing 'ma' for time.
4
Note the ambiguity of 'ma' and its resolution
'Ma' can also indicate condition (e.g., 'ma yaftah Allah'). Hanafis prioritize the temporal meaning here because the context is a suspended divorce that would make sense as a time-bound condition.
If the husband intended condition, the ruling might differ, but the literal temporal meaning applies.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو قال انت طالق مالم اطلقك او متى لم اطلقك او متى مالم اطلقك و سکت طلقت لانه اضاف الطلاق الى زمان خال عن التطليق وقد وجد حيث سكت وهذا لان كلمة متى ومتى ما صريح في الوقت لانهما من ظروف الزمان وكذا كلمة ما للوقت قال الله تعالى ما دمت حيا اى وقت الحيوية ترجمہ اور اگر کہا کہ تو طلاق والی ہے اس وقت کہ میں تجھ کو طلاق نہ دوں یا جب تک کہ میں تجھ کو طلاق نہ دے دوں ۔ اور شوہر خاموش ہو گیا تو (عورت) طلاق والی ہو گئی۔ کیونکہ طلاق کو ایسے زمانہ کی طرف منسوب کیا ہے۔ جو طلاق دینے سے خالی ہے۔ اور ( وہ زمانہ ) پایا گیا جب وہ خاموش ہوا۔ اور یہ اسلئے کہ کلمہ متی اور متی ما وقت کے معنی میں صریح ہے۔ کیونکہ وہ دونوں ظروف زبان میں سے ہیں۔ اور ایسے ہی کلمہ ما وقت کیلئے ہے۔ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا ”جب تک کہ میں زندہ رہوں یعنی زندگی کے وقت تک۔ تشریح صورت مسئلہ اگر مرد نے اپنی منکوحہ سے کہا انت طالق ما لم اطلقک یا کہا انت طالق منی لم اطلقک یا کہا انت طالق متى مالم اطلقک اور کہنے کے بعد سکوت اختیار کیا۔ تو فورا طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی۔ دلیل یہ ہے کہ ان تینوں صورتوں میں طلاق ایسے زمانے کی طرف منسوب کی گئی ہے، جو خالی عن التطلیق ہو۔ اور جیسے ہی وہ خاموش ہوا ایسا زمانہ پایا گیا اسوجہ سے طلاق سکوت کے فورا بعد واقع ہو گئی۔ صاحب ہدایہ وضاحت کرتے ہوئے فرماتے ہیں کہ لفظ متی اور متی ما چونکہ ظروف زمان میں سے ہیں۔ اسلئے یہ دونوں وقت کے معنی میں صریحی ہیں۔ اور اسی طرح لفظ ما بھی وقت کیلئے آتا ہے جیسا کہ حضرت عیسی سے حکایت کرتے ہوئے اللہ رب العزت نے فرمایا وأوصانى بالصلوة والزكوة ما دمت حیا یعنی مجھ کو حکم دیا نماز اور زکوۃ کا جب تک میں زندہ رہوں۔ فوائد لفظ ما جس طرح وقت کیلئے آتا ہے اس طرح شرط کیلئے بھی آتا ہے، مثلاً خداوند قدوس نے فرمایا مـا يفتح الله للناس من رحمة فلا ممسك لها و ما يمسك فلا مرسل له من بعدہ یعنی اگر اللہ لوگوں کے واسطے رحمت ( کا دروازہ ) کھول دے تو اس کو کوئی روکنے والا نہیں۔ اور اگر روک لے تو اس کو کوئی اس کے بعد چھوڑنے والا نہیں۔ اس آیت میں لفظ ما شرط کے معنی میں استعمال کیا گیا ہے۔ پس لفظ ما اگر صرف وقت کے معنی میں استعمال کیا گیا نہ کہ شرط کے معنی میں تو طلاق واقع ہونی چاہئے ۔ ورنہ اس کا حکم وہ نہیں ہوگا جو تشریح میں گذر چکا۔
And if he said, 'You are divorced as long as I have not divorced you,' or 'You are divorced when I do not divorce you,' or 'You are divorced when I have not divorced you,' and he remained silent, she is divorced, because he attributed divorce to a time free from divorce, and that time was found when he was silent. And that is because the word 'matta' and 'matta ma' are explicit in meaning time, as they are among adverbs of time. Similarly, the word 'ma' is for time. Allah Almighty said: 'As long as I live' i.e., the time of life. Explanation: If a man said to his wife 'You are divorced as long as I have not divorced you' or 'You are divorced from me when I do not divorce you' or 'You are divorced when I have not divorced you' and after saying it he remained silent, then divorce occurs immediately. The proof is that in all three cases, divorce is attributed to a time free from divorce, and as soon as he became silent, that time was found, so divorce occurred right after silence. The author of Al-Hidayah clarifies that the words 'matta' and 'matta ma' are adverbs of time, so they are explicit in meaning time. Similarly, the word 'ma' is also used for time, as in the verse from Prophet Isa: 'And He has enjoined upon me prayer and zakah as long as I live' meaning the time of life. Benefit: The word 'ma' is also used for condition, e.g., God said: 'Whatever mercy Allah opens to people, none can withhold it; and whatever He withholds, none can release it afterward.' In this verse, 'ma' is used in the sense of condition. So if the word 'ma' is used only in the sense of time, divorce must occur; otherwise, the ruling is not as passed in the explanation.
Source pages p. 262

Commentary
This passage deals with a conditional divorce using phrases like 'ma lam utallik' (as long as I have not divorced you), 'matta lam utallik' (when I do not divorce you), and 'matta ma lam utallik' (when I have not divorced you). If the husband says any of these and then remains silent, divorce occurs immediately. The reasoning is that these words are explicit in indicating time (zarf al-zaman). The husband attached the divorce to a time that is free from the act of divorcing. Since he remains silent, that time actually occurs (i.e., he does not divorce her), so the condition is fulfilled and divorce takes effect. The author emphasizes that 'ma' in such contexts can mean time, as in the Qur'anic verse 'ma dumtu hayyan' (as long as I live). However, 'ma' can also indicate a condition, as in another verse. If the husband intends the word 'ma' as a condition (i.e., if I divorce you, then you are divorced), the ruling differs; but if it is purely temporal, divorce occurs upon silence. The Hanafi school considers the literal temporal meaning as primary, and silence triggers the divorce.

Key Terms
متى (matta): A word indicating time, meaning 'when' or 'whenever'.
ما (ma): Can mean 'as long as' (time) or 'if' (condition). Context determines which.
سکوت (sukut): Silence after uttering the divorce formula, indicating the realization of a time free from divorce.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) No divorce occurs until he says 'I divorce you'.
B) Divorce occurs immediately after silence.
C) Divorce occurs only if he intends to divorce her.
D) The statement is considered a joke and has no effect.

Key Takeaway
When a husband says 'You are divorced as long as I have not divorced you' and remains silent, the divorce takes effect immediately, as silence fulfills the temporal condition.

Divorce Conditioned on Absence: Timing
Ruling on conditional divorce with negative condition

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain when divorce occurs in the conditional phrase 'You are divorced if I do not divorce you' and apply the analogy to other conditions of impossibility.

Core Idea
Divorce conditioned on an absence occurs only when all possibility is gone — at death or despair.

This passage from the Hidayah deals with a specific conditional divorce phrase. The ruling is counterintuitive: the divorce does not happen immediately but is postponed to the moment of death or complete despair. The analogy to the condition of not going to Basra clarifies the principle of impossibility.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The husband says 'You are divorced if I do not divorce you.' The ruling is that she is not divorced until he dies (or despairs of life).
The condition is 'adam al-tatliq' (absence of divorce).
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is qiyas (analogy) to the case of 'If I do not go to Basra, you are divorced.' In that case, divorce occurs when he despairs of going.
The common illa is that the condition is fulfilled only at the point of impossibility.
3
Analyze the illa and analogy
The illa is that the condition (absence of an act) is not realized until there is no possibility left to perform the act. Here, 'not divorcing' is only certain at death or despair.
Thus, divorce occurs just before death (or during death-throes).

Source Text

And if he said 'You are divorced if I do not divorce you', she is not divorced until he dies, because absence (of divorce) is not realized except at despair from life, and that is the condition, just as in his saying 'If I do not go to Basra'. And her death is like his death — that is the correct view. Explanation: If a man says 'You are divorced if I do not divorce you', then divorce will occur at the time of death, i.e., when the husband has despaired of life and there is no time left to say 'You are divorced'. The proof is that in this case, the occurrence of divorce is suspended on the absence of divorce, and the absence of divorce is only realized when he is completely hopeless of life, because before that time there is always the possibility of divorce. So when the condition of absence of divorce is fulfilled at the time of despair, divorce occurs. This is like someone saying 'If I do not go to Basra, then you are divorced' — divorce occurs when he despairs of going. The author of Hidayah says that the wife's death is at the same level as the husband's death. That is, just as divorce occurs just before the husband's death, similarly it occurs just before the wife's death. This is the correct view, although in Nawadir there is a narration contrary to this.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage deals with the phrase 'You are divorced if I do not divorce you'. The key issue is that the condition (absence of divorce) is not realized until there is no possibility left to divorce, i.e., at the time of death or despair. Therefore, the divorce does not occur immediately but only when the husband is at the point of death and can no longer pronounce divorce. The author compares this to the example of swearing by a condition of not going to Basra. The Hidayah also states that the same applies if the wife dies — it occurs just before her death, as the condition is then fulfilled. The author notes that this is the sound view, though Nawadir (rare transmissions) contain a contrary report.

Key Terms
عدم التطلیق (adam al-tatliq): The absence of divorce; the condition that must be fulfilled.
الیاس عن الحیاة (al-ya's an al-hayat): Despair of life; the point of hopelessness before death.

Dispute on the Meaning of 'Iza' in Talaq: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the meaning of 'iza' in a conditional talaq

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the phrase 'You are divorced when I do not divorce you' and explain how the ambiguity of 'iza' affects the timing of talaq.

Core Idea
The word 'iza' is ambiguous between time and condition, so talaq does not occur immediately unless intention clarifies it.

This passage from Al-Hidayah presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani, regarding a conditional talaq using the word 'iza'. The Sahibayn argue that 'iza' exclusively denotes time, while Abu Hanifa demonstrates its dual usage. Understanding this dispute illuminates how Hanafi jurists handle linguistic ambiguity in legal rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the factual scenario
The husband says to his wife: 'You are divorced when I do not divorce you' (or 'when I do not divorce you') using the word 'iza'. The question is whether talaq occurs immediately upon silence or is postponed.
2
State the Sahibayn's position and evidence
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad hold that 'iza' is exclusively for time. They cite Quran 81:1 (When the sun is wrapped up) and poetic usage. Therefore, upon silence, the condition 'when I do not divorce you' is fulfilled and talaq occurs immediately.
3
State Abu Hanifa's position and evidence
Abu Hanifa argues that 'iza' can be used for both time and condition. He cites another poetic verse where 'iza' indicates condition. Because of this ambiguity, the word cannot be taken to mean time alone, so talaq does not occur immediately; it is postponed until the husband's death.
4
Analyze the linguistic argument
Both sides use Arabic poetry to support their reading of 'iza'. Abu Hanifa's approach gives priority to the possibility of condition, preventing immediate talaq due to doubt. This is a typical Hanafi method: when a word has multiple meanings, the default is to avoid applying the more severe ruling (talaq) until certainty.
5
Distinguish from the 'mashi'a' case and note the role of intention
The Hidayah contrasts this case with 'You are divorced when you wish' (mashi'a), where ambiguity does not change the outcome because the wife retains control. Here, the dispute applies when the husband has no specific intention. If he intends time, talaq occurs immediately; if he intends condition, it occurs at the end of life.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
و لو قال انت طالق اذالم اطلقك او اذا مالم اطلقك لم تطلق حتى يموت عند ابي حنيفة وقالا تطلق حين سکت لان كلمة اذا للوقت قال الله تعالى اذالشمس كورت وقال قائلهم شعر واذا تكون كريهة ادعى لها و اذا يحاس الحيس يدعى جندب فصار بمنزلة متى و متى ما ولهذا لو قال لامرأته انت طالق اذاشئت لا يخرج الامر من يدها بالقيام من المجلس كما في قوله متى شئت ولابي حنيفة انه يستعمل في الشرط ايضا قال قائلهم شعر و استغن ما اغناک ربک بالغنی فاذا تصبك خصاصة فتجمل فان اريد به الشرط لم تطلق في الحال وان اريد به الوقت تطلق فلا تطلق بالشك والاحتمال بخلاف مسالة المشية لانه على اعتبار انه للوقت لا يخرج الامر من يدها و على اعتبار انه للشرط يخرج والامر صارفى يدها فلا یخرج بالشک والاحتمال وهذا الخلاف فيما اذالم تكن له نية اما اذانوى الوقت يقع فى الحال ونوى الشرط يقع في آخر العمرلان اللفظ يحتملهما ترجمہ اور اگر کہا تو طلاق والی ہے جب میں تجھے طلاق نہ دوں تو طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی یہاں تک کہ (شوہر ) مر جائے ابوحنیفہ کے نزدیک۔ اور (امام) ابو یوسف اور امام محمد نے کہا کل (ان کے قول کے الفاظ کہنے کے بعد خاموش ہو جانے پر) طلاق واقع ہو جاتی ہے اس لئے کہ کلمہ اذا وقت کے لئے ہے۔ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا جب سورج لپیٹا جائے گا۔ اور ان کا کہنے والا (شاعر) کہتا ہے شعر الخ۔ پس یہ متی اور متی ما کے حکم میں ہو گیا۔ اور یہی وجہ ہے کہ اگر آدمی اپنی عورت سے کہے انت طالق اذا شئت تو عورت کا اختیار مجلس کے قیام سے ختم نہیں ہوتا جیسے متی شئت کے قول میں۔ ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ اذا شرط کے لئے بھی استعمال ہوتا ہے۔ ان کا کہنے والا (شاعر) کہتا ہے شعر الخ پس اگر اذا شرط کے معنی میں لیا جائے تو طلاق اس وقت واقع نہ ہوگی اور اگر وقت کے معنی میں لیا جائے تو واقع ہو گی۔ پس طلاق شک اور احتمال کی وجہ سے واقع نہیں ہوگی۔ بخلاف مسئلہ مشیت کے کیونکہ وہاں اگر وقت کے اعتبار سے لیا جائے تو عورت کا اختیار اس کے ہاتھ سے نہیں جاتا اور اگر شرط کے اعتبار سے لیا جائے تو ساتھ ہی اختیار نکل جاتا ہے اور معاملہ عورت کے ہاتھ میں ہے۔ سو شک و احتمال سے اختیار نہیں نکلتا۔ اور یہ اختلاف اس صورت میں ہے جب اس کی نیت نہ ہو۔ اگر نیت وقت کی ہو تو طلاق فورا واقع ہو گی اور نیت شرط کی ہو تو عمر کے آخر میں واقع ہو گی کیونکہ لفظ دونوں احتمال کو برداشت کرتا ہے۔
And if he said 'You are divorced when I do not divorce you' or 'when I do not divorce you', she is not divorced until he dies according to Abu Hanifa. And the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said she is divorced when he is silent, because the word 'iza' is for time. Allah said: 'When the sun is wrapped up' [81:1]. And their poet says: 'And when a calamity occurs, they call upon her...' So it becomes like 'mata' and 'mata ma'. For this reason, if a man says to his wife 'You are divorced when you wish', the matter does not leave her hand upon rising from the session, as in the phrase 'mata shi'ta'. And Abu Hanifa's proof is that 'iza' is also used for condition. Their poet says: 'And seek independence while your Lord has enriched you with wealth, but if harm touches you, then be patient.' So if it is intended as condition, she is not divorced immediately; if intended as time, she is divorced. Therefore, she is not divorced due to doubt and possibility. Unlike the issue of will (mashi'a), because if considered for time, the matter does not leave her hand; if considered for condition, it leaves her hand, and the matter is in her hand. So it does not leave by doubt and possibility. And this difference is when he has no intention. But if he intends time, it occurs immediately; if he intends condition, it occurs at the end of life, because the word can bear both.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad) regarding the phrase 'You are divorced when I do not divorce you' using the word 'iza'. The Sahibayn argue that 'iza' is unequivocally for time, citing the Quranic verse 'When the sun is wrapped up' and poetry. Therefore, upon silence, the time of non-divorce is found, and talaq occurs immediately. Abu Hanifa counters that 'iza' can also be used for condition, as in another poetic verse. Since the word is ambiguous, it cannot be taken to mean time alone, and thus talaq does not occur immediately due to doubt. He distinguishes this from the case of 'You are divorced when you wish' where the difference does not affect the outcome. The Hidayah states that this dispute applies when the husband has no specific intention. If he explicitly intends time, talaq occurs immediately; if he intends condition, it occurs at the end of life.

Key Terms
اذا (iza): A word that can mean 'when' (time) or 'if' (condition).

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) Never
D) Only if the wife asks

Key Takeaway
The ambiguity of 'iza' in a conditional talaq prevents immediate divorce unless the husband's intention clarifies it.

When Does Divorce Occur with 'If I Do Not Divorce You'?
Ruling with qiyas proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the conditional divorce formula 'in lam utalliqki' and explain the qiyas jaliyyah that delays the divorce to the moment of death.

Core Idea
A conditional divorce based on not divorcing occurs only at death, because non-existence is complete only when action becomes impossible.

This lesson examines a specific conditional divorce formula: 'You are divorced if I do not divorce you' (in lam utalliqki). The Hanafi school rules that divorce does not occur immediately, but only at the moment of death. We will explore the reasoning, which relies on analogy to a similar case of conditional divorce involving coming to Basra. Understanding this ruling clarifies how impossibility (al-ya's) functions in ta'liq al-talaq.

Guided Path
1
State the ruling
Identify the hukm: divorce does not occur immediately, but only when the husband becomes hopeless of life (near death).
The same applies if the wife dies first – divorce occurs before her death.
2
Analyze the condition
The condition is 'if I do not divorce you'. The non-occurrence of divorce (adam al-tatliq) is a negative condition that can only be fully realized when no possibility remains to divorce – i.e., at death.
Before death, the husband could always divorce, so the condition is not yet fulfilled.
3
Examine the qiyas
The text analogizes to the case 'if I do not come to Basra, you are divorced'. In both cases, the negated action becomes impossible only at hopelessness of life.
This is qiyas jaliyyah: the illa is impossibility of performing the negated action.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Although the Nawadir contains a contrary narration, the author of Al-Hidayah affirms this as the correct (sahih) position, and it is the mufta bihi.
Zahir al-Riwayah supports this ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

And if he said: 'You are divorced if I do not divorce you,' she is not divorced until he dies, because the non-existence (of divorce) is not realized except with hopelessness of life, and that is the condition, as in his saying 'if I do not come to Basra.' And her death is like his death. This is correct. Urdu explanation: And if he said: You are divorced if I do not divorce you, then divorce does not occur until he dies. Because the non-existence of divorce is not realized except at the time of hopelessness of life, and that is the condition. As in his saying 'in lam at al-basra.' And the death of the woman is in the status of the man's death. This is correct. Explanation of the issue: If a man said: 'You are divorced if I do not divorce you,' then in this case divorce occurs at the time of death, i.e., it occurs when the husband becomes hopeless of life, and there remains no time in which he could say the words 'you are divorced.' The proof is that in this issue, the occurrence of divorce is suspended upon the non-occurrence of divorce. And the realization of non-occurrence of divorce will be when he becomes completely hopeless of life. Because before the time of hopelessness, there is always the possibility of giving divorce. So when at the time of hopelessness the condition of non-divorce is fulfilled, then at that time divorce will occur. And this is like if someone said: 'If I do not come to Basra, then you are divorced.' In this case also, divorce occurs when he becomes completely hopeless of coming to Basra. The author of Hidayah says: The death of the woman is in the status of the man's death. That is, just as divorce will occur a little before the man's death, similarly divorce will occur a little before the woman's death. This is the correct saying, although in the Nawadir there is a contrary narration.
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on a specific conditional divorce formula: 'You are divorced if I do not divorce you.' The text establishes that divorce does not occur immediately upon uttering the condition, but only at the moment of the husband's death when he becomes hopeless of life and cannot physically divorce. The reasoning is that the non-occurrence of divorce (al-'adam) is only verified when there is no possibility left for the husband to divorce, which is at the point of death. This is analogous to a condition like 'if I do not come to Basra,' where divorce occurs only when hope of going is lost. The text also notes that the wife's death triggers the same ruling as the husband's death, meaning divorce occurs just before her death as well. This is the correct (sahih) position, though a contrary narration exists in the Nawadir.

Key Terms
عدم تطلیق (adam al-tatliq): The non-occurrence or absence of divorce, which is the condition for the divorce to be triggered in the phrase 'in lam utalliqki'.
الیاس عن الحیوۃ (al-ya'u 'an al-hayat): Hopelessness of life, i.e., the point of death when the person has no remaining ability or time to act.

Key Takeaway
A conditional divorce based on a negated action (e.g., 'if I do not divorce you') is delayed until the moment of death, because only then is the condition fully realized.

10 min
Timing of Divorce with 'Idha Lam Utalliqki' – Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
Intra-Hanafi dispute on timing of talaq with 'idha'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on the timing of divorce when the husband says 'You are divorced when I do not divorce you' and explain how intention determines the ruling.

Core Idea
Because 'idha' can mean 'when' or 'if', divorce timing depends on intention; without it, doubt prevents immediate effect.

In this lesson, we examine an intra-Hanafi dispute about a conditional divorce formula using the Arabic word 'idha'. The core question: when does divorce occur if a husband says 'You are divorced when I do not divorce you'? Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) reached different conclusions based on the linguistic ambiguity of 'idha'. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to analyze the impact of language on legal rulings.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the two positions within the Hanafi school: Abu Hanifa's view that divorce occurs at death, and the Sahibayn's view that divorce occurs immediately upon silence.
Both are legitimate Hanafi views, but the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position depends on intention.
2
Identify the opponent and their view
The opponent here is the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Their view is that the wife is divorced immediately when the husband becomes silent (i.e., does not divorce her in that sitting).
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Understand the Sahibayn's dalil: they argue that 'idha' primarily denotes time (waqt), citing Quranic and poetic evidence. They analogize 'idha' to 'mata' (when), which in a previous case triggers immediate divorce upon silence.
They emphasize the indicative mood of the verb after 'idha' as evidence that it is for time, not condition.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response
Abu Hanifa argues that 'idha' is also used for condition (shart) in Arabic, citing a poetic example. Because the word has dual usage, without a specific intention, it cannot be assigned solely to time. Doubt (shakk) prevents the immediate occurrence of divorce.
The response hinges on the principle that in cases of linguistic ambiguity, the default is to avoid harm until certainty.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical consequence: without intention, Abu Hanifa says no divorce until death; the Sahibayn say immediate divorce. With clear intention, the divorce follows the intended meaning. The mufta bihi position is that without intention, divorce does not occur immediately.
This aligns with the Hanafi preference for caution in marital matters.

And if he said: 'You are divorced when I do not divorce you' or 'when I have not divorced you,' she is not divorced until he dies according to Abu Hanifa. The two said: She is divorced at the moment he becomes silent. Because the word 'idha' is for time. Allah said: 'When the sun is wrapped up.' And a poet said: 'And when a calamity occurs, I am summoned for it/And when hais is prepared, Jundab is summoned.' So it becomes like 'matta' and 'matta ma.' For this reason, if he said to his wife 'You are divorced when you wish,' the authority does not leave her hand by leaving the gathering, as in his saying 'matta shi'ta.' And for Abu Hanifa, it is also used for condition. A poet said: 'And seek sufficiency as your Lord enriches you, then if hardship befalls you, show patience.' So if it is intended for condition, she is not divorced immediately; if intended for time, she is divorced. So she is not divorced due to doubt and probability, unlike the issue of 'mashiy'a,' because on the consideration that it is for time, the authority does not leave her hand, and on the consideration that it is for condition, it leaves. And the matter is in her hand, so it does not leave due to doubt and probability. This difference is when he has no intention. But if he intends time, it occurs immediately; if he intends condition, it occurs at the end of life, because the word can bear both. Urdu explanation: And if he said: 'You are divorced when I do not divorce you' or 'when I have not divorced you,' then there is a difference in the time of occurrence of divorce. Imam Abu Hanifa says: Divorce will occur a little before death, at the time of hopelessness. The Sahibayn say: Divorce will occur immediately upon silence. The gist of the Sahibayn's proof is that the word 'idha' is used for time. Because Allah's saying 'wa idha al-shamsu kuwirat' translates to 'when the sun is wrapped up.' Similarly, a poet's verse: 'And when a calamity occurs, I am summoned for it/And when hais is prepared, Jundab is summoned.' In this verse, 'idha' appears twice, both times for time, not condition, because if it were for condition, 'takun' and 'yuhas' would be in jussive mood, but the poet used them in indicative. So when 'idha' is for time, it becomes like 'matta' and 'matta ma,' and the same rule applies. Therefore, if someone said 'you are divorced when you wish,' the wife's authority does not end by leaving the gathering, as in 'matta shi'ta.' And Abu Hanifa's proof is that 'idha' is also used for condition. The author of Hidayah cited a verse...
Source pages p. 263

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the conditional divorce formula using 'idha' (when/if) as in 'You are divorced when I do not divorce you.' Abu Hanifa holds that divorce does not occur until death (hopelessness), while the two Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that divorce occurs immediately upon the husband's silence. The Sahibayn base their argument on the primary usage of 'idha' for time (waqt), citing the Qur'anic verse 'When the sun is wrapped up' and a poetic line where 'idha' clearly indicates time. They analogize 'idha' to 'matta' (when), which in a previous issue triggers immediate divorce upon silence. Abu Hanifa counters that 'idha' is also used for condition (shart), citing another poetry line. Because the word can bear both meanings, when the husband has no specific intention, the divorce does not occur immediately due to doubt. However, if the husband intends time, it occurs immediately; if he intends condition, it occurs at the end of life. The practice (mufta bihi) thus depends on intention, and without intention, divorce is not immediate.

Key Terms
اذا (idha): A word that can denote either time ('when') or condition ('if') in Arabic, causing ambiguity in conditional divorce.
متی (mata): Equivalent to 'when' in time; used analogically to 'idha' for time-based interpretation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Sahibayn, when does divorce occur if a man says 'You are divorced when I do not divorce you'?
A) At death
B) Immediately upon silence
C) After one month
D) Never

Key Takeaway
The timing of divorce with 'idha' depends on intention; without it, doubt prevents immediate effect, in line with the Hanafi principle of caution in marital matters.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
12 min
The Dispute on the Meaning of 'Idha' in Divorce
Explains intra-Hanafi dispute on meaning of 'idha' in divorce

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on whether the word 'idha' indicates time or condition in divorce formulas and apply the principle that doubt prevents divorce.

Core Idea
When a word can mean time or condition, doubt prevents immediate divorce—certainty is required for talaq.

This lesson explores a classic intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) regarding the word 'idha' in divorce phrases like 'anta taliq idha lam utalliqka'. The disagreement hinges on whether 'idha' indicates time (like 'mata' meaning 'when') or condition (like 'in' meaning 'if'). Understanding this dispute reveals how Hanafi jurists applied linguistic analysis and the principle that certainty is required for divorce.

Guided Path
1
State the dispute
Identify the two positions: Abu Hanifa says divorce occurs near death; Sahibayn say it occurs immediately upon silence. The phrase in question is 'anta taliq idha lam utalliqka' or 'idha ma lam utalliqka'.
The dispute only applies when the husband has no specific intention.
2
Examine the Sahibayn's proof
The Sahibayn argue that 'idha' primarily indicates time, citing Quran 81:1 ('wa idha al-shamsu kuwirat') and a line of poetry where 'idha' is used with indicative verbs, proving it is not conditional.
The poetic evidence shows the verb is not jussive, so 'idha' here denotes time, not condition.
3
Examine Abu Hanifa's proof
Abu Hanifa counters that 'idha' is also used for condition, citing a verse where 'idha' governs a jussive verb ('wa idha tusibka khasasatun fa tajammal'). This proves conditional usage.
The jussive verb indicates that 'idha' functions as a conditional particle in that context.
4
Analyse the outcome: doubt prevents divorce
Because 'idha' can mean either time or condition, if the husband has no intention, there is doubt (shakk) about his meaning. Since certainty is required for divorce, the doubt prevents immediate divorce. Thus, according to Abu Hanifa, divorce is postponed until near death.
This contrasts with the Sahibayn's view, where 'idha' is taken as time, so divorce is immediate.
5
Apply the role of intention
The author clarifies that the dispute only arises when the husband has no intention. If he intends time, divorce occurs immediately; if he intends condition, it occurs at the end of life. The word's ambiguity allows his intention to prevail.
Intention (niyyah) resolves the ambiguity and determines the timing of divorce.

نزدیک اور صاحبین نے فرمایا کہ مطلقہ ہو جائے گی جس وقت (شوہر نے ) سکوت اختیار کیا۔ کیونکہ کلمہ از اوقت کیلئے ہے۔ اللہ تعالیٰ نے فرمایا۔ جب آفتاب بے نور ہو جائے گا۔ اور قائل نے کہا۔ جب کوئی ناگوار چیز پائی جائے تو اس کے واسطے میں بلایا جاتا ہوں ۔ اور جب حلوا ما نڈا تیار کیا جائے تو جندب کو بلایا جاتا ہے۔ پس مٹی اور مٹی ما کے مرتبہ میں ہو گیا اور اسی وجہ سے اگر اپنی بیوی سے کہا انت طالق اذا شئت تو عورت کے ہاتھ سے مجلس سے کھڑا ہونے کی وجہ سے اختیار نہیں نکلے گا۔ جیسا کہ اسکے قول متی شئت میں ۔ اور ابوحنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ لفظ اذا شرط میں بھی استعمال کیا جاتا ہے۔ کسی نے کہا۔ بے پروا ہی رکھ جب تک غنی رکھے تجھ کو تیرا رب مالداری کے ساتھ ۔ اور اگر مجھ کو تنگدستی پہنچے تو صبر جمیل اختیار کر۔ پس اگر اس سے شرط کا ارادہ کیا گیا ہے تو فی الحال طلاق (واقع ) نہیں ہوگی۔ اور اگر اس سے وقت کا ارادہ کیا گیا ہے تو طلاق ( واقع) ہو جائے گی ۔ پس شک اور احتمال کی وجہ سے طلاق نہیں پڑے گی ۔ بخلاف مسئلہ مشیت کے۔ کیونکہ یہ اعتبار کرتے ہوئے کہ (لفظ اذا) وقت کیلئے ہے۔ عورت کے ہاتھ سے اختیار نہیں نکلے گا۔ اور اس اعتبار پر کہ شرط کیلئے ہے۔ اختیار ( عورت کے ہاتھ سے نکل جائے گا) اور طلاق کا معاملہ عورت کے ہاتھ میں (یقیناً) ہے۔ پس شک اور احتمال کی وجہ سے نہیں نکلے گا۔ اور خلاف اس صورت میں ہے جبکہ شوہر کی کوئی نیت نہ ہو۔ بہر حال جب نیت کی وقت کی تو فی الحال ( طلاق) واقع ہو جائے گی ۔ اور اگر شرط کی نیت کی تو آخری عمر میں واقع ہوگی کیونکہ لفظ دونوں کا احتمال رکھتا ہے۔
تشریح مسئلہ، اگر مرد نے اپنی منکوحہ سے کہا انت طالق اذا لم اطلقك يا اذا مالم اطلقک تو ان الفاظ کے ساتھ وقوع طلاق کے وقت میں اختلاف ہے چنانچہ امام ابو حنیفہ فرماتے ہیں کہ موت کے کچھ پہلے پاس کے وقت طلاق واقع ہوگی۔ اور صاحبین فرماتے ہیں کہ خاموش ہوتے ہی طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی۔ صاحبین کی دلیل کا حاصل یہ ہے کہ لفظ از اوقت کے معنی میں مستعمل ہے۔ کیونکہ اللہ تعالیٰ کے ارشاد و اذا الشمس كورت میں لفظ از اوقت کیلئے ۔ ترجمہ ہو گا۔ جس وقت آفتاب بے نور ہو جائے گا۔ اور ایسے ہی ایک شاعر کا شعر ہے:
واذا تكون كريهة أدعى لها واذا يحاس الحيس يُدعى جندب اور جس وقت کوئی ناگوار چیز پائی جائے تو اس کیلئے میں بلایا جاتا ہوں اور جب حلوا ما نڈ تیار کیا جائے تو جندب کو بلایا جاتا ہے“ اس شعر میں لفظ اذا دو جگہ ہے اور دونوں جگہ وقت کیلئے ہے نہ کہ شرط کیلئے کیونکہ اگر شرط کیلئے ہوتا تو تکون اور یحاس دونوں شرط کی وجہ سے مجزوم ہوتے یعنی لکن اور بےحس ہوتے ،مگر شاعر نے دونوں افعال کو غیر مجزوم استعمال کیا ہے۔ جس سے معلوم ہوتا ہے کہ اذا دونوں جگہ شرط کیلئے نہیں بلکہ وقت کیلئے ہے۔ پس جب لفظ اذا وقت کیلئے ہے تو یہ لفظ اذا متی اور متی ما کے مرتبہ میں ہو گیا۔ اور چونکہ لفظ اذا متی کے معنی میں ہے اسی وجہ سے اگر کسی شخص نے اپنی بیوی سے کہا انت طالق اذا شئت تو اس صورت میں عورت کا اختیار قیام عن المجلس کی وجہ سے ختم نہیں ہوتا۔ پس اس سے بھی معلوم ہوا کہ لفظ اذا متی کے معنی میں ہے۔ لہذا جو حکم متی کا ہے وہی لفظ اذا کا ہوگا۔ اور متی کا حکم پہلے مسئلہ میں گذر چکا کہ سکوت کے فورا بعد طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی ۔ لہذا اذا کی صورت میں بھی سکوت کے فورا بعد طلاق واقع ہوگی نہ کہ عمر کے آخری لمحہ میں۔ اور امام ابو حنیفہ کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ لفظ اذا، وقت کے علاوہ شرط کے معنی میں بھی مستعمل ہے۔ صاحب ہدایہ نے استدال میں شعر
پیش کیا ہے:
و استغن ما اغناک ربک بالغنی
و اذا تصبك خصاصة فتجمل
” بے پرواہی رکھ جب تک کہ تجھ کو تیرے رب نے فنی بنایا ہے مالداری کے ساتھ ۔ اور اگر تجھ کو تنگدستی لاحق ہو تو تو صبر جمیل اختیار کر اس شعر میں اذا شرط کیلئے ہے اس لئے کہ تصبک مجزوم ہے۔ اگر اذا شرطیہ نہ ہوتا تو تضبک یاب کے ساتھ ہونا چاہئے تھا۔ حاصل یہ کہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک اذا شرط کیلئے بھی آتا ہے۔ جیسا کہ ابھی معلوم ہوا۔ اور ظرف اور وقت کیلئے بھی آتا ہے۔ جیسا کہ صاحبین کی دلیل کے ذیل میں معلوم ہوا ۔ پس اگر انت طالق اذا لم اطلقک یا اذا مالم اطلقک میں اذا۔ سے شرط کے معنی مراد لیئے جائیں تو فی الحال طلاق واقع نہیں ہو گی۔ جیسا کہ لفظ ان کی صورت میں اور اگر اذا کو وقت کیلئے مانا جائے تو فی الحال طلاق واقع ہونی چاہئے ۔ جیسا کہ لفظ متی کی صورت میں۔ خلاصہ یہ کہ وقوع طلاق میں شک ہو گیا۔ اور شک کی وجہ سے طلاق واقع نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ اسلئے ہم کہتے ہیں کہ یہاں فی الحال طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی۔ اور مسئلہ مشیت اس کے برعکس ہے۔ کیونکہ انت طالق اذا شئت میں اگر اذا کو وقت کیلئے مانا گیا تو عورت کا اختیارختم نہیں ہوگا۔ بلکہ باقی رہے گا۔ جیسا کہ انت طالق متی شمت میں قیام عن امجلس کے باوجود عورت کا اختیار
باقی رہتا ہے۔ اور اگر لفظ اذا کو شرط کیلئے مانا جائے تو عورت کا اختیار قیام عن انلس سے ختم ہو جائے گا۔
حاصل یہ کہ ایک احتمال کی وجہ سے اختیار عورت کے ہاتھ سے نکل جائے گا۔ اور ایک احتمال کی وجہ سے نہیں نکلے گا۔ اور اختیار عورت کے ہاتھ میں بالیقین ہے۔ لہذا شک اور احتمال کی وجہ سے نہیں نکلے گا مطلب یہ کہ اختیار کا عورت کے ہاتھ سے نہ نکلنا اسلئے نہیں کہ از امتی کے معنی میں ہے۔ جیسا کہ صاحبین نے کہا بلکہ حقیقت یہ ہے کہ اذا کے معنی میں چونکہ شک واقع ہو گیا۔ اور شک کی وجہ سے یقینی چیز زائل نے ہےکہ اذا واقع او کی وجہسے نہیں ہوتی ۔ اسلئے اختیار جو عورت کے ہاتھ میں بالیقین ہے شک کی وجہ سے نہیں نکلے گا۔
صاحب ہدایہ فرماتے ہیں کہ امام صاحب اور صاحبین کے درمیان یہ اختلاف اس وقت ہے جبکہ شوہر نے اپنے کلام سے کوئی نیت نہیں کی ہے۔ لیکن اگر اس نے لفظ اذا سے وقت کی نیت کی ہے تو طلاق فی الحال واقع ہو جائے گی ۔ اور اگر شرط کی نیت کی ہے تو آخر عمر میں واقع ہوگی۔ کیونکہ لفظ از ادونوں کا احتمال رکھتا ہے۔
فوائد لفظ اذا کے بارے میں اصل اختلاف اہل لغت اور اہل نحو کا ہے۔ اہل کوفہ کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ اذا شرط کیلئے بھی استعمال کیا جاتا ہے۔ اور وقت کیلئے بھی دونوں برابر ہیں۔ اور اہل بصرہ کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ وقت کیلئے حقیقت ہے اور شرط کیلئے مجاز ۔ امام صاحب نے اہل کوفہ کے مذہب کو اختیار کیا ہے۔ اور صاحبین نے اہل بصرہ کے مذہب کو ترجیح دی ہے۔ واللہ اعلم
And near to [the view of] the Sahibayn, they said that the divorcée will become divorced at the time the husband remained silent. Because the word 'idha' is for time. Allah the Exalted said: 'When the sun is darkened' (Quran 81:1). And a poet said: 'And when a calamity occurs, I am summoned for it, and when 'hays' is prepared, Jundub is summoned.' So it became similar to 'mata' and 'mata ma' (words for 'when'). And for this reason, if he said to his wife 'You are divorced when you wish' (anta taliq idha shi't), then the option will not leave the woman's hand due to standing from the gathering, just as in his saying 'mata shi't'. And the proof of Abu Hanifa is that the word 'idha' is also used for condition. Someone said: 'Be unconcerned as long as your Lord enriches you with wealth, and if (idha) poverty afflicts you, then exercise beautiful patience.' So if by it he intended condition, then divorce does not occur immediately; and if by it he intended time, then divorce occurs immediately. So due to doubt and probability, divorce does not fall. Contrary to the issue of 'mashi'ah' (will). Because considering that the word 'idha' is for time, the option will not leave the woman's hand; and considering that it is for condition, the option will leave her hand. And the matter of divorce is (certainly) in the woman's hand. So it will not leave due to doubt and probability. And the disagreement is in the case when the husband has no intention. Nevertheless, when he intended time, divorce occurs immediately; and if he intended condition, it occurs at the end of life, because the word carries both probabilities. Elaboration of the issue: If a man said to his wife 'You are divorced when I do not divorce you' (anta taliq idha lam utalliqka) or 'when I have not divorced you' (idha ma lam utalliqka), then there is disagreement regarding the time of occurrence of divorce. Thus Imam Abu Hanifa says that divorce will occur near the time of death a little before. And the Sahibayn say that as soon as he becomes silent, divorce occurs. The summary of the Sahibayn's proof is that the word 'idha' is used in the meaning of time. Because Allah's saying 'wa idha al-shamsu kuwirat' — the word 'idha' is for time; the translation would be 'when the sun is darkened.' And similarly a poet's verse: 'Wa idha takunu karihatun ud'a laha wa idha yuhasu al-haysu yud'a Jundub' — 'And when a calamity occurs, I am summoned for it, and when 'hays' is prepared, Jundub is summoned.' In this verse, the word 'idha' appears twice and in both places it is for time, not for condition, because if it were for condition, then 'takun' and 'yuhas' would be in the jussive mood due to the condition, but the poet used both verbs in the indicative (non-jussive). This indicates that 'idha' in both places is not for condition but for time. So when the word 'idha' is for time, it becomes similar to 'mata' and 'mata ma'. And because the word 'idha' is in the meaning of 'mata', therefore if a person said to his wife 'anta taliq idha shi't', then in that case the woman's option does not terminate due to her standing from the gathering. Thus it is also known that the word 'idha' is in the meaning of 'mata'. Hence the same ruling that applies to 'mata' applies to the word 'idha'. And the ruling of 'mata' has passed in the previous issue: that immediately after silence, divorce occurs. Therefore, in the case of 'idha', also immediately after silence divorce occurs, not at the last moment of life. And Imam Abu Hanifa's proof is that the word 'idha' is also used in the meaning of condition besides time. The author of al-Hidayah presented a verse in argument: 'Wa istaghni ma aghnaka rabbuka bi al-ghina, wa idha tusibka khasasatun fa tajammal' — 'Be unconcerned as long as your Lord enriches you with wealth, and if (idha) poverty afflicts you, then exercise beautiful patience.' In this verse, 'idha' is for condition because 'tusibka' is in the jussive. If 'idha' were not conditional, 'tusibka' would have been with 'ya'. Conclusion: According to Imam (Abu Hanifa), 'idha' is used for condition as well, as just learned, and it is also used for time/context, as learned under the Sahibayn's proof. So if in 'anta taliq idha lam utalliqka' or 'idha ma lam utalliqka', the meaning of condition is intended from 'idha', then divorce does not occur immediately, as in the case of the word 'in'. And if 'idha' is considered for time, then divorce should occur immediately, as in the case of the word 'mata'. Summary: A doubt arose regarding the occurrence of divorce, and due to doubt, divorce does not occur. Therefore we say that here divorce does not occur immediately. And the issue of 'mashi'ah' (will) is opposite to this. Because in 'anta taliq idha shi't', if 'idha' is considered for time, then the woman's option will not terminate but will remain, just as in 'anta taliq mata shi't' the woman's option remains despite standing from the gathering. And if the word 'idha' is considered for condition, then the woman's option will terminate by standing from the gathering. Conclusion: due to one probability, option will leave her hand, and due to another probability, it will not leave. And the option is certainly in the woman's hand. Therefore, due to doubt and probability, it will not leave. Meaning: The non-removal of option from her hand is not because 'idha' is in the meaning of 'mata' as the Sahibayn said, but the reality is that since doubt occurred regarding the meaning of 'idha', and due to doubt a certain thing does not cease, therefore the option which is certainly in the woman's hand will not leave due to doubt. The author of al-Hidayah says: This disagreement between Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn is when the husband did not intend anything by his utterance. However, if he intended time by the word 'idha', then divorce occurs immediately; and if he intended condition, then it occurs at the end of life, because the word carries both probabilities. Benefit: The original disagreement about the word 'idha' is among lexicographers and grammarians. The Kufan school holds that 'idha' is used for condition and for time, both equally. The Basran school holds that it is real (haqiqah) for time and figurative (majaz) for condition. Imam Abu Hanifa adopted the Kufan school, and the Sahibayn gave preference to the Basran school. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 264

Commentary
This passage discusses the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the word 'idha' in divorce formulas. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani) argue that 'idha' always indicates time, like 'mata' (when), so when a husband says 'You are divorced if/when I do not divorce you' and then remains silent, divorce occurs immediately upon his silence. Their proof includes the Quranic verse 'When the sun is darkened' where 'idha' refers to a future time, and a line of poetry where 'idha' is used for time, as indicated by the non-jussive verbs. Abu Hanifa, however, argues that 'idha' can also indicate condition, like 'in' (if). He cites a verse where 'idha' governs a jussive verb, showing conditional meaning. Because 'idha' can mean either, if the husband has no specific intention, there is doubt (shakk) as to whether he meant time or condition, and divorce is not established by doubt. Therefore, divorce does not occur immediately upon silence; rather, it occurs at the end of life (i.e., near death) if he meant condition, and immediately if he meant time. The author clarifies that this dispute applies only when the husband has no explicit intention (niyyah). If he intends time, divorce occurs immediately; if condition, at death's approach. The passage also notes the underlying grammatical difference between the Kufan and Basran schools, with Abu Hanifa following the Kufan view that 'idha' is equally used for time and condition, while the Sahibayn follow the Basran view that it is primarily for time and only figuratively for condition.

Key Terms
اذا (idha): This passage discusses whether idha indicates time (like 'mata', 'when') or condition (like 'in', 'if') in the context of divorce.
متی (mata): A word meaning 'when' that clearly indicates time, used as a comparison point for idha.
شک (shakk): Doubt about the meaning of idha leads to non-occurrence of divorce, as certainty is required for divorce to take effect.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when does divorce occur if a husband says 'anta taliq idha lam utalliqka' without any intention, following the Sahibayn's view?
A) Immediately upon his silence.
B) Near the end of his life.
C) Not at all because the condition is unfulfilled.
D) Only if he repeats the phrase.

Key Takeaway
The word 'idha' is ambiguous in Arabic, and that ambiguity, when coupled with no intention, creates doubt; and in Hanafi law, doubt prevents the immediate occurrence of divorce.

Talaq — Divorce
advanced
8 min
The Ruling on 'Anta Taliq ma lam utalliqka anta taliq'
Explains the ruling on a specific divorce wording with an exception via istihsan.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the istihsan exception to conditional divorce pronouncements and state the resulting number of divorces.

Core Idea
The second 'anta taliq' is excepted by context; only one divorce occurs despite the wording.

This passage from al-Hidayah discusses a tricky divorce wording. The husband says 'You are divorced as long as I have not divorced you; you are divorced.' The literal wording suggests two divorces, but the Hanafi school uses istihsan to rule that only one divorce takes place. We will examine the qiyas argument and the istihsan resolution.

Guided Path
1
Identify the divorce wording and its apparent meaning
The husband says 'anta taliq ma lam utalliqka anta taliq' in one connected sentence. Literally, it seems to pronounce two divorces: one conditional on not having divorced her, and one unconditional.
The phrase 'ma lam utalliqka' functions as a condition.
2
Understand Zufar's qiyas argument
Zufar argues by qiyas that both pronouncements should occur because there is a moment (the time before uttering the second 'anta taliq') when the condition 'he had not divorced her' was true, making the first conditional divorce effective, and the second unconditional divorce also effective.
Qiyas would lead to two divorces for a wife with whom cohabitation occurred.
3
Recognize the istihsan basis
Istihsan overrides qiyas here: the time of uttering the second 'anta taliq' is excepted from the condition by contextual indication (dalalat al-hal). The husband's intention is to confirm the first divorce, not to add another—similar to a man who swears 'I will not reside in this house' while he is already in it; the moment of utterance is excepted.
The goal (bar) of the wording is to affirm the first divorce, which cannot be achieved without this exception.
4
Apply the istihsan to reach the Hanafi ruling
Thus the second 'anta taliq' does not count as a separate divorce; only one divorce occurs. This is the mufta bihi (operative) position.
The Hanafi majority adopts istihsan; Zufar's qiyas is set aside.

و لو قال انت طالق مالم اطلقك انت طالق فهي طالق بهذه التطليقة معناه قال ذلک موصولا به والقياس ان يقع المضاف فيقعان ان كانت مدخولابها وهو قول زفر لانه وجد زمان لم يطلقها فيه وان قل وهو زمان قوله انت طالق قبل ان يفرغ منها وجه الاستحسان ان زمان البرمستثنى عن اليمين بدلالة الحال لان البرهو المقصود ولا يمكنه تحقق البر الا ان يجعل هذا القدر مستثنى واصله من حلف لا يسكن هذا الدار
And if he said: 'You are divorced as long as I have not divorced you; you are divorced' – then she is divorced by this divorce. Meaning: he said that connectedly. And by analogy (qiyas), the added (second pronouncement) would occur, so both occur if she is one with whom cohabitation occurred. This is the statement of Zufar, because a time existed in which he did not divorce her, albeit a little, and that is the time of his saying 'you are divorced' before he finishes it. The basis of istihsan is that the time of the [؟] is excepted from the oath by contextual indication, because the [؟] is the intended [؟], and it is not possible for him to achieve [؟] unless this amount is made an exception. Its origin is from one who swore: 'I will not reside in this house.'
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage discusses the ruling when a husband says: 'You are divorced as long as I have not divorced you; you are divorced' (anta taliq ma lam utalliqka anta taliq). The husband connects the two phrases. According to Zufar (a Hanafi jurist), by analogy (qiyas), both pronouncements would be effective: the first 'anta taliq' conditional on not having divorced her, and the second 'anta taliq' unconditional, so she is divorced twice. But istihsan (juristic preference) here dictates that the time of uttering the second 'anta taliq' is excepted from the condition. Why? Because the context indicates that the husband's intention is to confirm the first conditional divorce, not to add a second divorce. He is saying: 'You are divorced by this divorce that I am uttering now, during the time I am saying it.' The original model is a man who swears 'I will not reside in this house' – if he says 'I will not reside in this house' while he is already in the house, the time of his utterance is excepted. So similarly, the moment of the second 'anta taliq' is not counted as a time when he did not divorce her, because he is divorcing her at that very moment. The passage is incomplete, but the ruling is that the second 'anta taliq' does not cause a second divorce; rather, it emphasizes the first. The authority weight is not fully clear, but it seems to be from the later discussions in al-Hidayah.

Key Terms
انت طالق مالم اطلقك انت طالق (anta taliq ma lam utalliqka anta taliq): A specific divorce wording: 'You are divorced as long as I have not divorced you; you are divorced.'
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that overrides qiyas due to contextual indication and necessity.
بر (bar): Fulfillment of the oath or statement; achieving the intended goal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the istihsan mentioned, what is the effect of the second 'anta taliq' in 'anta taliq ma lam utalliqka anta taliq'?
A) It adds a second divorce.
B) It is excepted and does not count as a separate divorce.
C) It invalidates the first divorce.
D) It makes the divorce conditional on something else.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, contextual indication (dalalat al-hal) can override literal qiyas, resulting in a single divorce for conditional wordings like 'anta taliq ma lam utalliqka anta taliq'.

Dispute on the Word Idha in Suspended Talaq
Intra-Hanafi dispute on idha in suspended talaq and mashiyyah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on the ambiguity of 'idha' in suspended talaq and explain how doubt preserves the wife's option or non-occurrence of talaq.

Core Idea
Doubt in the meaning of 'idha' prevents talaq from occurring immediately, preserving certainty.

In this lesson, we explore an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and his two distinguished students, Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani. The dispute revolves around the Arabic word 'idha' when used in suspended talaq formulas. Is 'idha' a conditional particle like 'in', or a temporal particle like 'mata'? The answer determines whether talaq occurs immediately or only upon a future condition. This seemingly linguistic nuance has real fiqh consequences, as we will see.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed word and its usage
Locate the word 'idha' in the phrases 'anti taliq idha lam utalliqki' and 'anti taliq idha shi'ti'. Recognize that the dispute concerns the linguistic category of 'idha' – whether it indicates a condition (shart) or time (zaman).
The same word appears in both talaq and mashiyyah contexts.
2
State the positions of Imam Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn
Imam Abu Hanifa, following the Kufan school of grammar, holds that 'idha' is used equally for condition and time. The Sahibayn, following the Basran school, hold that 'idha' is primarily for time. This leads to different rulings.
The disagreement is rooted in linguistics, not fiqh principles.
3
Apply the positions to the talaq case
If 'idha' indicates condition, talaq does not occur immediately (like 'in'). If it indicates time, talaq occurs immediately (like 'mata'). Due to ambiguity, the Hanafi position is that talaq is not immediate.
The principle 'al-yaqin la yazulu bi al-shakk' is applied: certainty (non-occurrence) is not removed by doubt.
4
Apply the positions to the mashiyyah case
In 'anti taliq idha shi'ti', if 'idha' is temporal, the wife's option continues even after leaving the assembly. If conditional, the option ends upon leaving. Again, doubt preserves the status quo (option remains).
This shows consistency: doubt favours the existing certainty.
5
Note the role of intention
The author of Hidayah clarifies that the dispute applies only when the husband has no specific intention. If he intends time, talaq is immediate; if condition, it is delayed. Intention resolves the ambiguity.
This is a practical resolution for actual cases.

Source Text

اشرف الہدایہ شرح اردو ہدایہ جلد چہارم
و استغن ما اغناک ربک بالغنی
و اذا تصبك خصاصة فتجمل
” بے پرواہی رکھ جب تک کہ تجھ کو تیرے رب نے فنی بنایا ہے مالداری کے ساتھ ۔ اور اگر تجھ کو تنگدستی لاحق ہو تو تو صبر جمیل اختیار کر اس شعر میں اذا شرط کیلئے ہے اس لئے کہ تصبک مجزوم ہے۔ اگر اذا شرطیہ نہ ہوتا تو تضبک یاب کے ساتھ ہونا چاہئے تھا۔ حاصل یہ کہ امام صاحب کے نزدیک اذا شرط کیلئے بھی آتا ہے۔ جیسا کہ ابھی معلوم ہوا۔ اور ظرف اور وقت کیلئے بھی آتا ہے۔ جیسا کہ صاحبین کی دلیل کے ذیل میں معلوم ہوا ۔ پس اگر انت طالق اذا لم اطلقک یا اذا مالم اطلقک میں اذا۔ سے شرط کے معنی مراد لیئے جائیں تو فی الحال طلاق واقع نہیں ہو گی۔ جیسا کہ لفظ ان کی صورت میں اور اگر اذا کو وقت کیلئے مانا جائے تو فی الحال طلاق واقع ہونی چاہئے ۔ جیسا کہ لفظ متی کی صورت میں۔ خلاصہ یہ کہ وقوع طلاق میں شک ہو گیا۔ اور شک کی وجہ سے طلاق واقع نہیں ہوتی ہے۔ اسلئے ہم کہتے ہیں کہ یہاں فی الحال طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی۔ اور مسئلہ مشیت اس کے برعکس ہے۔ کیونکہ انت طالق اذا شئت میں اگر اذا کو وقت کیلئے مانا گیا تو عورت کا اختیارختم نہیں ہوگا۔ بلکہ باقی رہے گا۔ جیسا کہ انت طالق متی شمت میں قیام عن امجلس کے باوجود عورت کا اختیار باقی رہتا ہے۔ اور اگر لفظ اذا کو شرط کیلئے مانا جائے تو عورت کا اختیار قیام عن انلس سے ختم ہو جائے گا۔ حاصل یہ کہ ایک احتمال کی وجہ سے اختیار عورت کے ہاتھ سے نکل جائے گا۔ اور ایک احتمال کی وجہ سے نہیں نکلے گا۔ اور اختیار عورت کے ہاتھ میں بالیقین ہے۔ لہذا شک اور احتمال کی وجہ سے نہیں نکلے گا مطلب یہ کہ اختیار کا عورت کے ہاتھ سے نہ نکلنا اسلئے نہیں کہ از امتی کے معنی میں ہے۔ جیسا کہ صاحبین نے کہا بلکہ حقیقت
