اگر شرط کی نیت کی ہے تو آخر عمر میں واقع ہوگی۔ کیونکہ لفظ از ادونوں کا احتمال رکھتا ہے۔ فوائد لفظ اذا کے بارے میں اصل اختلاف اہل لغت اور اہل نحو کا ہے۔ اہل کوفہ کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ اذا شرط کیلئے بھی استعمال کیا جاتا ہے۔ اور وقت کیلئے بھی دونوں برابر ہیں۔ اور اہل بصرہ کا مذہب یہ ہے کہ وقت کیلئے حقیقت ہے اور شرط کیلئے مجاز ۔ امام صاحب نے اہل کوفہ کے مذہب کو اختیار کیا ہے۔ اور صاحبین نے اہل بصرہ کے مذہب کو ترجیح دی ہے۔ واللہ اعلم
Book of Divorce. Presented: 264 Ashraf al-Hidaya Sharh Urdu Hidaya Volume Four. 'And be independent with what your Lord has given you of wealth, and if poverty afflicts you, then adopt beautiful patience.' In this verse, idha is for condition because tasbuk is in the jussive. If idha were not conditional, tasbuk would be with ya. The conclusion is that according to Imam Sahib, idha is used for condition as just learned, and also for time and occasion as learned under the Sahibayn's proof. So if in 'anti taliq idha lam utalliqki' or 'idha ma lam utalliqki' idha is taken to mean condition, then talaq does not occur immediately, as in the case of the word 'in'. And if idha is taken for time, then talaq should occur immediately, as in the case of the word 'mata'. In summary, doubt arises in the occurrence of talaq, and due to doubt, talaq does not occur. Therefore we say that here talaq does not occur immediately. And the issue of mashiyyah is contrary to this because in 'anti taliq idha shi'ti', if idha is taken for time, the wife's option does not end but remains, as in 'anti taliq mata shi'ti' even after leaving the assembly, the wife's option remains. And if idha is taken for condition, then the wife's option ends upon leaving the assembly. The conclusion is that due to one probability, the option would leave the wife's hand, and due to another, it would not. And the option is definitely in the wife's hand, so due to doubt and probability, it will not leave. The meaning is that the option not leaving the wife's hand is not because idha means 'mata' as the Sahibayn said, but the reality is that because doubt occurred in the meaning of idha, and due to doubt a certain thing is not removed, therefore the option which is definitely in the wife's hand will not leave due to doubt. The author of Hidaya says that this difference between Imam Sahib and the Sahibayn is when the husband did not have any intention from his speech. But if he intended time with idha, then talaq will occur immediately, and if he intended condition, it will occur at the end of life because idha has both probabilities. Benefits: The original difference about idha is among linguists and grammarians. The Kufan school holds that idha is used for condition and also for time, both equally. The Basran school holds that it is real for time and metaphorical for condition. Imam Sahib adopted the Kufan school, and the Sahibayn gave preference to the Basran school. And Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the word 'idha' when used in suspending talaq. The passage type is an intra-madhhab dispute between Imam Abu Hanifa and the two companions (Sahibayn: Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani). The core issue is whether 'idha' in phrases like 'anti taliq idha lam utalliqki' indicates a condition (like 'in') or a time (like 'mata').

Imam Abu Hanifa, following the Kufan grammarians, holds that 'idha' can be used for both condition and time equally. Therefore, if a husband uses 'idha' without specifying his intention, ambiguity arises. Because of this doubt, the ruling is that talaq does not occur immediately (since it might be conditional) and the wife's option (in the case of 'idha shi'ti') does not end upon leaving the assembly (since it might be time-based). The Sahibayn, following the Basran grammarians, hold that 'idha' is primarily for time, so it would cause immediate talaq and end the wife's option. However, the Hanafi position is that doubt prevents certainty, so the stronger probability (the wife's definite option or non-occurrence of talaq) prevails.

The author of Al-Hidayah, al-Marghinani, clarifies that this dispute applies only when the husband has no specific intention. If he intends time, talaq occurs immediately; if condition, at the end of the condition. This shows the importance of niyyah in resolving linguistic ambiguity. The underlying linguistic dispute between Kufan and Basran schools is also noted, with Imam Abu Hanifa adopting the Kufan view and the Sahibayn preferring the Basran view. This passage demonstrates how fiqh rulings can hinge on subtle linguistic principles and the prioritization of certainty over doubt (al-yaqin la yazulu bi al-shakk).

Key Terms
اذا (idha): A word that can indicate either a future condition (like 'in') or a future time (like 'mata'). The meaning is ambiguous without context or intention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
In the phrase 'anti taliq idha lam utalliqki', what is the Hanafi ruling (based on Imam Abu Hanifa's view) if the husband has no specific intention?
A) Talaq occurs immediately because idha indicates time.
B) Talaq does not occur immediately because idha is ambiguous.
C) Talaq occurs only if the wife leaves the house.
D) The wife has the option to divorce herself.

Key Takeaway
The ambiguity of the word 'idha' in suspended talaq prevents immediate occurrence of talaq, preserving the wife's option, unless the husband's intention clarifies the meaning.

Suspended Talaq: The Dispute Between Qiyas and Istihsan
Explains dispute between qiyas and istihsan

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi majority position on the suspended talaq formula 'anti taliq ma lam utalliqki anti taliq' and evaluate Imam Zufar's counter-argument based on qiyas.

Core Idea
The time to utter an oath is excepted from its condition — istihsan overrides strict qiyas.

This lesson examines a classic Hanafi dispute over a cunning talaq formula. When a husband says 'You are divorced as long as I have not divorced you, you are divorced,' does one divorce occur or two? The answer hinges on whether the brief moment of uttering the first part is considered a valid time of 'not divorcing.' The majority uses istihsan to prevent an unintended second divorce, while Imam Zufar insists on strict qiyas.

Guided Path
1
State the contested formula and the core question
Write down the exact Arabic phrase and identify the two potential talaq: the suspended one (attached to the condition) and the immediate second one. The core question is whether both occur or only one.
The phrase is spoken without pause — 'mawsulan bihi'.
2
Present Imam Zufar's qiyas argument
Identify the condition: there is a moment (the time to say the first six letters until 'lam') when the wife is not yet divorced. Therefore, the condition 'ma lam utalliqki' is met, triggering the suspended talaq. Thus two talaq occur if the wife is madkhul biha.
Zufar's reasoning is strict qiyas: if a condition is literally fulfilled, its consequence follows.
3
Present the majority's istihsan argument
The time needed to fulfill the oath is excepted by implication of the situation (dalalat al-hal). Without this exception, the husband could never fulfill his oath because as soon as he starts the first part, he violates it. Therefore, the suspended talaq does not occur; only the second explicit talaq takes effect.
This istihsan is based on the principle that the oath's intended purpose (fulfillment) must be possible.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
If the wife is madkhul biha, under Zufar's view two talaq occur; under the majority view only one. This affects the number of remaining revocable divorces the husband has.
The ruling is limited to cases where the wife is madkhul biha (non-virgin after consummation).
5
Note the tarjih and mufta bihi
The text clearly favors istihsan, which is the view of the majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) and is mufta bihi. Al-Marghinani presents it as the correct view.
The majority view is from Zahir al-Riwayah and is the relied-upon position for fatwa.

و لو قال انت طالق مالم اطلقك انت طالق فهي طالق بهذه التطليقة معناه قال ذلک موصولا به والقياس ان يقع المضاف فيقعان ان كانت مدخولابها وهو قول زفر لانه وجد زمان لم يطلقها فيه وان قل وهو زمان قوله انت طالق قبل ان يفرغ منها وجه الاستحسان ان زمان البرمستثنى عن اليمين بدلالة الحال لان البرهو المقصود ولا يمكنه تحقق البر الا ان يجعل هذا القدر مستثنى واصله من حلف لا يسكن هذا الدار فاشتغل بالنقلة من ساعته واخواته علی مایاتیک فی الایمان ان شاء الله تعالیٰ

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو بدا یه جلد چهارم
۲۶۵
فاشتغل بالنقلة من ساعته واخواته علی مایاتیک فی الایمان ان شاء الله تعالیٰ
کتاب الطلاق
ترجمہ اور اگر کہا کہ تو طلاق والی ہے جس وقت میں تجھ کو طلاق نہ دوں تو طلاق والی ہے تو یہ عورت اس طلاق دینے سے مطلقہ ہو گی۔ اس مسئلہ کی مراد یہ ہے کہ اس نے ( انت طالق ) اس کے ساتھ ملا کر کہا۔ اور قیاس یہ ہے کہ جو طلاق ( زمانہ کی ) طرف مضاف ہے وہ بھی واقع ہو جائے گی ۔ پس دونوں واقع ہوں گی۔ اگر ( وہ عورت ) مدخول بہا ہے۔ اور یہی قول ہے امام زفر کا۔ کیونکہ ایسا زمانہ پایا گیا جس میں اس نے اس عورت کو طلاق نہیں دی ہے اگر چہ کم ہے اور وہ زمانہ ہے اس کا قول انت طالق قبل اس کے کہ اس سے فارغ ہو ۔ اور وجہ استحسان یہ ہے کہ قسم پوری کرنے کا زمانہ دلالت حال کی وجہ سے یمین سے مستثنیٰ ہے۔ کیونکہ قسم پوری کرنا ہی مقصود یمین ہے۔ اور اس کیلئے قسم پوری کرنے کا متفق ہونا ممکن نہیں۔ مگر یہ کہ اتنی مقدار کو مستقلی قرار دے دیا جائے۔ اور اس اختلاف کی اصل وہ شخص ہے جس نے قسم کھائی کہ اس مکان میں نہیں رہے گا۔ پھر اسی وقت سامان منتقل کرنے میں لگ گیا۔ اور اس کے نظائر اسی تفصیل پر جو کتاب الایمان میں انشاء اللہ آئے گا۔
تشریح مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ اگر مرد نے اپنی منکوحہ سے کہا انت طالق مالم اطلقك انت طالق اور یہ بعد والا انت طالق کلام سابق کے ساتھ ملا کر کہا درمیان میں کوئی فصل نہیں کیا تو اس آخر والے انت طالق سے ایک طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی ۔ اور قیار کا متقاضا یہ ہے کہ جو طلاق مسالم اطلقک کی جانب منسوب کی گئی ہے وہ بھی واقع ہو جائے ۔ تو اب اس صورت میں دو طلاق واقع ہوں گی ۔ ایک وہ طلاق جو منسوب کی گئی ہے اور ایک اس سے جو بعد میں انت طالق ہے۔ مگر یہ کہ دو طلاقیں اس وقت واقع ہوں گی جبکہ عورت مدخول بہا ہو۔ امام زفر کا یہی قول ہے۔ امام زفر کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ انت طالق کو معلق کیا گیا ہے ایسے زمانے پر جو خالی عن التطبیق ہو ۔ اور وہ پایا گیا اگر چہ بہت کم ہے۔ تفصیل اس کی یہ ہے کہ انت طالق میں سات حروف ہیں جب تک مرد قاف تک تکلم نہیں کرے گا طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی ۔ چنانچہ اگر کسی نے لام تک تکلم کیا۔ اور خاموش ہو گیا تو طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی۔ اب اس مسئلہ میں جب مرد نے بعد والے انت طالق کا تلفظ کیا تو چھ حروف کے تلفظ تک یعنی لام کے تلفظ تک اتنا وقت پایا گیا کہ وہ خالی عن التطلیق ہے۔ پس شرط کے پائے جانے کی وجہ سے طلاق مضاف بھی واقع ہو جائے گی ۔ اور بعد والا انت طالق تو غیر معلق ہے لہذا ایک اس سے واقع ہو جائے گی۔ اسی طرح امام زفر فر ماتے ہیں کہ اس مسئلہ میں دو طلاقیں واقع ہوں گی۔
وجہ استحسان یہ ہے کہ قسم کھانے کے بعد اسکو اتنا وقت ضرور ملنا چاہئے جس میں حالف اپنی قسم کو پورا کر سکے۔ کیونکہ یمین سے ختم پورا کرنا ہی مقصود ہے۔ اور یہ اس وقت ممکن نہیں جب تک کہ اتنا وقت متنی قرار نہ دیا جائے۔ پس انت طالق مالم اطلقک کے بعد اتنا وقت مالنا چاہئے ۔ جس میں انت طالق کے ساتھ حروف کا تلفظ کر سکے۔ لام تک چھ حروف کے تلفظ کا وقت معتبر نہیں ۔ کیونکہ یہ وقت قسم پوری کرنے کیلئے نا کافی ہے۔ اور اس اختلاف کی اصل کتاب الایمان کا ایک مسئلہ ہے۔ مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک شخص نے قسم کھائی میں اس مکان میں نہیں رہوں گا۔ پھر اسی وقت اپنا سامان اس مکان سے منتقل کرنے میں مشغول ہو گیا تو اس صورت میں استحسانا حانث نہیں ہوگا۔ اور امام زفر کے نزدیک قیاساً حانث ہو جائے گا۔ اس مسئلہ کی اور بہت سی نظیریں ہیں جو کتاب الایمان میں بیان کی جائیں گی۔ انشاء اللہ واللہ اعلم ۔
And if he said: 'Anti taliq ma lam utalliqki anti taliq', then she is divorced with this divorce. Meaning he said that connected to it. And by qiyas, the added (talaq) would occur, so both would occur if she is a non-virgin who has been consummated. This is the saying of Zufar, because there is found a time in which he did not divorce her, even if little, and that time is the time of his saying 'anti taliq' before he finishes it. The basis of istihsan is that the time of fulfilling the oath is excepted from the oath by implication of the situation, because fulfilling the oath is the intended purpose, and he cannot achieve fulfillment unless this amount is made excepted. Its origin is from one who swore not to live in this house, then immediately engaged in moving his belongings, and its analogues according to what will come to you in the Book of Oaths, if Allah wills. (Urdu translation and commentary follow, explaining that only one talaq occurs by istihsan, while by qiyas two occur. The commentary details the reasoning of Zufar and the istihsan response.)
Source pages p. 265

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute concerning a specific formulation of suspended talaq. The husband says, 'Anti taliq ma lam utalliqki anti taliq' — 'You are divorced as long as I have not divorced you, you are divorced.' The phrase is spoken connectedly (without pause). The dispute is between Imam Zufar (using qiyas) and the majority view (using istihsan).

By qiyas (analogy), as held by Imam Zufar, two divorces would occur. His reasoning: In the first part 'anti taliq ma lam utalliqki', the talaq is suspended upon the condition of not divorcing. Since the husband then says 'anti taliq' immediately after, there is a very brief moment (the time it takes to say the first six letters until 'lam') during which he has not yet divorced her. Therefore, the condition is fulfilled (he did not divorce her during that moment), so the suspended talaq occurs. Then the second 'anti taliq' is an immediate divorce, so two talaq occur in total. This applies only if the wife is a non-virgin (madkhul biha).

By istihsan (juristic preference), the majority Hanafi view (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) holds that only one talaq occurs — from the second 'anti taliq'. The reason is that the time needed to complete the utterance of the oath (the first 'anti taliq ma lam utalliqki') is excepted from the oath. Since the very act of uttering the oath takes some minimal time, that time is not considered a valid period of 'not divorcing'. Without that exception, it would be impossible for the husband to fulfill his oath because as soon as he says the first part, he would immediately violate it. Therefore, the condition is not considered to have been fulfilled, and only the second explicit talaq takes effect.

The passage analogizes to a case from the Book of Oaths: if a man swears not to live in a house and immediately starts moving his belongings out, he is not considered to have lived in it for an instant (by istihsan), by qiyas he would be. This shows the principle that the time immediately necessary to fulfill the oath is excluded. So here, the husband's utterance of the suspension itself gives him the necessary time to fulfill the condition by saying the second 'anti taliq'.

In practice, the mufta bihi view is istihsan: only one talaq occurs. This protects against unintended multiple divorces due to linguistic technicalities.

Key Terms
استحسان (istihsan): Juristic preference that departs from strict qiyas in favor of a more equitable ruling, often based on custom, necessity, or implied exception.
قياس (qiyas): Analogical deduction that applies the ruling of an original case to a new case due to shared effective cause.
دلالة الحال (dalalat al-hal): Implication of the situation or context, used in Hanafi fiqh to infer legal rulings from circumstances without explicit textual indication.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the majority Hanafi view (istihsan) in the phrase 'anti taliq ma lam utalliqki anti taliq', how many divorces occur?
A) Two divorces, because the suspended one occurs during the brief utterance.
B) One divorce, because the time of utterance is excepted from the condition.
C) Three divorces, because the husband repeated 'taliq'.
D) No divorce, because the condition is impossible.

Key Takeaway
In the formula 'anti taliq ma lam utalliqki anti taliq', the Hanafi majority uses istihsan to rule that only one talaq occurs, excepting the utterance time from the condition.

Talaq — Divorce

Meaning of 'Yawm' in Conditional Divorce
Ruling on divorce contingent on 'day' of marriage and definition of 'yawm'.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rule distinguishing extended vs. non-extended actions to determine whether 'yawm' means daytime or absolute time in conditional divorce.

Core Idea
When used with a non-extended action like divorce, 'yawm' means absolute time, covering night and day.

In this lesson, we examine a classic Hanafi ruling on conditional divorce using the word 'yawm' (day). The author of Al-Hidayah explains that the meaning of 'yawm' depends on the verb it accompanies—whether the action is extended or not. We'll trace the linguistic and Quranic proof for this distinction.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditional divorce ruling
State the default ruling when a man says 'The day I marry you, you are divorced' and marries at night: the divorce occurs.
This is the core ruling being established.
2
Locate the dalil
Identify the Quranic proof: Surah al-Anfal (8:16) where 'yawma'idhin' means 'on that occasion'.
The verse is used to show that 'yawm' can denote absolute time.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the verse proves that 'yawm' is used for absolute time. The Quranic context refers to a specific moment, not the whole bright day.
This establishes the linguistic flexibility of 'yawm'.
4
Apply the distinction between extended and non-extended actions
If the verb is extended (e.g., fasting, woman's option), 'yawm' means bright part of the day. If non-extended (like divorce), it means absolute time. Divorce is a single utterance, thus non-extended.
This is the key tarjih mechanism.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومن قال لامرأة يوم اتزوجك فانت طالق فتزوجها ليلا طلقت لان اليوم يذكر ويراد به بياض النهار فيحمل عليه اذاقرن بفعل يمتد كالصوم والامر باليدلانه يراد به المعيار وهذا اليق به ويذكر ويراد به مطلق الوقت قال الله تعالى ومن يُولهم يومند دبره والمراد به مطلق الوقت فيحمل عليه اذا قرن بفعل لا يمتد و الطلاق من هذا القبيل فينتظم الليل والنهار ولو قال عنيت به بياض النهار خاصة دين فى القضاء لانه نوى حقيقة كلامه و الليل لايتناول الا السواد والنهار لا يتناول الا البياض خاصة وهو اللغة
And if someone said to a woman, 'The day I marry you, you are divorced,' and he married her at night, she is divorced because the word 'yawm' is [sometimes] mentioned and intended to mean the brightness of the day, so it is construed accordingly when paired with an extended action like fasting and the command [for a woman to choose], because it is intended as a measure, and this is more fitting for it. And [yawm] is mentioned and intended to mean absolute time; Allah said: 'And whoever turns his back to them on that day' and the intended meaning is absolute time. So it is construed accordingly when paired with a non-extended action, and divorce is of this category, so it includes night and day. And if he said, 'I intended by it only the brightness of the day,' it is accepted in court because he intended the literal meaning of his speech, and night only comprises darkness, and day only comprises brightness specifically, and that is the language.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage provides the ruling and linguistic reasoning for a conditional divorce using the word 'yawm' (day). If a man says to a woman, 'Yawma atazawwajuki fa-anti taliq' (the day I marry you, you are divorced), and he marries her at night, the divorce takes effect because 'yawm' can mean absolute time, not necessarily daytime. The author explains that 'yawm' is ambiguous: it can mean the bright part of the day (nahar) or absolute time (including night). Which meaning is applied depends on the verb it accompanies. If the verb is extended (mumtadd) like fasting or a woman's option in divorce, 'yawm' refers to daytime (the measure). If the verb is non-extended (ghayr mumtadd) like divorce itself, 'yawm' means absolute time, covering night and day. The Quranic evidence is verse 8:16, where 'yawma'idhin' means 'on that occasion,' not just daytime. The husband's subjective intention (niyyah) is upheld in judicial determination (qada'), but the default ruling is that the word operates broadly.

Key Terms
يوم (yawm): In this context, a word that can mean either the bright part of the day (nahar) or absolute time (including night), depending on the verb it accompanies.
نهار (nahar): The bright part of the day from sunrise to sunset.
ليل (layl): The night, from sunset to sunrise, comprising darkness.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a man says 'yawma atazawwajuki fa-anti taliq' and marries at night, why does the divorce occur?
A) Because 'yawm' always means the complete 24-hour day.
B) Because divorce is a non-extended action, so 'yawm' is taken as absolute time.
C) Because the husband must have intended absolute time.
D) Because night is included in 'yawm' by default without any condition.

Key Takeaway
When used with a non-extended action like divorce, 'yawm' means absolute time, so the condition is fulfilled even at night.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
15 min
Yawm in Conditional Divorce: Including Night by Linguistic Principle
Ruling with proof using linguistic and Quranic evidence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to STATE the Hanafi ruling on conditional divorce using 'yawm' and EXPLAIN how the linguistic principle of qarina (context) determines whether 'yawm' includes night.

Core Idea
In conditional divorce, 'yawm' includes night when the condition is a non-extended act — context decides meaning.

When a husband says 'On the day I marry you, you are divorced,' does marrying at night trigger the divorce? The Hanafi school rules yes. This lesson unpacks the ruling and its proof, grounded in a sophisticated linguistic principle from usul al-fiqh. Understanding this principle is essential for correctly interpreting conditional statements in Islamic law.

Guided Path
1
State the Ruling
Identify the exact conditional statement and note that the divorce occurs if marriage happens at night. The ruling is that divorce takes effect immediately upon marriage at night.
2
Understand the Ambiguity of 'Yawm'
The word 'yawm' has two possible meanings: the whiteness of the day (daylight) or absolute time (including night). Recognize that context determines which meaning is intended.
3
Apply the Qarina Principle
If 'yawm' is linked to an extended act (fiʿl mumtadd, e.g., fasting), it means daylight as a measure. If linked to a non-extended act (e.g., divorce), it means absolute time. Classify divorce as non-extended.
4
Find the Quranic Evidence
The verse 'And whoever turns his back to them on that day...' (Surah Anfal 8:16) uses 'yawm' for absolute time, supporting the interpretation for non-extended acts.
The verse uses 'yawm' for a moment of battle, not a full day.
5
Note the Exception for Intention
If the husband explicitly intended only daylight, his intention is accepted in court, so divorce would not occur if marriage at night.
This is because he intends the literal meaning of his speech.

ترجمہ جس شخص نے ایک عورت سے کہا جس دن میں تجھے سے نکاح کروں تو طلاق والی ہے۔ پھر اس سے رات میں نکاح کر لیا تو طلاق ہو جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ یوم مذکور ہوتا ہے اور اس سے مراد بیاض نہار ہوتا ہے۔ لہذا (یوم) کو کلام کی نیت کی ہے۔ اور رات شامل نہیں مگر سیاہی کو اور نہار شامل نہیں ہو گا مگر سفیدی کو بالخصوص اور یہی لغت ہے۔ تشریح مسئلہ ایک شخص نے کسی عورت سے یوم اتز و جک فانت طالق کہا۔ پھر اس عورت سے رات میں ہے کہ لفظ یوم مغل نمند کے ساتھ مقارن ہوگا یا فعل غیر متد کے ساتھ ۔ اگر فعل ممتد کے ساتھ مقارن ہے تو یوم سے مراد بیاض نہار ہوگا۔ فعل ممتد سے مراد یہ ہے کہ اس فعل کے کرنے میں کچھ مدت لگتی ہو۔ مثلا روزہ عورت کا طلاق میں اختیار، پہننا ، سواری کرنا سکونت کرنا وغیرہ۔ بہر حال اس صورت میں یوم سے مراد بیاض نہار اسلئے ہوگا کہ یوم سے مراد معیار ہے اور بیاض نہار معیار بننے کے زیادہ لائق ہے۔ اور معیار سے مراد یہ ہے کہ وہ بقدر فعل مقدر ہو۔ مثلاً یوم میں روزہ تو یوم روزہ کیلئے معیار ہوگا۔
اور اگر لفظ یوم فعل غیر ممتد کے ساتھ مقارن ہو تو یوم سے مراد مطلق وقت ہوگا۔ جیسا کہ آیت میں یو منذ سے مراد مطلق وقت ہے۔ فعل غیر ممتد سے مراد یہ ہے کہ اس فعل میں وقت مدید کی ضرورت نہیں ہے۔ بلکہ مطلق وقت اس کیلئے کافی ہے۔ اور طلاق بھی فعل غیر ممتد کے قبیلہ سے ہے۔ لہذا یوم اتز و جک فانت طالق میں لفظ یوم رات و دن کو شامل ہوگا۔ رات و دن میں جب بھی نکاح کرے گا طلاق ہو جائیگی ۔ البتہ اس کلام میں اگر مرد نے بالخصوص بیاض نہار کی نیت کی ہے۔ تو قصاً تصدیق کی جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ اس شخص نے حقیقت کلام کی ثیت کی ہے۔ زیادہ تفصیل اصول فقہ کی کتابوں میں ہے۔ اس کا مطالعہ کر لیا جائے۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب
And whoever says to a woman, 'On the day I marry you, you are divorced,' then he marries her at night, she is divorced. Because the word 'yawm' is mentioned and by it is meant the whiteness of the day (daylight). So it is interpreted as daylight when it is connected to an extended act like fasting and [the woman's] option, because by it is meant the measure, and daylight is more suitable for that. And it is mentioned and by it is meant absolute time. Allah Most High said: 'And whoever turns his back to them on that day...' and by it is meant absolute time. So it is interpreted as absolute time when it is connected to a non-extended act. And divorce is of this category, so it includes night and day. And if he said, 'I intended only the whiteness of the day (daylight),' it is believed in the court because he intends the reality of his speech. And night includes only darkness and day includes only whiteness, and that is the language. Translation: A person who said to a woman, 'On the day I marry you, you are divorced,' then he married her at night, divorce will occur. Because 'yawm' is mentioned and its meaning is daylight. Therefore, 'yawm' is taken to mean daylight when it is accompanied by an extended act, like fasting and the woman's option. Because by it is meant the measure, and daylight is more suitable for that. And 'yawm' is also mentioned and by it is meant absolute time. Allah Most High said: 'Whoever turns his back to them on that day...' and by it is meant absolute time. So 'yawm' is taken to mean absolute time when it is accompanied by a non-extended act. And divorce is of this category, so it includes night and day. And if he said, 'I intended only daylight,' it is believed in the court because he intends the reality of his speech. And night includes only darkness and day includes only whiteness, and that is the language. Explanation: The issue: A person said to a woman, 'On the day I marry you, you are divorced.' Then he married her at night, divorce will occur. The evidence for this issue is related to a principles discussion. First, note that three words are mentioned: nahaar (daylight), layl (night), yawm (day). 'Nahaar' applies specifically from sunrise to sunset. 'Layl' applies to darkness, i.e., from sunset to dawn. As for the word 'yawm', some opine that it is shared between daylight and absolute time. Most opine that it is literal for daylight and metaphorical for absolute time. In both cases, 'yawm' is a container. One of the two probabilities is given preference due to a qarina (contextual clue). The qarina is a principle: If the word 'yawm' is accompanied by an extended act, then by 'yawm' is meant daylight. An extended act is one that takes some duration, like fasting, the woman's option in divorce, wearing, riding, dwelling, etc. In this case, 'yawm' means daylight because by 'yawm' is meant the measure, and daylight is more suited to be a measure. And by 'measure' is meant that it is commensurate with the act. For example, fasting in a day: the day is the measure for the fast. And if the word 'yawm' is accompanied by a non-extended act, then by 'yawm' is meant absolute time, as in the verse 'on that day' meaning absolute time. A non-extended act is one that does not require a long time; rather, absolute time is sufficient for it. And divorce is of the type of non-extended act. Therefore, in 'On the day I marry you, you are divorced,' the word 'yawm' includes both night and day. Whenever he marries, divorce will occur. However, if the man specifically intended daylight, then in the court it is believed because he intended the reality of his speech. More detail is in the books of usul al-fiqh. It should be studied. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 267

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement followed by a detailed proof. The ruling: If a man says to a woman, 'On the day I marry you, you are divorced,' and then he marries her at night, the divorce occurs. The proof relies on a linguistic principle from usul al-fiqh: the word 'yawm' (day) has two possible meanings—daylight (whiteness of the day) or absolute time (including night). The correct meaning is determined by the nature of the act it is linked to. If the act is extended (e.g., fasting, which takes the whole daylight period), then 'yawm' means daylight because it serves as a measure for the act. If the act is non-extended (e.g., divorce, which is instantaneous), then 'yawm' means absolute time, including both day and night. The Quranic verse (Surah Anfal 8:16) is cited as evidence where 'yawm' means absolute time. Thus, for a conditional divorce, 'yawm' includes night, so marriage at night triggers the divorce. However, if the husband explicitly intended only daylight, his intention is accepted in the court because he is acting on the literal meaning of his word. The commentary emphasizes that this is a principle of linguistic interpretation. The author then gives an Urdu explanation reinforcing the same points: the three terms nahaar, layl, yawm; the shared or metaphorical nature of yawm; and the qarina principle. The ruling is clear: unless the husband specifies daytime, divorce occurs even at night.

Key Terms
یوم (yawm): In this text, 'yawm' is ambiguous between daylight and absolute time; its meaning is determined by the qarina (context).
فعل ممتد (fiʿl mumtadd): An act that requires a continuous duration, like fasting or wearing clothes.
قرینہ (qarīna): A contextual clue that determines which meaning of an ambiguous word is intended.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, if a man says 'On the day I marry you, you are divorced' and marries at night, does divorce occur?
A) No, because night is not considered 'yawm'.
B) Yes, because 'yawm' includes night when linked to a non-extended act like divorce.
C) Only if the husband intended night as well.
D) No, unless the husband specifies daytime.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, 'yawm' in a conditional divorce includes night when the condition involves a non-extended act, according to the qarina principle.

Talaq — Divorce

When 'I Am Divorced from You' Does Not Count as Divorce
Ruling on the phrase 'Ana minki taliq' and the dispute with Shafi'i

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the phrase 'Ana minki taliq' and explain why it differs from the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
The phrase 'I am divorced from you' effects no divorce because divorce removes a restriction exclusive to the wife.

This lesson examines a common misconception: that any phrase indicating separation with divorce intention constitutes a valid divorce. The Hanafi school draws a careful linguistic and legal distinction based on the nature of the restriction being removed. Understanding this distinction is critical for correct fatwa and for appreciating how legal theory (usul) shapes fiqh rulings.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify the ruling for 'Ana minki taliq', 'Ana minki bain', and 'Alayki haram' as given in the text.
Note the contrast: taliq is ineffective; bain and haram are effective with intention.
2
Identify the Shafi'i objection and its proof
Extract Imam al-Shafi'i's argument that marriage ownership is shared, so divorce should be attributable to either spouse.
The Shafi'i proof: milk al-nikah is shared; divorce removes a shared bond.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
Understand the Hanafi distinction: divorce (talaq) removes a restriction (qayd) specific to the wife, while ibana removes connection (wusla) and tahrim removes permissibility (hill), both of which are shared.
This is the core of the ikhtilaf: what exactly does divorce remove?
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
State the practical consequence: Hanafis say no divorce; Shafi'is say divorce if intended.
A mufti must know which ruling applies to the questioner's madhhab.
5
Note the authority of the Hanafi position
The Hanafi position is from zahir al-riwayah and all Hanafi imams agree.
This is the mufta bihi for Hanafis.

انا منک طالق میں نیت طلاق سے بھی طلاق واقع نہیں ہوتی
فصل ومن قال لا مرأته انا منك طالق فليس بشيء وان نوى طلاقا ولوقال انا منک بائن او علیک حرام ينوى الطلاق فهي طالق وقال الشافعي يقع الطلاق فى الوجه الأول ايضا اذانوى لان ملک النکاح مشترک بین الزوجين حتى ملكت المطالبة بالوطى کمایملک هو المطالبة بالتمكين وكذا الحل مشترك بينهما والطلاق وضع لازالتهما فيصح مضافا اليه كما يصح مضافا اليها كما في الابانة والتحريم ولنا ان الطلاق لازالة القيدوهو فيها دون الزوج الاترى انها هي الممنوعة عن التزوج بزوج أخر والخروج ولوكان لازالة الملك فهو عليها لانها مملوكة والزوج مالک ولهذا سميت منكوحة بخلاف الابانة لانها لازالة الوصلة وهى مشتركة وبخلاف التحريم لانه لازالة الحل وهو مشترک فصحت اضافتهما اليهما ولا تصح اضافة الطلاق الا اليها
ترجمہ (یہ) فصل ہے۔ کسی نے اپنی بیوی سے کہا میں تجھ سے طالق ہوں تو یہ کچھ نہیں ہے اگر چہ طلاق کی نیت کی ہو۔ اور اگر کہا میں تجھ سے بائن ہوں یا تجھ پر حرام ہوں طلاق کی نیت کرتا ہے تو یہ طلاق والی ہو گی۔ اور امام شافعی نے فرمایا کہ طلاق واقع ہوگی پہلی صورت میں بھی جبکہ نیت کی ہو۔ کیونکہ ملک مشترک ہے میاں بیوی کے درمیان حتی کہ وہ عورت وطی کے مطالبہ کی مالک ہے جیسا کہ شوہر قدرت علی الوطی پر مطالبہ کا مالک ہے۔ اور ایسے ہی حلت ان دونوں کے درمیان مشترک ہے۔ اور طلاق ان دونوں کو زائل کرنے کیلئے وضع کی گئی ہے۔ پس طلاق (شوہر) کی طرف منسوب ہو کر صحیح ہو گی ۔ جیسا کہ عورت کو زوج آخر کے ساتھ نکاح کرنے سے روکا جاتا ہے اور نکلنے سے۔ اور اگر طلاق ملک زائل کرنے کیلئے ہے تو ملک عورت پر ہے۔ کیونکہ عورت مملوکہ ہے اور شوہر مالک۔ اور اسی وجہ سے منکوحہ نام رکھا گیا۔ بخلاف اہانت کے۔ اسلئے کہ ابانت تعلق کو زائل کرنے کیلئے ہے اور تعلق مشترک ہے۔ اور بخلاف تحریم کے۔ کیونکہ تحریم حلت کو زائل کرنے کیلئے ہے۔ اور حلت مشترک ہے۔ لہذا ان دونوں کی نسبت زوجین کی طرف درست ہوگی ۔ اور طلاق کی نسبت صحیح نہیں ہے مگر عورت کی طرف۔ تشریح یہ فصل عورتوں کی جانب طلاق منسوب کرنے کے بیان میں ہے۔ اور چونکہ اضافت طلاق الی النساء مخالف ہے اضافتِ طلاق الی الرجال کے اس وجہ سے اس کو علیحدہ فصل میں بیان کیا ہے۔ صورت مسئلہ یہ ہے کہ ایک مرد نے اپنی بیوی سے کہا انا منگ طالق اور طلاق کی نیت بھی کی ہے تو طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی ۔ اور اگر انا منک بائن یا انا علیک حرام کہا اور طلاق کی نیت بھی ہے تو طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی۔ حضرت امام شافعی فرماتے ہیں کہ اگر نیت کی ہے تو انا منک طالق سے بھی طلاق واقع ہو جائے گی ۔
With 'Ana minki taliq' divorce does not occur even with intention.
Chapter: And whoever says to his wife, 'I am divorced from you,' then it is nothing, even if he intended divorce. And if he said, 'I am separated from you (bā'in)' or 'You are forbidden to me (harām),' intending divorce, then she is divorced. Al-Shafi'i said: Divorce occurs in the first case as well when he intends, because the ownership of marriage is shared between the spouses, so much so that she owns the right to demand intercourse just as he owns the right to demand submission, and similarly, permissibility is shared between them. And divorce is legislated to remove both, so it is valid when attributed to him just as it is valid when attributed to her, like in ibāna (separation) and taḥrīm (prohibition). Our evidence is that divorce is for removing the restriction, and that is in her, not the husband. Do you not see that she is the one prohibited from marrying another husband and from leaving? And if it is for removing ownership, then it is upon her because she is owned and the husband is the owner, and for this reason she is called 'manqūḥa' (married). Unlike ibāna, because it is for removing the connection, and it is shared. And unlike taḥrīm, because it is for removing permissibility, and it is shared. So attributing both to them is correct, but attributing divorce is only correct to her.
Translation: This is a chapter. Someone said to his wife, 'I am divorced from you,' then it is nothing, even if he intended divorce. And if he said, 'I am separated from you' or 'You are forbidden to me,' intending divorce, then she is divorced. Imam Shafi'i said: Divorce occurs in the first case as well when he intends, because ownership of marriage is shared between the spouses, to the extent that the woman owns the right to demand intercourse just as the husband owns the right to demand submission. And similarly, permissibility is shared between them. Divorce is legislated to remove both, so it is valid when attributed to him just as it is valid when attributed to her, as in ibāna and taḥrīm. Our evidence: Divorce is for removing the restriction, and that is in her, not the husband. Do you not see that she is the one prohibited from marrying another husband and from leaving? And if it is for removing ownership, then it is upon her because she is owned and the husband is the owner, and for this reason she is called 'manqūḥa'. Unlike ibāna, because it is for removing the connection, and it is shared. And unlike taḥrīm, because it is for removing permissibility, and it is shared. So attributing both to them is correct, but attributing divorce is only correct to her.
Explanation: This chapter is about attributing divorce to women. And since attributing divorce to women is different from attributing divorce to men, it has been mentioned in a separate chapter. The issue: A man said to his wife, 'I am divorced from you' and he also intended divorce, then divorce does not occur. And if he said, 'I am separated from you' or 'You are forbidden to me' and he intended divorce, then divorce occurs. Imam Shafi'i says that if he intended, then divorce occurs with 'I am divorced from you' as well.
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage is an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i. The ruling: If a husband says to his wife 'Ana minki taliq' (I am divorced from you), even with the intention of divorce, no divorce occurs according to the Hanafis. However, if he says 'Ana minki bā'in' (I am separated from you) or 'Alayki harām' (you are forbidden to me) intending divorce, then divorce occurs. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that divorce should occur in all cases because the marriage bond is shared—both spouses have rights and the divorce removes that shared bond. Therefore, attributing divorce to oneself should be valid. The Hanafi response is that divorce is specifically for removing a restriction (qayd) that applies only to the wife: she is prevented from marrying others and from leaving the marital home. The husband does not have such restrictions. Therefore, divorce cannot be attributed to him. In contrast, ibāna (separation) removes the connection (wusla) which is shared, and taḥrīm (prohibition) removes permissibility (hill) which is shared, so those can be attributed to either spouse. The Hanafi position is that the essence of divorce is to release the wife from the marriage bond, which is only she is bound. The commentary in Urdu reinforces this, explaining that this chapter deals with attributing divorce to women, which is different from attributing it to men. The practical result: the phrase 'I am divorced from you' does not effect divorce even with intent, whereas 'I am separated from you' or 'you are forbidden' do effect divorce if intended.

Key Terms
انامنک طالق (ana minki taliq): A phrase where the husband says 'I am divorced from you'; it does not effect divorce even with intention.
ابانت (ibāna): Separation or dissolution of marriage; it removes the connection (wusla) which is shared, so it can be attributed to either spouse.
تحریم (taḥrīm): Making something forbidden; here it refers to saying 'You are forbidden to me' which effects divorce with intention.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) She is divorced immediately
B) No divorce occurs
C) Divorce occurs only if the wife agrees
D) It is considered a metaphorical divorce

Key Takeaway
The phrase 'Ana minki taliq' does not effect divorce in Hanafi fiqh, even with intention, because divorce removes a restriction exclusive to the wife.

The Scope of 'Yawm' in Conditional Divorce
Ruling on the scope of 'yawm' in a conditional divorce.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rule for the word 'yawm' in conditional divorce and apply the exception when the husband intends only daytime.

Core Idea
In Hanafi law, 'yawm' means a full 24-hour period in conditional divorce, unless the husband proves he intended only the daylight.

This lesson examines the interpretation of the word 'yawm' (day) when used in a conditional divorce pronouncement. The Hanafi school follows the linguistic fact that 'yawm' includes both day and night, so the divorce takes effect even if marriage occurs at night. However, if the husband claims he intended only the daytime, his word is accepted because he is giving an interpretation of his own intention. Understanding this ruling helps clarify how linguistic usages affect the validity of conditional statements in family law.

Guided Path
1
Identify the conditional phrase
Look at the statement 'Yawma utazawwijuka fanti taliq'. The phrase uses 'yawm' as the condition for divorce.
2
Define 'yawm' linguistically
In Arabic, 'yawm' generally refers to a 24-hour period from sunrise to sunrise or from sunset to sunset, encompassing both day and night.
The Hanafi school adopts this broad definition for legal contexts unless context narrows it.
3
State the default ruling
Therefore, if the husband marries at any time within that 24-hour period, the divorce takes effect immediately.
This is the mufta bihi position.
4
Note the exception for intention
If the husband specifically intended only the daytime (biyad al-nahar), his word is accepted because he is asserting a literal interpretation of his own speech.
This exception relies on the principle that a person's intention can qualify the meaning of a general term.
5
Understand the usul foundation
The author notes that more detailed discussion is found in usul al-fiqh, where the rules for 'amm and khass are examined.
This case is a practical application of the maxim: al-umur bi-maqasidiha.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
کتاب الطلاق
اشرف البدایہ شرح ارد؛ بدائیہ جلد چہارم کے قبیلہ سے ہے۔ لہذا یوم اتز و جک فانت طالق میں لفظ یوم رات و دن کو شامل ہوگا۔ رات و دن میں جب بھی نکاح کرے گا طلاق ہو جائیگی ۔ البتہ اس کلام میں اگر مرد نے بالخصوص بیاض نہار کی نیت کی ہے۔ تو قصاً تصدیق کی جائے گی ۔ کیونکہ اس شخص نے حقیقت کلام کی ثیت کی ہے۔ زیادہ تفصیل اصول فقہ کی کتابوں میں ہے۔ اس کا مطالعہ کر لیا جائے۔ واللہ اعلم بالصواب
The Book of Divorce. This is from the commentary of Ashraf al-Bidayah, which is of the fourth volume of Bidayah. Therefore, in 'yawm utazawwijuka fanti taliq', the word 'yawm' includes night and day. Whenever he marries, during night or day, divorce will occur. However, if the man specifically intended the daytime (biyad al-nahar), then it is accepted according to his statement, because he has intended the literal meaning of the word. More detail is found in books of usul al-fiqh. Study that. And Allah knows best what is correct.
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage presents a ruling on the word 'yawm' (day) in a conditional divorce pronouncement. The literal meaning of 'yawm' in Arabic encompasses a full 24-hour period, including both night and day. Therefore, when a man says, 'On the day I marry you, you are divorced,' the divorce takes effect immediately upon marriage, whether it occurs during the day or at night. However, if the man claims that he intended only the daytime (biyad al-nahar, the period of daylight), his word is accepted, since he has intended the literal reality of the word. The author notes that a more detailed discussion of such linguistic matters is found in the books of Usul al-Fiqh. This is a straightforward ruling based on common usage.

Key Terms
یوم (yawm): A 24-hour period including both day and night.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Only if he specifically intended day.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi law, the word 'yawm' in a conditional divorce includes both day and night, and the husband's claim of intending only daytime is accepted.

Talaq — Divorce

The phrase 'Ana minki taliq' does not effect divorce even with intention
Inter-madhhab dispute on attributing divorce to oneself

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the phrase 'ana minki taliq' and explain why it differs from the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Divorce removes a restriction exclusive to the wife — the phrase 'I am divorced' cannot trigger talaq.

Is a husband's statement 'I am divorced from you' sufficient to end a marriage if he intends divorce? The Hanafi school says no, while Imam al-Shafi'i says yes. This dispute hinges on the very definition of talaq: does it remove a restriction unique to the wife, or a mutual right? This lesson unpacks the arguments and the practical difference in rulings.

Guided Path
1
Identify the disputed scenario
The case: a husband says to his wife 'ana minki taliq' (I am divorced from you) with the intention of divorce. According to the Hanafi matn, this 'is nothing' – no divorce occurs. Contrast this with the phrases 'ana minki bain' and 'anti alayya haram' where divorce does occur with intention.
The dispute is only about the first phrase.
2
Understand the Shafi'i argument
Imam al-Shafi'i argues that divorce removes both ownership (milk) and permissibility (hill), which are mutual between spouses. Therefore, divorce can be attributed to either spouse, just like ibanah (separation) and tahrim (prohibition), which are mutual.
The key concept: milk al-nikah is shared.
3
Analyze the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school responds that talaq specifically removes a restriction (qayd) that is exclusive to the wife: she cannot marry another or leave without permission. The husband has no such restriction. Even if talaq is about ownership, the husband alone owns the marriage bond. Hence, attributing divorce to the husband is invalid.
The distinction: qayd vs. waslah/hill.
4
Distinguish from ibanah and tahrim
Ibanah removes the mutual connection (ta'alluq), and tahrim removes the mutual permissibility (hill). Both are shared, so they can be attributed to either spouse. Talaq is unique in targeting a unilateral restriction.
The analogy with ibanah and tahrim fails because the attribute removed is not mutual.
5
Determine the practical consequence
In practice, if a husband says 'ana minki taliq' intending divorce, Hanafis rule no divorce, while Shafi'is rule a revocable divorce. The thamarah al-khilaf (practical difference) affects whether the couple remains married.
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is that no divorce occurs.

In the phrase 'I am divorced from you', divorce does not occur even if intention. Section: And whoever says to his wife 'I am divorced from you' then it is nothing even if he intends divorce. And if he says 'I am bain (irrevocably divorced) from you' or 'you are haram upon me' intending divorce, then she is divorced. And al-Shafi'i said: Divorce occurs in the first case as well when he intends, because ownership of marriage is common between the spouses, such that she has the right to demand intercourse just as he has the right to demand submission. And similarly, permissibility (hill) is shared between them. And divorce is legislated to remove both. So it is valid to attribute it to him just as it is valid to attribute it to her, as in the case of ibanah (separation) and tahrim (prohibition). And our evidence is that divorce is to remove the restriction (qayd), and that is on her, not on the husband. Do you not see that she is prevented from marrying another husband and from going out? And if it is for removing ownership, then it is upon her because she is owned and the husband is the owner. For this reason she is called mankuha (married). Unlike ibanah, because it is for removing the connection (waslah), which is shared. And unlike tahrim, because it is for removing permission (hill), which is shared. So it is valid to attribute both to either spouse, but attribution of divorce is not valid except to her. Translation: This is a section. Someone said to his wife 'I am divorced from you', then it is nothing even if he intended divorce. And if he said 'I am bain from you' or 'you are haram upon me' intending divorce, then it is divorce. And Imam Shafi'i said that divorce will occur in the first case as well when he intends. Because ownership is common between husband and wife, so much so that the woman owns the right to demand intercourse just as the husband owns the right to demand submission. And similarly, permissibility is shared between them. And divorce is legislated to remove both. So it is valid to attribute it to the husband just as it is valid to attribute it to the wife. As in ibanah and tahrim. And if divorce is for removing ownership, then ownership is upon the woman because she is owned and the husband is the owner. For this reason she is called mankuha. Unlike ibanah, because it is for removing connection, and connection is shared. And unlike tahrim, because it is for removing permissibility, and permissibility is shared. So attribution of both is valid to either spouse, but attribution of divorce is not valid except to the wife. Explanation: This section is about attributing divorce to women. And since attribution of divorce to women is contrary to attribution of divorce to men, it is mentioned in a separate section. The case is that a man said to his wife 'I am divorced from you' and intended divorce; divorce does not occur. And if he said 'I am bain from you' or 'you are haram upon me' and intended divorce, then divorce occurs. Imam Shafi'i says that if he intended, then from 'I am divorced from you' as well, divorce occurs. Imam Shafi'i's evidence is that ownership of marriage is common between the spouses. Thus the woman has the right to demand intercourse from her husband. And similarly, permissibility is shared between them. Thus each of them is a locus of enjoyment for the other. And the death of either ends the marriage. Both are owners? And divorce is legislated to remove both ownership of marriage and permissibility. Therefore, just as it is correct to attribute divorce to the wife, it is also correct to attribute it to the husband, just as ibanah and tahrim can be attributed to either. Our evidence is that divorce is for removing the restriction (qayd) of marriage, and the restriction is upon the woman for the man, not upon the man for the woman. So you see that the restriction is on the woman: she cannot marry another and cannot go out of the house. So since the restriction of marriage is only on the woman, therefore to remove it, divorce can only be attributed to the woman, not to the man. Hence, through 'I am divorced from you', attributing divorce to the man is not valid, even if intention is present. And if we also concede that divorce is for removing ownership, as Imam Shafi'i said, even then his view is not established. Because divorce is to remove ownership of marriage, and ownership is only on the woman, not on the man. Thus the woman is called the owned (mamluka) and the husband is the owner (malik). For this reason, the woman is called mankuha, not naih. So when ownership is on the woman, divorce will occur on the woman, not from the woman to the man. At most, from Imam Shafi'i it might be said: since ownership is only on the woman and not the man, why then does the woman have the right to demand intercourse? We will answer: the woman's right to demand only implies that the husband is indebted (madyun), but being indebted does not necessitate being owned. As for the analogy with ibanah, the response is: the essence of the response is that ibanah is valid to attribute to both spouses because it removes the connection (ta'alluq), which is shared. And similarly, tahrim is valid for both because it removes permissibility (hill), which is shared. As for divorce, it is for removing the restriction (qayd), and the restriction is only on the woman, not the man. Therefore, divorce can only be attributed to the woman, not the man.
Source pages p. 268

Commentary
This passage presents an inter-madhhab dispute between the Hanafi school and Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the effect of the phrase 'ana minki taliq' (I am divorced from you). The Hanafi position, stated in the matn, is that saying these words does not effect a divorce, even if the husband intends divorce. In contrast, saying 'ana minki bain' or 'anti alayya haram' with intention does effect divorce. Imam al-Shafi'i argues that 'ana minki taliq' should also effect divorce when intended, because marriage involves mutual ownership (milk) and permissibility (hill) shared between spouses. Since divorce is legislated to remove both, it can be attributed to either spouse, just like ibanah (separation) and tahrim (prohibition). The Hanafi response is that divorce specifically removes a restriction (qayd) that is placed on the wife, not the husband. The wife is prohibited from marrying others and from leaving the house, restrictions that do not apply to the husband. Even if we consider divorce as removing ownership (milk), the ownership is the husband's right over the wife, not the reverse; hence the wife is the owned (mamluka) and the husband is the owner (malik). Thus divorce naturally pertains to the wife. The analogy with ibanah and tahrim fails because ibanah removes the connection (which is mutual) and tahrim removes the permissibility (which is also mutual), while divorce uniquely removes a restriction exclusive to the wife. The passage also addresses a potential objection: if ownership is only on the wife, why does she have the right to demand intercourse? The answer is that this right indicates the husband's obligation (dayn), not that she owns him. This is a classic Hanafi position emphasizing the distinctive nature of talaq as a power vested exclusively in the husband.

Key Terms
طلاق (talaq): A legal term for dissolving marriage; it is the removal of the restriction (qayd) of marriage from the wife.
قید (qayd): The restriction imposed by marriage that prevents the wife from marrying another and from leaving the house without permission.
ملک النکاح (milk al-nikah): Ownership of the marriage bond; in the Hanafi view, it is a right of the husband over the wife.
ابانت (ibanah): Separation; removal of the connection (ta'alluq) between spouses, which is mutual.
تحریم (tahrim): Prohibition; removal of permissibility (hill) between spouses, which is mutual.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the reason that the phrase 'ana minki taliq' (I am divorced from you) does not effect divorce?
A) The husband did not say the magic words.
B) Talaq removes a restriction exclusive to the wife, so it cannot be attributed to the husband.
C) The wife must also agree to the divorce.
D) It is not a valid formula because it is not in Arabic.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school rules that a husband saying 'I am divorced from you' does not effect divorce, because talaq uniquely removes a restriction placed only on the wife.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
8 min
The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on 'Anti Taliq Wahidatan Aw La'
Intra-Hanafi ruling on doubt in divorce numbers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the phrase 'anti taliq wahidatan aw la' and explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement between Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Core Idea
Adding 'aw la' after specifying a number of divorces introduces uncertainty that nullifies the entire pronouncement.

The phrase 'anti taliq wahidatan aw la' (you are divorced one or not) raises a subtle legal question: does the doubt affect the number of divorces or the occurrence itself? In this passage from al-Hidayah, we find an intra-Hanafi dispute with two positions from Imam Muhammad and two from Abu Yusuf. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to parse conditional language in divorce pronouncements and appreciate the Hanafi emphasis on certainty in talaq.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core phrase and issue
Read the passage and locate the phrase 'anti taliq wahidatan aw la'. The issue is whether this utterance effects any divorce or is void due to the doubt created by 'aw la'.
The phrase directly attached 'aw la' to the number, not to the entire statement.
2
Map the positions of the three imams
Identify the views: Abu Hanifa and the later view of Abu Yusuf say no divorce. The earlier view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (in one narration) say one revocable divorce. Muhammad also has another narration where it is nothing.
Note the two narrations from Muhammad.
3
Analyze the reasoning for each position
For Abu Hanifa and later Abu Yusuf: the 'aw la' introduces doubt in the occurrence itself because the number is integral. For Muhammad (first narration): the doubt is only in the number, so the 'one' is dropped, leaving 'you are divorced' which implies one. For the second narration: it follows Abu Hanifa's reasoning.
The key distinction is whether doubt attacks the number or the occurrence.
4
Compare with the case 'anti taliq, aw la'
Note the difference: when 'aw la' is attached to the entire phrase, doubt is in the occurrence, so it's universally void. Here, it's attached to the number, causing the dispute.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
انت طالق واحدۃ اولا سے کچھ بھی واقع نہیں ہوگا
و لو قال انت طالق واحدۃ اولافليس بشيء قال رضى الله عنه هكذا ذكر فى الجامع الصغير من غير خلاف وهذا قول ابي حنيفة وابى يوسف اخراو على قول محمد وهو قول ابى يوسف اولا تطلق واحدة رجعية ذكر قول محمد في كتاب الطلاق فيما اذا قال لامرأته انت طالق واحدة اولاشيء ولا فرق بين المسألتين ولو كان المذكور ههنا قول الكل فعن محمد روايتان له انه ادخل الشك فى الواحدة لدخول كلمة اوبينها وبين النفى فيسقط اعتبار الواحدة ويبقى قوله انت طالق بخلاف قوله انت طالق اولالانه ادخل الشك في اصل الايقاع فلا يقع ولهما ان الوصف متى قرن بالعدد كان الوقوع بذكر العدد الاترى انه لو قال لغير المدخول بها
From 'you are divorced one or not' nothing occurs. And if he said 'you are divorced one or not' then it is nothing. Radi Allahu anhu said: This is how it is mentioned in al-Jami' al-Saghir without disagreement. And this is the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf later? And according to Muhammad's view, and it is the view of Abu Yusuf first? She divorces one revocable. Muhammad's view is mentioned in the book of divorce regarding when he said to his wife 'you are divorced one or not' nothing. And there is no difference between the two issues. And if it is mentioned here the view of all, then from Muhammad there are two narrations: He (Muhammad) says that he introduced doubt in the one (divorce) due to the entry of the word 'or' between it and negation, so the consideration of the one is dropped and his statement 'you are divorced' remains. Unlike his statement 'you are divorced or not' because he introduced doubt in the original occurrence, so it does not occur. And for them (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), whenever a description is joined with a number, the occurrence is by mentioning the number. Do you not see that if he said to a non-consummated wife ...
Source pages p. 269

Commentary
This passage discusses the effect of the phrase 'anti taliq wahidatan aw la' (you are divorced one or not). According to the Hanafi school, uttering this phrase does not result in any divorce. The text refers to a ruling recorded in al-Jami' al-Saghir without disagreement, indicating it is from Zahir al-Riwayah. The positions of the three leading Hanafi jurists are presented: Abu Hanifa and, in a later view, Abu Yusuf hold that no divorce occurs. The earlier view of Abu Yusuf, and the view of Muhammad al-Shaybani, is that one revocable divorce takes place. However, the text notes that Muhammad has two narrations: in one, the doubt affects the number, so the 'one' is dropped, leaving 'anti taliq' (you are divorced) without a number, which would effect a single divorce. But the preferred view (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa and the later view of Abu Yusuf: no divorce occurs. The reasoning is that the word 'aw la' (or not) introduces uncertainty into the actual occurrence of the divorce, not merely into the number. Therefore, the pronouncement is invalid. In contrast, if he says 'anti taliq, aw la' (you are divorced, or not), that does not effect divorce either because the doubt is on the occurrence itself. The passage also compares with a case involving a non-consummated wife, which cuts off.

Key Terms
اولا (aw la): The phrase 'or not' indicating doubt or alternative.
واحدۃ (wahidatan): One (divorce).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to Abu Hanifa, if a man says to his wife 'Anti taliq wahidatan aw la', what is the ruling?
A) One revocable divorce occurs.
B) One irrevocable divorce occurs.
C) No divorce occurs.
D) Three divorces occur.

Key Takeaway
When doubt enters the pronouncement of talaq, the entire act is invalid, and no divorce occurs.

Talaq — Divorce
intermediate
10 min
The Ruling on 'Anti Taliq Wahidatan Aw La': An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on ambiguous divorce expression

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on the expression 'anti taliq wahidatan aw la', explain the proof of each side, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Doubt on the number attached to divorce can nullify the entire divorce according to the two shaykhs.

This passage from Al-Hidayah addresses a deceptively simple phrase: 'you are divorced one or not'. The commentator reveals that the claim of unanimity in al-Jami' al-Saghir is inaccurate; there is a genuine intra-Hanafi disagreement on whether any divorce occurs. We will dissect the positions of the three leading Hanafi imams and understand how the precise location of doubt (shakk) determines the legal outcome.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three positions
List the rulings of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Imam Muhammad on 'anti taliq wahidatan aw la'. Note that each Imam may have multiple narrations.
Abu Hanifa: no divorce. Abu Yusuf: first view one revocable, second view no divorce. Imam Muhammad: two narrations (no divorce / one revocable).
2
Examine the proof of Imam Muhammad
Imam Muhammad argues that the doubt is only on the number 'wahidatan' because 'aw' intervenes. The number drops, leaving 'anti taliq', which alone imposes one revocable divorce. Contrast with 'anti taliq aw la' where doubt is on the divorce itself.
His proof uses the principle: shakk in the attribute nullifies the attribute, but the original remains.
3
Examine the proof of the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf's second view)
They argue that when the attribute (taliq) is mentioned with a number, the divorce is attributed to the number. The number is an attribute of the omitted 'tatliqah'. Hence doubt on the number becomes doubt in the original iqa', preventing divorce.
Analogy: 'anti taliq thalatha' results in three divorces, proving the number governs occurrence.
4
Determine the mufta bihi and its authority
Al-Hidayah and the commentator rely on the two shaykhs' view (no divorce) as the operative position. This aligns with the zahir al-riwayah from al-Jami' al-Saghir.
Tarjih authority: Al-Marghinani in Al-Hidayah.

ثلاث کا ذکر لغو ہوتا۔ اور یہ اسلئے کہ واقع در حقیقت وہ موصوف محذوف ہے۔ اس کے معنی ہیں انت طالق تطليقة واحدة۔ چنانچہ بتحقیق گذر چکا۔ اور جب واقع وہ ہے جس کی عدد نعت ہے تو شک اصل ایقاع میں داخل ہوا۔ پس دو روایتیں ہیں۔ ایک یہ کہ مذکورہ مسئلہ انت طالق واحدة اولا میں کوئی طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی۔ دوسری روایت یہ کہ ایک رجعی واقع ہو جائے گی۔ پہلی روایت جامع صغیر میں ہے اور دوسری روایت مبسوط کی کتاب الطلاق میں مذکور ہے۔

امام محمد کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ انت طالق واحدة اولاً میں واحدة اور نفی کے درمیان شک ہو گیا۔ پس شک کی وجہ سے واحدة کا اعتبار تو ساقط ہو گیا ہے اور انت طالق بسلامت باقی رہا۔ اور چونکہ انت طالق سے ایک طلاق رجعی واقع ہو جاتی ہے اس وجہ سے ایک طلاق رجعی واقع ہو جائے گی۔ برخلاف انت طالق اولا کے۔ کیونکہ یہاں اصل طلاق ہی میں شک ہے۔ اور ایقاع طلاق میں اگر شک ہو جائے تو طلاق واقع نہیں ہوتی۔ لہذا اس صورت میں طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی۔

اشرف البدایہ شرح اردو بدایہ جلد چہارم

شیخین کی دلیل یہ ہے کہ وصف یعنی طالق کو جب عدد کے ساتھ مل کر ذکر کیا جائے (مثلاً کہا جائے انت طالق واحد یا اثنتین یا ثلاثا) تو وقوع طلاق عدد کے ساتھ ہوگا نہ کہ صیغہ صفت کے ساتھ۔ چنانچہ اگر کسی نے اپنی غیر مدخول بہا بیوی سے انت طالق ثلاثا کہا تو اس پر تین طلاقیں واقع ہو جائیں گی۔ اگر طلاق کا وقوع صیغہ صفت کے ساتھ ہوتا تو ثلاثا کا ذکر لغو ہوتا۔ اور وقوع طلاق عدد کے ساتھ اس وجہ سے ہے کہ واقع ہونے والا در حقیقت وہ موصوف ہے جو محذوف ہے۔ پس انت طالق واحدة کے معنی ہیں انت طالق تطليقة واحدة۔ اور جب واقع ہونے والا وہ موصوف ہے جس کے لیے عدد صفت ہے تو اس صورت میں اصل ایقاع طلاق میں شک پیدا ہو گیا۔ اور اصل ایقاع میں شک پیدا ہونے سے طلاق واقع نہیں ہوتی۔ اس وجہ سے یہاں طلاق واقع نہیں ہوگی۔
If one says 'You are divorced thrice,' she is divorced thrice. If occurrence was by the attribute, mentioning the number would be pointless. This is because what actually occurs is the described (al-man'ut) which is omitted, meaning 'you are divorced once' as previously mentioned. When what occurs is that to which the number is an attribute, doubt enters the original act (asl al-iqa'), so nothing occurs. Translation: And if he says 'you are divorced one or not,' nothing occurs. The author of Hidayah said: It is mentioned in al-Jami' al-Saghir without disagreement. However, this is the view of Abu Hanifa; the second view of Abu Yusuf and the view of Imam Muhammad and the first view of Abu Yusuf is that one revocable divorce occurs. Imam Muhammad's view is mentioned in al-Mabsut's book of talaq in the case when someone says to his wife 'anti taliq wahidatan aw la shay'' and there is no difference between the two cases. Here it is mentioned that it is the view of the whole (kull). So Imam Muhammad has two narrations. Imam Muhammad's proof: Doubt is introduced into 'wahidatan' because the word 'aw' enters between 'wahidatan' and negation, so the effect of 'wahidatan' falls away, leaving 'anti taliq'. Unlike 'anti taliq aw la' because doubt enters the original iqa', so no divorce occurs. The proof of the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf in second view): When the attribute (taliq) is mentioned together with the number, occurrence of divorce is with the number. Do you not see that if one says to a non-consummated wife 'anti taliq thalatha', three divorces occur. If occurrence were with the attribute, mentioning 'thalatha' would be futile. This is because what occurs is the described (mawsuf) which is omitted; its meaning is 'anti taliq tatliqatan wahidatan'. When what occurs is that to which the number is an attribute, doubt enters the original iqa', so nothing occurs. Explanation: If someone says to his married wife 'anti taliq wahidatan aw la', no divorce occurs with this speech. The author of Hidayah says that this ruling is in al-Jami' al-Saghir without disagreement, but it is not so; there is disagreement: this is the view of Abu Hanifa, while the second view of Abu Yusuf [is that nothing occurs? Actually from context: first view of Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad say one revocable divorce]. The proof that according to Imam Muhammad one revocable divorce occurs is that in al-Mabsut's book of talaq, Imam Muhammad's view is mentioned in the case when someone says to his married wife 'anti taliq wahidatan aw la shay''; in that case, he says one revocable divorce occurs. So in this case also one revocable divorce occurs. If it is accepted that what is mentioned in al-Jami' al-Saghir is the view of the whole (i.e., no divorce), then Imam Muhammad has two narrations: one that no divorce occurs, another that one revocable occurs. The first is in al-Jami' al-Saghir, the second in al-Mabsut. Imam Muhammad's proof: In 'anti taliq wahidatan aw la', doubt occurs between 'wahidatan' and negation; due to doubt, the consideration of 'wahidatan' drops, and 'anti taliq' remains sound. Since 'anti taliq' yields one revocable divorce, one revocable divorce occurs. Unlike 'anti taliq aw la' because here doubt is in the original divorce, and if doubt occurs in the iqa' of divorce, divorce does not occur. Therefore in that case no divorce occurs. The proof of the two shaykhs: When the attribute (taliq) is mentioned together with the number (e.g., one says 'anti taliq wahid' or 'ithnatayn' or 'thalatha'), occurrence of divorce is with the number, not with the verbal form of the attribute. Thus if one says to his non-consummated wife 'anti taliq thalatha', three divorces occur. If occurrence were with the verbal form of the attribute, mentioning 'thalatha' would be futile. Occurrence of divorce with the number is because what occurs in reality is the described (mawsuf) that is omitted. So 'anti taliq wahidatan' means 'anti taliq tatliqatan wahidatan'. When what occurs is the described for which the number is an attribute, then doubt arises in the original iqa' of divorce, and doubt in the original iqa' prevents divorce from occurring. Hence here no divorce occurs.
Source pages p. 270

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the expression 'anti taliq wahidatan aw la' (you are divorced one or not) and similar expressions. The base matn from al-Hidayah states that no divorce occurs, claiming this is agreed upon in al-Jami' al-Saghir. The commentator points out that there is disagreement. The positions are: (1) Abu Hanifa: no divorce occurs. (2) Abu Yusuf has two views: first view one revocable divorce, second view no divorce. (3) Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani has two narrations: one from al-Jami' al-Saghir that no divorce occurs, another from al-Mabsut that one revocable divorce occurs. The reasoning revolves around the role of doubt. Imam Muhammad argues that in 'anti taliq wahidatan aw la', the doubt is between the number 'wahidatan' and the negation 'la', so the number is dropped but the divorce phrase remains, giving one revocable divorce. In contrast, 'anti taliq aw la' introduces doubt into the very act of divorcing, so nothing occurs. The two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf's second view) argue that when the attribute (taliq) is combined with a number, the divorce is attributed to the number, not the attribute. They use the example of 'anti taliq thalatha' where three divorces occur. If the divorce were attributed to the attribute, mentioning the number would be pointless. Therefore in 'anti taliq wahidatan aw la', the doubt enters the original iqa' because the number is an attribute of the omitted described (tatliqah wahidah), and doubt in the original prevents divorce. The passage concludes that the relied-upon position is that no divorce occurs, as per the base matn and the two shaykhs' view.

Key Terms
وصف (wasf): The attribute or description, here referring to the word 'taliq' itself as a description of the woman.
عدد (adad): The number mentioned alongside the divorce, such as one, two, or three.
موصوف (mawsoof): The described entity; here the omitted 'tatliqah' (divorce act) that is being described by the number.
نعت (na't): Adjective or attribute; the number functions as a na't for the omitted 'tatliqah'.
ایقاع (iqa'): The act of effecting or causing something; here the act of issuing divorce.
شک (shakk): Doubt or uncertainty between two possibilities; a key concept in this ruling.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon position in the Hanafi school (mufta bihi), what is the ruling when a husband says 'anti taliq wahidatan aw la'?
A) One revocable divorce occurs.
B) No divorce occurs.
C) Three divorces occur.
D) One irrevocable divorce occurs.

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, when a divorce expression includes a number followed by 'aw la', the doubt falls on the number, but because the number is an attribute of the omitted divorce act, the doubt becomes doubt in the original iqa', preventing divorce entirely.
